Salah — Prayer
advanced
10 min
Ruling When One Remembers a Missed Prayer While Praying a Current Prayer
Rulings on the invalidity of a current prayer when remembering a missed one

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of fasad mawquf (suspended invalidity) and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and al-Shafi'i on this issue.

Core Idea
Praying a current prayer while remembering a missed one renders it invalid: fasad mawquf (Abu Hanifa) or fasad ba't (Sahibayn).

One of the most detailed sub-rulings in the chapter on qada' is the case where a person begins a current prayer while remembering that he owes a missed prayer. The Hanafi school holds that this invalidates the current prayer, but there is a significant internal disagreement on the nature of that invalidity. This lesson unpacks the concepts of suspended invalidity (fasad mawquf) and absolute invalidity (fasad ba't), along with the conditions that can salvage the prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
If one prays a current fard prayer while remembering a missed prayer (even if the missed is Witr), the current prayer becomes invalid.
This is agreed upon by Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, but they differ on the type of invalidity.
2
Identify the two types of invalidity
Abu Hanifa says it becomes fasad mawquf (suspended invalidity) – the prayer is invalid but can become valid if the missed prayer is made up later before six more prayers pass. The Sahibayn say it becomes fasad ba't (absolute invalidity) – completely void with no chance of becoming valid.
Muhammad also adds a condition about the recommended time.
3
Consider the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the current prayer does not become invalid at all, based on the principle that one should not nullify a valid act of worship.
The Hanafi response is that the prayer was performed while being aware of an obligation that should precede it.
4
Understand the condition for suspended invalidity
According to Abu Hanifa, if the person prays six or more prayers after the invalid one without making up the missed prayer, then the invalid prayer can be considered valid (i.e., it becomes valid retrospectively).
This is linked to the concept of numerousness dropping order.
5
Apply to the case of old and new missed prayers
The passage discusses whether a new missed prayer (recent) or an old one (from long ago) triggers the invalidity. The fatwa is that the new one does, but there is disagreement on old ones.
If one has many old missed prayers, the ruling may differ to avoid hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب قضاء الفوائت بضيق الوقت، والنسيان وصيرُورتها ستَّا، ولم يعد بعودها إلى القلة، فلو صلى فرضاً ذاكراً فائتة ولو وتراً فشد فرضه موقوفا. كانت أي الترتيب أي الفوائت كفجر مثلاً وقت تذكره وقتاً للفائتة، ولا تذكرها هنا، فوجب العمل بالدليل المقطوع به، وروي أنه عليه صلى المغرب يوماً، فقال هل رآني أحد منكم صليت العصر، فقالوا: لا، فصلى العصر ولم يعد المغرب، ولو وجب الترتيب مع النسيان لأعاد المغرب، والثالث كثرة الفوائت ثم اختلفوا في أدنى حد الكثرة، ففي ظاهر الرواية أن يصير الفوائت ستا، فإذا خرج وقت السادسة سقط الترتيب، وعند زفر أن يزيد على شهر كالجنون إذا استغرق الشهر، وروي عن محمد أن السقوط بصيرورتها خمسا والصحيح جواب ظاهر الرواية؛ لأن الفائتة لا تدخل في حد التكرار بدخول وقت السادسة وإنما تدخل بخروج وقت السادس (مستخلص) وقال ملا مسكين: سواء كانت الفائتة قديمة أو حديثة، فالحديثة تسقط الترتيب اتفاقا، وفي القديمة اختلاف المشايخ، وذلك كمن ترك صلاة شهر، ثم صلّى مدة ولم يقض تلك الصلوات حتى ترك صلاة، ثم صلى أخرى ذاكراً للفائتة الحديثة لم تجز عند البعض، ويجعل الماضي كأن لم يكن زجراً له، وقيل تجوز، وعليه الفتوى؛ لأن الاشتغال بهذه الفائتة ليس بأولى من الاشتغال بالفوائت القديمة، وفي الاشتغال بالكل تفويت الفريضة عن وقتها. (انتهى مع زيادة من الفتح) بضيق الوقت لأنه ليس من الحكمة تفويت الوقتية، والمراد من الوقت المستحب في الأصح. (ط،ع) والنسيان للفائتة؛ لأن الناسي عاجز حتى لو نسي الفائتة وصلى الوقتية ثم تذكرها، يقضي الفائتة ولم يعد الوقتية، وقال مالك: لا يسقط بهما. (مسكين) وصيرورتها: أي يسقط أيضاً مع صيرورة الفائتة ست صلوات بخروج وقت السادسة. (مسكين) إلى القلة بأن كانت عليه صلوات فائتة، فقضى بعضها حتى قل ما بقي لا يعود الترتيب فيما بقي؛ لأن الساقط لا يحتمل العود، وقال أبو حفص الكبير وعليه الفتوى، وهو اختيار شمس الأئمة وفخر الإسلام، وقيل: يعود الترتيب. (ع) موقوفاً [ أي فساداً موقوفاً عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما تفسد فساداً باتاً] أي لو صلى العصر مثلاً ذاكراً أنه لم يصل الظهر فسد عصره إن لم يكن في آخر الوقت والعبرة لأصل الوقت عندهما، وعند محمد للوقت المستحب حتى لو شرع في العصر وهو ناس للظهر ، ثم تذكر الظهر في وقت لو اشتغل به يقع العصر في الوقت المكروه، يقطع العصر عندهما ويصلي الظهر ثم يصلي العصر، وعنده يمضي في العصر ثم يصلي الظهر بعد غروب الشمس، فإذا فسدت الفريضة لا يبطل أصل الصلاة عندهما، وعند محمد يبطل، كذا ذكر عامة مشايخنا هذا الاختلاف، وقيل: لا خلاف بينهم بأنه لا يبطل أصل الصلاة، ثم العصر يفسد فسادا موقوفاً حتى لو صلى بعده ست صلوات أو أكثر و لم يعد الظهر أعاد الكل جائزاً، وعندهما يفسد فسادا باتاً لا جواز له بحال، وقال الشافعي: لا يفسد أصلاً، وقوله: "ولو وتراً" أي ولو كان المتروك وتراً فكذلك عنده خلافاً لهما. (مسكين)
Chapter on Making Up Missed Prayers: [The obligation of order] drops due to narrowness of time, forgetfulness, and their becoming six, and it does not return when they become few. So if one prays a current obligation while remembering a missed prayer, even if it is Witr, then his current prayer becomes suspended invalid [according to Abu Hanifa]. [Commentary] meaning the order of the missed prayers. For example, if one remembers a missed Fajr during the time of [another] prayer, that time becomes a time for the missed prayer, and he does not perform it here? So it is obligatory to act on the definitive proof. It is narrated that he (peace be upon him) prayed Maghrib one day and said, 'Did any of you see me pray Asr?' They said, 'No.' So he prayed Asr and did not repeat Maghrib. If order were obligatory despite forgetfulness, he would have repeated Maghrib. The third [condition] is numerousness of missed prayers. Then they differed on the minimum of numerousness: in the apparent narration, it is that the missed prayers become six; when the time of the sixth exits, order drops. According to Zufar, it exceeds a month, like insanity if it covers a month. It is narrated from Muhammad that the dropping occurs when they become five, and the correct is the answer of the apparent narration because a missed prayer does not enter into the limit of repetition with the entering of the time of the sixth but enters with the exiting of the time of the sixth. (Mustakhlas) Mulla Miskin said: Whether the missed prayer is old or new, the new one drops the order by agreement. Regarding the old one, there is disagreement among the mashayikh. For example, if one leaves a month of prayers, then prays for a while without making up those prayers until he leaves a prayer, then prays another remembering the new missed prayer, it is not valid according to some, and they make the past as if it never happened as a deterrent. It is said it is valid, and that is the fatwa because occupying oneself with this missed prayer is not more deserving than occupying oneself with old missed prayers, and occupying oneself with all would cause the loss of the obligatory prayer in its time. (End with addition from al-Fath) [The dropping] is due to narrowness of time because it is not from wisdom to lose the timely prayer, and what is meant is the recommended time according to the most correct. (T, A) And forgetfulness of the missed prayer because the forgetful person is incapacitated. So if one forgets the missed prayer and prays the timely prayer, then remembers it, he makes up the missed prayer and does not repeat the timely prayer. Malik said: It does not drop by these two. (Miskin) And their becoming six: i.e., it drops also with the missed prayers becoming six prayers by the exit of the time of the sixth. (Miskin) To fewness: if one has missed prayers, so he makes up some until what remains is few, the order does not return regarding what remains because that which has dropped does not bear returning. Abu Hafs al-Kabir said, and the fatwa is upon it, and it is the choice of Shams al-A'imma and Fakhr al-Islam. It is said the order returns. (A) Suspended: i.e., suspended invalidity according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two, it becomes absolutely invalid. i.e., if one prays Asr for example while remembering that he did not pray Zuhr, then his Asr becomes invalid if it is not at the end of the time, and the consideration is for the beginning of time according to the two, and according to Muhammad it is for the recommended time. So if one begins Asr while forgetful of Zuhr, then remembers Zuhr at a time that if he occupied himself with it, Asr would fall in the disliked time, then he cuts off Asr according to the two and prays Zuhr then Asr. According to him, he continues in Asr then prays Zuhr after sunset. So when the obligatory prayer becomes invalid, the origin of the prayer is not nullified according to the two, but according to Muhammad it is nullified. Thus most of our mashayikh mentioned this disagreement. It is said there is no disagreement among them that the origin of the prayer is not nullified. Then Asr becomes invalid with suspended invalidity so that if he prays after it six prayers or more and does not repeat Zuhr, he repeats all validly. According to the two, it becomes absolutely invalid with no validity at all. Al-Shafi'i said: It does not become invalid at all. And his saying: 'even if it is Witr' means even if the missed is Witr, likewise according to him, contrary to the two. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on making up missed prayers (Qada' al-Fawa'it) presents the rulings on when the obligation to perform missed prayers in order (tartib) drops. The author begins by stating three conditions that lift the requirement of tartib: (1) narrowness of time for the current prayer, meaning if one fears losing the current prayer's recommended time, he may pray it before making up the missed one; (2) forgetfulness of the missed prayer—the forgetful person is excused and does not need to repeat the current prayer upon remembering; and (3) the missed prayers becoming numerous, defined in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya) as six missed prayers. Once the time of the sixth missed prayer exits, tartib drops. The text then discusses disagreements: Zufar defines numerousness as exceeding a month, while a narration from Muhammad suggests five. The correct position is the apparent narration because a missed prayer does not enter the count of repetition until its time exits. The passage then addresses a scenario where a person remembers a missed prayer while performing a current prayer. According to Abu Hanifa, the current prayer becomes 'suspended invalid' (fasad mawquf)—it is invalid but can be rendered valid if the missed prayer is later made up before six more prayers pass. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), it becomes absolutely invalid (fasad ba't) and cannot be redeemed. The text also notes that al-Shafi'i holds it does not become invalid at all. The relied-upon fatwa is on the view of Abu Hafs al-Kabir that once tartib drops due to numerousness, it does not return even if the missed prayers become few. This chapter is a key source for understanding Hanafi rulings on making up missed prayers and the intricacies of order.

Key Terms
فَسَاد مَوْقُوف (fasad mawquf): Suspended invalidity: the prayer is invalid but may become valid if conditions are later fulfilled (e.g., missed prayer made up before six more prayers pass).
فَسَاد بَاتّ (fasad ba't): Absolute invalidity: the prayer is void and cannot become valid under any circumstance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on a current prayer if one remembers a missed prayer while performing it?
A) It is absolutely invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is suspended invalid; it can become valid if the missed prayer is made up before six prayers pass.
C) It is valid as long as the missed prayer is made up later.
D) It is invalid only if the missed prayer is from the same day.

Key Takeaway
When remembering a missed prayer during a current prayer, the current prayer becomes invalid; Abu Hanifa holds fasad mawquf while the Sahibayn hold fasad ba't.

The Ruling and Timing of Sujud al-Sahw
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Sujud al-Sahw, identify its evidence, and explain why the Hanafi school holds it after the salam despite opposing views.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Sahw is wajib after the salam to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.

This passage from the Chapter on Sujud al-Sahw establishes the core ruling: two prostrations are obligatory after the salam, with tashahhud and salam, to repair any deficiency caused by forgetfulness. It also addresses why the Hanafi school places this prostration after the salam, contrasting with the views of Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i, and clarifies the manner of performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Ruling
Identify the exact ruling: Sujud al-Sahw is wajib, performed after the salam, consisting of two prostrations, tashahhud, and salam. Note the level of obligation (wajib) and its basis.
The text states 'يجب بعد السلام سجدتان' — obligatory after salam.
2
Locate the Primary Evidence
Find the dalil: the hadith of Thawban where the Prophet ﷺ commands 'Whoever forgets in prayer, let him prostrate two prostrations.' Also the explicit saying 'For every forgetfulness, two prostrations after the salam.'
The command (amr) indicates wujub in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the Justification
The text compares sujud al-sahw to blood offerings (dimā') in Hajj as obligatory compensations, but notes that prayer compensation is from the same category (jins) as the act itself.
Jabr (compensation) is like qada', hence placed after prayer section.
4
Analyze the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Malik: if deficiency, before salam; if increase, after. Shafi'i: always before salam. The Hanafi response: the two narrations of actions conflict, so we adhere to the explicit command (qawl), which is unambiguous.
The disagreement is in preference (al-ūlā), not permissibility (al-jawāz).
5
Determine the Manner of Performance
Perform two prostrations, then sit for tashahhud and send blessings, then give one salam to the right (the sound view). This avoids confusion for followers.
The text prefers one salam to the right to avoid disrupting the congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو في بيان أحكام يجب بعد السلام سجدتان بتشهد وتسليم في الصحيح الفائت، جبر باب سجود السهو: هذا من قبيل إضافة السبب إلى المسبب، والأصل أن يكون المضاف إليه سببا للمضاف كما في خيار الشرط وخيار العيب وسجدة التلاوة، وهذا لأن الإضافة للاختصاص أي اختصاص المضاف بالمضاف إليه، وأقوى الاختصاص اختصاص الأثر بالمؤثر، ولما كان سجود السهو لإصلاح ما فات أشبه قضاء ولهذا أخر هذا الباب عنها. (مسكين) يجب إلخ : أي للأمر به؛ لرواية ثوبان عن النبي علي: "من" سها في الصلاة فليسجد سجدتين"؛ ولأنه شرع لجبر النقصان، وهو واجب كالدماء في الحج غير أنه لما كان للمال مدخل فيه كان بالدماء، بخلاف الصلاة؛ لأن شأن الجبر أن يكون من جنس الكسر ، وقوله : بعد السلام، وهو عندنا، وقال مالك: إن كان السهو بالنقصان سجد قبل السلام؛ لأنه النقصان، وإن كان عن زيادة يسجد بعد السلام؛ لأنه ترغيم الشيطان، وحكي أن أبا يوسف كان مع هارون الرشيد، فجاء مالك فقال له أبو يوسف ما قولك في هذه المسألة؟ فأجاب بمذهبه، فقال له أبو يوسف: ما قولك لو وقع السهو في الزيادة والنقصان جميعاً فسكت مالك متحيراً وقال: على هذا أدركنا مشايخنا، فقال أبو يوسف: الشيخ تارة يخطئ وتارة يصيب، فظن أن أبا يوسف قال له: الشيخ تارة يخطي وتارة يصيب، وقال الشافعي يسجد قبل السلام؛ لما روي أن النبي عليها سجد للسهو قبل السلام، ولنا قوله علي: "لكل سهو سجدتان بعد السلام، وروي أنه عليه يسجد سجدتين للسهو بعد السلام، فتعارضت روايتان بفعله، وبقي التمسك بقوله علي سالماً، ولأن سجود السهو مما لا يتكرر، فيؤخر عن السلام حتى لو سها عن السلام يجبر به، وهذا الخلاف في الأولوية دون الجواز، وقال بعضهم: سجود السهو سنة. (مستخلص، مسكين) بتشهد: متعلق بـ "يجب" وبصلاة النبي عليه و بدعاء في الصحيح. (ط) وتسليم: [فيه إيماء إلى أن سجدة السهو يرفع التشهد دون القعدة بخلاف الصلبية حيث ترفعهما، وكذا التلاوية على المختار (ط)] أي تسليم آخر بعد التشهد الثاني، فالحاصل أن في سجود السهو ثلاثة اختلافات: الأول في صفته وهو واجب في الصحيح، والثاني في محله وهو بعد السلام عندنا والثالث في كيفيته، وهي أن سجدتين ثم يتشهد ثم يسلم ثم اختلف في السلام الأول: فقيل : يسلم تسليمتين، وهو الصحيح، وقيل: تسليمة وجهه، ولا ينحرف عن القبلة، وقيل: تسليم واحد عن يمينه ويأتي بالصلاة على النبي في قعدة السهو، هو الصحيح؛ لأن في صورة التسليمتين يظن المقتدون فراغ الإمام عن الصلاة، فينصرفون ويقوم المسبوق لأداء ما بقي عليه صلاته، فيختل أمر الجماعة. (عيني وغيره) واحدة تلقاء يسجد والدعاء
Chapter on the Prostration of Forgetfulness: In explaining the rulings: Two prostrations are obligatory after the salam, with tashahhud and salam in the correct [view], compensating for what is missed. Chapter on Sujud al-Sahw: This is of the type of attributing the cause to the effect, and the principle is that the annexed-to is the cause for the annexed, as in option of condition, option of defect, and prostration of recitation. This is because the annexation is for specification, i.e., specification of the annexed to the annexed-to, and the strongest specification is the specification of the effect to the cause. Since sujud al-sahw is to repair what is missed, it resembles making up (qada'), and therefore this chapter is placed after [prayer]. (Miskin) 'It is obligatory' etc.: i.e., due to the command for it; from the narration of Thawban from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever forgets in prayer, let him prostrate two prostrations.' And because it is legislated to compensate for deficiency, and it is obligatory like the blood [offerings] in Hajj, except that since wealth has an entry in it, it is with blood [offerings], contrary to prayer because the nature of compensation is that it be of the same kind as the defect. And his saying: 'after the salam' is our [position]. Malik said: If the forgetfulness is from deficiency, he prostrates before the salam because of the deficiency; if from increase, he prostrates after the salam to anger Satan. It is narrated that Abu Yusuf was with Harun al-Rashid, and Malik came. Abu Yusuf asked him: 'What is your opinion on this issue?' He answered according to his madhhab. Abu Yusuf said: 'What is your opinion if forgetfulness occurs in both increase and deficiency?' Malik fell silent, perplexed, and said: 'We found our mashayikh upon this.' Abu Yusuf said: 'The shaykh errs sometimes and is correct sometimes.' So he thought Abu Yusuf said to him: 'The shaykh errs sometimes and is correct sometimes.' Al-Shafi'i said he prostrates before the salam because it is narrated that the Prophet (saw) prostrated for forgetfulness before the salam. We have his saying: 'For every forgetfulness, two prostrations after the salam,' and it is narrated that he (saw) would prostrate two prostrations for forgetfulness after the salam. So two narrations of his action are contradictory, and adherence to his saying remains sound, and because sujud al-sahw is not repeated, so it is delayed after the salam so that if one forgets the salam itself, it is compensated. This disagreement is in preference, not permissibility. Some said sujud al-sahw is sunnah. (Mustakhlas, Miskin) 'With tashahhud': attached to 'it is obligatory', and with sending blessings on the Prophet and supplication in the sound [view]. (T) 'And salam': [There is an indication that sujud al-sahw necessitates the tashahhud without the sitting, unlike the obligatory prayer where it necessitates both, and likewise the prostration of recitation according to the selected view (T)] i.e., another salam after the second tashahhud. So the result is that in sujud al-sahw there are three differences: the first is its description, that it is wajib according to the sound [view]; the second is its place, that it is after the salam according to us; the third is its modality, that it is two prostrations, then tashahhud, then salam. Then they differed regarding the first salam: it is said he gives one salam to his face and does not turn from the qibla; it is said one salam to his right and performs salawat on the Prophet in the sitting of forgetfulness. That [latter] is sound because in the form of two salams, the followers think the imam has finished the prayer, so they leave and the latecomer stands to complete his prayer, disrupting the congregation. (Ayni and others) One facing [the qibla] he prostrates and supplication.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on the prostration of forgetfulness (Sujud al-Sahw). The author begins by stating the ruling: two prostrations are obligatory after the salam, along with tashahhud and salam, to compensate for what is missed in prayer. The commentary explains that this chapter is placed after the discussion of prayers because Sujud al-Sahw resembles making up (qada'), as it repairs deficiencies. The proof is from the hadith of Thawban: 'Whoever forgets in prayer, let him prostrate two prostrations.' It is wajib (obligatory) like the blood offerings in Hajj, but here it is from the same category (prayer) to compensate for what is lacking. The text then contrasts with other schools: Malik distinguishes between deficiency (prostrate before salam) and increase (after salam), and when Abu Yusuf asked about both occurring together, Malik was unable to answer. Al-Shafi'i holds that it is before salam. The Hanafi position relies on the explicit command of the Prophet: 'For every forgetfulness, two prostrations after the salam.' The disagreement is in preference, not permissibility—meaning it is permissible to do it before salam but preferable after. The manner of the prostration includes two prostrations, then tashahhud, then salam. There is a dispute about the first salam: some say one salam while facing the qibla, some say two salams, and the sound view is one salam to the right with salawat in the sitting, to avoid disrupting the congregation. The passage also notes that some scholars consider it sunnah, but the correct view is that it is wajib.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer, obligatory after the salam.
جبر (jabr): Compensation for deficiency; sujud al-sahw is a form of jabr for forgetfulness in prayer.
السهو (al-sahw): Forgetfulness during prayer that necessitates sujud al-sahw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Causes of Sujud al-Sahw and Rulings on Returning for Qa'dah
Ruling on causes of sujud al-sahw and return for sittings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the causes of sujud al-sahw and apply the ruling for returning to the first sitting based on physical proximity.

Core Idea
Leaving any wajib in prayer requires sujud al-sahw; returning to correct a missed wajib depends on how close you are to the next position.

Sujud al-sahw is a vital mechanism to rectify forgetfulness in prayer without invalidating it. This lesson unpacks the causes that trigger sujud al-sahw, especially the principle of 'leaving a wajib', and clarifies when one must return to a forgotten sitting and when to simply compensate with prostrations at the end.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause of sujud al-sahw
The primary cause is leaving a wajib (obligatory but not fard) act, whether by omission, delay, alteration, addition, or repetition. Examples include forgetting the first sitting, delaying Fatiha, or reciting aloud when silent.
The cause can be any wajib; only two prostrations are needed even if multiple errors occur.
2
Classify the type of forgetfulness: first sitting vs. last sitting
For the first sitting (qa'dah ula), the ruling depends on how close the person is to the sitting position when he remembers. For the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah), the ruling depends on whether he has prostrated for the next rak'ah.
The first sitting is wajib in 3- or 4-rak'ah prayers; the last sitting is wajib and must be performed before salam.
3
Determine if return is required based on physical proximity
If the person is closer to sitting (e.g., buttocks raised, knees still on ground), he must return and sit, then continue without sujud al-sahw for that return. If he is closer to standing (fully erect), he does not return and performs sujud al-sahw at the end.
The criterion is the lower half of the body: if the lower half is straight, he is closer to standing.
4
Apply the ruling for the last sitting and note intra-Hanafi differences
If the last sitting is forgotten and the person remembers before prostrating for the next rak'ah, he returns. If he has already prostrated, the prayer is invalidated according to Abu Hanifa (upon raising the head) and Abu Yusuf (upon placing the forehead). However, Imam Muhammad allows building upon the prayer, and fatwa follows his view.
The practical consequence: according to the mufta bihi, the person can continue and later perform sujud al-sahw instead of repeating the prayer.

وقيل: لا، وهو الأشبه. (ط) لم يسجد للركعة التي قام عليها؛ لأن فيه إصلاح صلاته وأمكنه ذلك. (ط،ع) بطل فرضه: أي مطلقاً، سواء كان عامداً أو ساهياً؛ لأنه استحكم شروعه في النافلة قبل إكمال أركان المكتوبة، ومن ضرورته خروجه عن الفرض (فتح) برفعه وعند أبي يوسف بوضع الجبهة، وفائدة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا وضع جبهته فسبقه حدث فرفع رأسه للوضوء فتوضأ، فعند أبي يوسف لا يمكنه إصلاحها لبطلانها، وعند محمد يبني والفتوى على قوله [رمز الحقائق: ۸۷/۱]
By leaving a wajib, even if repeated. And the forgetfulness of his imam [applies to the follower] but not his own forgetfulness. If he forgets the first sitting (qa'dah), while he is in the fard, even if practically, if he is closer to it (the sitting), he returns; otherwise not, and he performs sujud al-sahw. And if he forgets the last [sitting], he returns as long as he has not prostrated [for the next rak'ah] and performs sujud al-sahw. If he prostrates, his fard is invalidated by his raising [his head from prostration?] due to delaying the fard of the sitting. 'By leaving a wajib' [attached to 'it is obligatory' i.e., sujud al-sahw is obligatory by leaving any wajib thing]. It inclusively covers advance, delay, and alteration, and includes leaving tashahhud or part of it because it is a composed dhikr, and the takbir of ruku' in the second rak'ah of the two Eids, and the takbir of qunut according to some. So sujud al-sahw is obligatory for leaving a wajib like leaving the first sitting, or delaying a wajib like delaying the recitation of al-Fatiha, or altering a wajib like reciting aloud where it should be silent or vice versa, or delaying a rukn like forgetting an obligatory prostration then remembering it in the second rak'ah and performing it, or delaying standing to the third by more than the extent of tashahhud, or repeating a rukn such as bowing twice or prostrating three times, or advancing a rukn such as bowing before reciting or prostrating before bowing. The author's statement 'by leaving a wajib' includes all, and two prostrations suffice even if the forgetfulness is repeated. (Fath) 'And even if repeated': leaving the wajib, so that no more than two prostrations are required. (T) 'And the forgetfulness of his imam etc.': i.e., upon the follower; because by following he becomes a follower of the imam, and it is not necessary that he was following at the time of forgetfulness. If he enters after the imam has prostrated one prostration of forgetfulness, he follows him in the second and does not make up the first. If after he has prostrated both, he does not make them up. If the imam does not prostrate, the follower does not prostrate because he would be opposing his imam, and he only undertook to perform as a follower. (Fath) 'Not by his own forgetfulness': i.e., it is not required upon him nor upon his imam [because of his own forgetfulness?]. The follower; because if he prostrates, it leads to opposition, and if the imam prostrates with him, the followed becomes a follower, which is not allowed. (Ayni) 'Closer': i.e., from standing. The meaning of closeness to sitting is that he raises his buttocks from the ground while his knees are on it, or it is said: as long as the lower half is not fully erect, he is closer to sitting; if he becomes erect, he is closer to standing, and the upper half is not considered. (Fath) 'He returns': as an obligation, and sits and recites tashahhud because what is close to a thing takes its ruling, and he does not perform sujud al-sahw according to the most correct view. (T, Ayni) 'Otherwise not': i.e., if he is not closer to sitting, he does not return because he is like one standing. This is determined by the lower half of a person: if the lower half is straight, he is closer to standing; otherwise not. (Ramz al-Haqaiq: 87/18) 'For sujud al-sahw': i.e., for leaving the wajib, i.e., the sitting. In the zahir al-riwayah: if he has not stood straight, he returns; if he has stood straight, he does not. If he returns, his prayer becomes invalid. And it is said: no, that is more similar. (T) 'He did not prostrate for the rak'ah he stood up from' because in it is the repair of his prayer and it is possible for him. (T, Ayni) 'His fard is invalidated': i.e., absolutely, whether intentional or forgetful; because he has firmly commenced a supererogatory act before completing the obligatory pillars, and necessarily he leaves the fard. (Fath) 'By raising his head from prostration' and according to Abu Yusuf, by placing the forehead. The benefit of the difference appears if he places his forehead and then had a hadath (ritual impurity) and raised his head for wudu and performed wudu. According to Abu Yusuf, he cannot repair it because it is invalidated; according to Muhammad, he builds upon it, and the fatwa is upon his statement. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 87/1]
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage explains the causes that necessitate sujud al-sahw and details the rulings when a forgetful person realizes his mistake, especially regarding the first and last sittings (qa'dah). The primary cause is 'leaving a wajib'—whether by omission, delay, change, addition, or repetition. This includes leaving the first sitting, delaying the recitation of al-Fatiha, reciting aloud when silent (or vice versa), delaying an obligatory prostration, etc. Importantly, even if the forgetfulness occurs multiple times, only two prostrations are required. The passage then discusses the follower's obligation: sujud al-sahw is due to the imam's forgetfulness, not the follower's own. If the follower errs independently, it is not addressed here. Next, it details the rule for forgetting the first sitting: if the person remembers while still close to the sitting position (i.e., not yet fully standing), he must return, sit, and recite tashahhud without an additional sujud al-sahw for that return. The criterion for closeness is based on the lower half of the body: if the buttocks are off the ground but knees still on it, or if the lower half is not straight, he is closer to sitting. If he has fully stood, he does not return and instead performs sujud al-sahw at the end. For the last sitting (tashahhud), if he forgets it and remembers before prostrating for the next rak'ah, he must return; if he prostrated, the prayer is invalidated because he has effectively begun a new rak'ah (considered supererogatory) without completing the fard. There is a difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding when exactly the invalidation occurs: Abu Hanifa says upon raising the head from the additional prostration; Abu Yusuf says upon placing the forehead. The later fatwa follows Muhammad's view that one can build upon the prayer (ibna') in certain cases. The passage underscores that sujud al-sahw is a robust mechanism to rectify many errors without invalidating the prayer, but it requires attention to detail.

Key Terms
بترك واجب (bi-tarki wajib): By leaving a wajib (obligatory but not fard) act in prayer, such as the first sitting or tashahhud.
القعود الأول (al-qu'ud al-awwal): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs, in which tashahhud is recited.
عاد (‘ada): To return to a previous position (e.g., to sit after starting to stand) to correct an omission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person forgets the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah) in a 3-rak'ah prayer. He remembers after he has prostrated for the next rak'ah. According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon opinion) in the Hanafi school, what should he do?
A) He must repeat the entire prayer because it is invalidated.
B) He should sit immediately, complete the prayer, and perform sujud al-sahw at the end.
C) He should complete the extra rak'ah as part of the prayer and then perform sujud al-sahw.
D) He should stop praying immediately and repeat the prayer from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw is wajib for leaving any wajib act, and the decision to return to a missed sitting depends on physical proximity; the prayer can often be salvaged even after an erroneous prostration by following the preferred Hanafi view of building (ibna').

Causes of Sajdah al-Sahw: Omission, Delay, Change, Repetition
States causes of sajdah al-sahw and unity of compensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four categories of causes that necessitate sajdah al-sahw and state that one set of two prostrations suffices for multiple forgetful acts in a single prayer.

Core Idea
Two sajdahs cover any number of forgetful acts in one prayer.

Sajdah al-sahw compensates for forgetfulness during prayer. This lesson classifies its causes: omission, delay, change, and repetition of an obligatory (wajib) act—and crucially, multiple lapses require only one set of two prostrations. Understanding this saves the worshipper from unnecessary additions in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
From the text, extract the four general causes: omitting a wajib (tark), delaying a wajib (ta'khir), changing a wajib (taghyir), and repeating a rukn or wajib (takrar). Also note that advancing (taqdim) falls under change.
The author's phrase 'by abandoning an obligatory [act]' is a broad umbrella covering all specific cases.
2
Map each category to examples
For each category, list the examples given: omission of first tashahhud, delay of Fatihah recitation, change from jahr to sirr or vice versa, repetition of two rukus, etc.
The examples help internalise what counts under each category.
3
Recognise the single compensation
Understand that the phrase 'two prostrations suffice even if forgetfulness is repeated' means multiple forgetful acts in one prayer require only one set of two sajdahs, not separate sets for each lapse.
This is a practical mercy: the worshipper does not repeat sajdah al-sahw for each mistake.
4
Apply to a scenario
Practice with a hypothetical: someone omits the first sitting and also repeats a ruku in the same prayer. Determine that one sajdah al-sahw suffices.
This step solidifies the ruling as actionable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو بترك واجب وإن تكرر، [متعلق بقوله: "يجب" أي يجب سجود السهو بترك شيء واجب. (ع)] وهو بإطلاقه شامل للتقديم والتأخير والتغيير وشامل لترك التشهد أو بعضه؛ لأنه ذكر منظوم، وتكبيرة الركوع في الركعة الثانية من العيدين وتكبيرة القنوت عند البعض أي يجب سجود السهو بترك واجب كترك القعدة الأولى أو تأخير واجب كتأخير قراءة الفاتحة أو تغيير واجب كالجهر فيما يخافت وبالعكس، أو تأخير ركن كترك السجدة الصلبية سهواً ثم تذكرها في الركعة الثانية فسجدها، وتأخير القيام إلى الثالثة بالزيادة على قدر التشهد، أو تكرار ركن بأن ركع ركوعين أو سجد ثلاث سجدات أو تقديم ركن بأن ركع قبل أن يقرأ أو سجد قبل أن يركع، وقول المصنف: "بترك واجب" يشمل الكل ويكفيه سجدتان وإن تكرر السهو. (فتح) وإن تكرر: ترك الواجب حتى لا يجب عليه أكثر من سجدتين. (ط)
Chapter of the prostration of forgetfulness: due to abandoning an obligatory [act], even if repeated. It is general, including [forgetfulness by] doing before, after, or changing [the obligatory act], and includes omitting the tashahhud or part of it because it is arranged dhikr, and the takbir of ruku in the second rak'ah of the two 'Eids and the takbir of qunut according to some. That is, sajdah al-sahw is required for omitting an obligatory [act] like omitting the first sitting, or delaying an obligatory [act] like delaying recitation of al-Fatihah, or changing an obligatory [act] like reciting aloud where it should be silent or vice versa, or delaying a pillar like forgetting a essential prostration then remembering it in the second rak'ah and performing it, or delaying standing to the third [rak'ah] by exceeding the amount of tashahhud, or repeating a pillar like performing two rukus or three sajdahs, or advancing a pillar like bowing before reciting or prostrating before bowing. The author's statement 'by abandoning an obligatory [act]' includes all, and two prostrations suffice even if forgetfulness is repeated. (Fath) 'Even if repeated': [meaning] the omission of the wajib, so that he is not required to do more than two prostrations. (Tah)
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the causes of sajdah al-sahw. The matn states that sajdah al-sahw is required for omitting a wajib, even if the omission is repeated. The commentator explains that 'by abandoning an obligatory [act]' includes three types: taqdim (doing a later part earlier), ta'khir (delaying), and taghyir (changing). Examples include omitting the first tashahhud, delaying the recitation of al-Fatihah, reciting aloud when required to be silent, delaying a prostration, or repeating a pillar like two rukus. The key point is that all these causes are covered by the author's phrase 'by abandoning an obligatory [act]', and one set of two prostrations suffices even if multiple forgetful acts occur.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer, wajib under certain conditions.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act less than fard; omission requires sajdah al-sahw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Four prostrations because the errors are of different types

Key Takeaway
One set of two prostrations compensates for any number of forgetful omissions, delays, changes, or repetitions of wajib acts in a single prayer.

The Follower's Sajdah al-Sahw: Following the Imam
Ruling on the follower's obligation for sajdah al-sahw: follows the imam, not his own forgetfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for a follower's sajdah al-sahw and apply it to scenarios of late joining and imam's omission.

Core Idea
The follower's sajdah al-sahw is dependent on the imam's – never for his own lapse.

In congregational prayer, the follower is bound to the imam's lead. This principle extends even to the corrective prostrations for forgetfulness. The passage clarifies that a follower never performs sajdah al-sahw for his own forgetfulness; he only follows the imam's sajdah. Understanding this rule prevents confusion and ensures the harmony of the congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the follower's sajdah al-sahw. Ruling: it is wajib upon the follower if the imam performs sajdah; it is not for his own forgetfulness.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard.
2
Understand the principle of dependency
The follower is a tabi' (dependent). His prayer is linked to the imam. Therefore, his sajdah al-sahw derives from the imam's.
This principle is central to the Hanafi ruling.
3
Apply to specific scenarios
If the follower joins after the imam has performed one prostration, he follows in the second only. If he joins after both, he does no sajdah. If the imam does no sajdah, the follower does none.
These are the key applications from the text.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools may allow the follower to perform sajdah for his own forgetfulness; the Hanafi school strictly follows the dependency principle.
This is a point of ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسهو إمامه لا بسهوه أي على المقتدي؛ لأنه بالاقتداء صار تبعاً للإمام، ولا يشترط أن يكون مقتدياً به وقت السهو، ولو دخل بعد ما سجد الإمام سجدةً من السهو يتابعه في الثانية، ولا يقضي الأولى، وإن بعد ما سجدهما لا يقضيهما، وإن لم يسجد الإمام لا يسجد المؤتم؛ لأنه مخالفاً يصير لإمامه، وما التزم الأداء إلا تبعاً. (فتح) لا بسهوه [ أي لا يجب عليه ولا على إمامه] أي المقتدي؛ لأنه لو سجد هو يؤدي إلى المخالفة، ولو سجد الإمام معه لانقلب المتبوع تابعاً، فلا يجوز. (ع)
And the forgetfulness of his imam [obligates sajdah] not his own forgetfulness. That is, upon the follower, because by following he becomes dependent on the imam. It is not a condition that he was following at the time of forgetfulness. If he enters after the imam has performed one prostration of forgetfulness, he follows him in the second and does not make up the first. If after he has performed both, he does not make them up. If the imam does not perform sajdah, the follower does not perform sajdah, because he would become opposing his imam, and he only undertook performance as a follower. (Fath) 'Not his own forgetfulness' [i.e. it is not required for him nor for his imam] i.e. the follower, because if he performs sajdah himself it leads to opposition, and if the imam performs sajdah with him, the followed would become a follower, so it is not permissible. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling for the follower (muqtadi) regarding sajdah al-sahw. The matn states: the forgetfulness of the imam (requires sajdah upon him), but not the follower's own forgetfulness. The commentator explains: the follower is a dependent of the imam, so he only follows the imam's sajdah. If he enters after the imam has done one prostration, he follows in the second but does not repeat the first. If the imam does no sajdah, the follower does none, as doing so would oppose the imam. The key principle: the follower's obligation is secondary to the imam.

Key Terms
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer, who follows the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Perform both prostrations immediately
B) Perform the first prostration only
C) Follow the imam in the second prostration and not make up the first
D) Not perform any sajdah al-sahw

Key Takeaway
A follower must never perform sajdah al-sahw for his own forgetfulness; he is bound to follow the imam's sajdah.

6 min
Returning for the First Tashahhud: Closer to Sitting
Ruling on returning to the first sitting when forgotten, based on proximity to sitting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether a person must return to the first sitting after forgetting it, based on the position of the lower half of the body.

Core Idea
Proximity to sitting is measured by the lower half of the body, not the upper.

Forgetting the first tashahhud is a common mistake in prayer. The Hanafi school provides a precise criterion for when to return to the first sitting, based on the body's position after standing. This passage explains the rule and its underlying measure, helping you apply it correctly in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is forgetting the first sitting (al-qu'ud al-awwal) in an obligatory prayer. The ruling depends on whether the person is closer to sitting or standing at the moment of recall.
The first sitting is wajib in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Understand the measure of proximity
The text states that proximity is determined by the lower half of the body. If the buttocks have been raised from the ground but the knees remain on the ground, the person is closer to sitting. If the legs are straightened (lower half upright), the person is closer to standing.
The upper half (torso) is not considered.
3
Apply the rule
If closer to sitting, the person must return (wajib), sit, and recite tashahhud. No sajdah al-sahw is needed. If closer to standing, they should not return and instead perform sajdah al-sahw at the end to compensate for the missed wajib.
Some narrations require sajdah al-sahw even after returning if the person was closer to sitting, but the most sound view (ashbah) says no sajdah.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school regarding returning when fully standing (straight upright). The zahir al-riwayah states that if a person returns after fully standing, the prayer is invalid. However, another view (considered more appropriate) holds that the prayer remains valid.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that the prayer does not become invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن سهى عن القعود الأول وهو أي المصلي في الفرض ولو عمليا إليه أقرب عاد، وإلا لا وسجد للسهو، أقرب: أي من القيام، ومعنى القرب إلى القعود أن يرفع إليتيه من الأرض وركبتاه إليها، وقيل: ما لم ينتصب النصف الأول فهو أقرب إلى القعود، وإن انتصب فهو إلى القيام أقرب ولا معتبر بالنصف الأعلى. (فتح) عاد: وجوباً، وقعد وتشهد؛ لأن ما قرب إلى الشيء يأخذ حكمه، ولا يسجد للسهو في الأصح. (ط،ع) وإلا لا أي وإن لم يكن إلى القعود أقرب لا يعود؛ لأنه كالقائم، ويعتبر ذلك بالنصف الأسفل من الإنسان، فإن كان النصف الأسفل مستوياً كان إلى القيام أقرب، وإلا لا. رمز الحقائق: ۸۷/۱۸] للسهو: أي لترك الواجب أي القعدة، وفي ظاهر الرواية: إن لم يستو قائما يعود، وإن استوى قائماً لا، فإن عاد فسدت صلاته، وقيل: لا، وهو الأشبه. (ط)
If he forgets the first sitting—that is, the praying person—in the obligatory [prayer], even if practically, if he is closer to sitting he returns, otherwise not, and performs sajdah al-sahw. 'Closer' meaning closer than standing. The meaning of proximity to sitting is that he raises his buttocks from the ground while his knees are on it. It is said: as long as he has not straightened the lower half, he is closer to sitting; if he straightens, he is closer to standing, and the upper half is not considered. (Fath) 'He returns' as an obligation, sits and recites tashahhud because what is close to a thing takes its ruling, and he does not perform sajdah al-sahw according to the most sound. (Tah, Ayni) 'Otherwise not': meaning if he is not closer to sitting, he does not return because he is like one standing. This is determined by the lower half of the person: if the lower half is upright, he is closer to standing, otherwise not. Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 87/18] 'For forgetfulness': meaning for omitting the wajib, i.e. the sitting. And in the zahir al-riwayah: if he is not straight while standing, he returns; if he is straight while standing, he does not. If he returns, his prayer is invalid; it is said: no, and that is more appropriate. (Tah)
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage details the ruling when one forgets the first tashahhud (al-qu'ud al-awwal) in an obligatory prayer. The matn says: if the person is closer to sitting than standing, he must return; otherwise, he continues and performs sajdah al-sahw. The commentator defines 'closer' based on the lower half of the body: if he has raised his buttocks but knees are on ground, he is closer to sitting; if he has straightened his legs, he is closer to standing. He must return only if closer to sitting. If he returns, it is obligatory to sit and recite tashahhud, and according to the most sound view, he does not need sajdah al-sahw. There is also a narration from Zahir al-Riwayah that if he is not fully standing, he returns; if fully standing, he does not, and if he returns, it invalidates the prayer, but another view says it does not.

Key Terms
القعود الأول (al-qu'ud al-awwal): The first sitting after the second rak'ah in prayers of three or four rak'ahs, during which the first tashahhud is recited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what determines whether one must return to the first sitting after forgetting it?
A) The upper half of the body
B) Whether the person has prostrated for the next rak'ah
C) Whether the lower half is upright or not
D) The intention of the person

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines proximity to sitting by the lower half of the body; returning is wajib only when closer to sitting, otherwise sajdah al-sahw suffices.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Moment of Invalidity When Adding a Fifth Rak'ah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on invalidity moment when adding a fifth rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when a forgotten fifth rak'ah invalidates the obligatory prayer, distinguish the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and apply the ruling when a sixth rak'ah is added.

Core Idea
Adding a fifth rak'ah turns the prayer to nafl; the moment of invalidity differs among Hanafi imams.

When a worshipper forgets the last tashahhud and stands for a fifth rak'ah, does the prayer become invalid immediately upon prostrating, or only after raising? This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and explains how to complete the prayer by adding a sixth rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act: forgetting the last tashahhud and standing for a fifth rak'ah. Ruling: if one prostrates for that fifth, the obligatory prayer becomes invalid (batil) and turns into a nafl (supererogatory) prayer. A sixth rak'ah must be added to form a valid pair of nafl.
This is the general ruling according to the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
The dispute concerns the exact moment the prayer becomes invalid. Abu Yusuf holds it is by placing the forehead on the ground (sajdah) for the fifth rak'ah. Muhammad holds it is by raising the head from that sajdah. The fatwa is on Muhammad's view.
Also, a separate dispute (ambiguous in text) may exist regarding whether the fifth rak'ah completes the fard or not; the relied-upon position is that it becomes nafl.
3
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
The difference matters when a break (hadath) occurs after placing the forehead but before raising. According to Abu Yusuf, the prayer is invalid and cannot be repaired. According to Muhammad, one can build upon it (yabni) after making wudu.
This is the key application of the ikhtilaf in daily practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن سهى عن الآخر عاد ما لم يسجد أي القعود وسجد للسهو، فإن سجد بطل فرضه برفعه لتأخير فرض القعود القعود إلى القعود بطل فرضه: أي مطلقاً، سواء كان عامداً أو ساهياً؛ لأنه استحكم شروعه في النافلة قبل إكمال أركان المكتوبة، ومن ضرورته خروجه عن الفرض (فتح) برفعه وعند أبي يوسف بوضع الجبهة، وفائدة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا وضع جبهته فسبقه حدث فرفع رأسه للوضوء فتوضأ، فعند أبي يوسف لا يمكنه إصلاحها لبطلانها، وعند محمد يبني والفتوى على قوله [رمز الحقائق: ۸۷/۱] وصارت نفلاً فيضم سادسة، وإن قعد في الرابعة ثم قام عاد وسلّم، وإن سجد للخامسة الركعات الخمس عندهما خلافا لمحمد إليها ركعة الركعة إلى القعود تم فرضه، وضم سادسة لتصير الركعتان نفلاً، وسجد للسهو ولو سجد للسهو في شفع الزائدتان لتأخيره السلام التطوع لم يين شفعاً آخر عليه
And if he forgets the last [sitting], he returns as long as he has not prostrated [for the next rak'ah] and performs sajdah al-sahw. If he has prostrated, his obligatory prayer becomes invalid due to his raising [for the fifth rak'ah]? because he has delayed the obligation of sitting... His obligatory prayer becomes invalid: absolutely, whether intentionally or forgetfully, because he has firmly entered into supererogatory prayer before completing the pillars of the obligatory prayer, and necessarily he exits the obligatory [prayer]. (Fath) 'By his raising' and according to Abu Yusuf, by placing the forehead. The benefit of the difference appears when he places his forehead and then hadath preceded him, so he raises his head for wudu and performs wudu: according to Abu Yusuf he cannot repair it because it is invalid; according to Muhammad he builds [upon it] and the fatwa is upon his saying. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 87/1] And it becomes nafl, so he adds a sixth. If he sat in the fourth then stood, he returns and says salam. If he prostrated for the fifth—the five rak'ahs according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) contrary to Muhammad?—the rak'ah added to the sitting completes his obligatory prayer, and he adds a sixth to make the two rak'ahs nafl, and performs sajdah al-sahw for delaying the salam. And if he performed sajdah al-sahw in a pair of supererogatory [rak'ahs], he does not build another pair upon it.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage covers multiple rulings. First, if one forgets the last tashahhud and stands for a fifth rak'ah: if he has not prostrated for that rak'ah, he must return, sit, complete the tashahhud, and perform sajdah al-sahw. If he has already prostrated, his obligatory prayer becomes invalid (batil) and it becomes a nafl prayer; he must add a sixth rak'ah to make the pair. The text notes a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf says invalidity occurs by placing the forehead (sajdah), while Muhammad says by raising from sajdah. The fatwa is on Muhammad's view. Regarding the fifth rak'ah: if one sits in the fourth then stands for a fifth, he must return and say salam. If he prostrates for the fifth, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two) the obligatory prayer is completed with that rak'ah, but one must add a sixth to make the two extra rak'ahs a valid nafl. Abu Hanifa's view differs (not fully detailed here). The text also briefly mentions that if one performs sajdah al-sahw in a supererogatory prayer of two rak'ahs, he cannot add another pair because it would invalidate the sajdah.

Key Terms
القعود الآخر (al-qu'ud al-akhir): The final sitting after the last rak'ah, during which the tashahhud and salam are performed.
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostrations of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory (voluntary) prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Upon standing for the fifth rak'ah
B) Upon placing the forehead for the fifth sajdah
C) Upon raising the head from the fifth sajdah
D) Upon completing the fifth rak'ah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that adding a fifth rak'ah after forgetting the last tashahhud turns the prayer to nafl, requiring a sixth, and the moment of invalidity is upon raising from sajdah per the fatwa.

Building After Sajdah al-Sahw in Nafl
Ruling on building upon sajdah al-sahw in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building additional rak'ahs after performing sajdah al-sahw in a supererogatory prayer and explain the consequence if one does so.

Core Idea
Building after sajdah al-sahw in nafl invalidates the sajdah; if done, it is valid but makruh tahrimi.

When performing a two-rak'ah nafl prayer, if one forgets and performs sajdah al-sahw, can he then add more rak'ahs? This lesson explains why building is not allowed and what happens if he does so anyway.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its normal ruling
Understand that the base act is a two-rak'ah nafl prayer with sajdah al-sahw performed at the end.
Sajdah al-sahw is performed after salam for forgetfulness.
2
Understand why building is prohibited
Building would place the sajdah in the middle of the prayer, invalidating it because sajdah al-sahw must be at the end.
The sajdah is intended for the first two rak'ahs only.
3
Know the consequence if one builds anyway
If one builds, the prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi, and the sajdah al-sahw must be repeated at the end.
Invalidation of sajdah does not invalidate the whole prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سجد للسهو في شفع الزائدتان لتأخيره السلام التطوع لم يين شفعاً آخر عليه، ولو سجد للسهو : أي لو صلى ركعتين تطوعاً وسها فيهما وسجد للسهو، فأراد أن يبني عليهما أخريين لم يين عليهما ؛ لأنه يبطل سجوده؛ لوقوعه في وسطها وإنما قيد الصلاة بالتطوع؛ لأن المسافر لو ركعتين وسها فيهما، وسجد للسهو، ثم نوى الإقامة، فإنه يتم صلاته أربعاً، ولم تفد السجدة السابقة فعليه إعادته. (مسكين للسهو لتأخيره السلام، ولا تنوبان عن سنة الظهر في الأصح. (ط، ع) التطوع : بأن تنفل شفعا وسها فيهما وسجد للسهو . (ع) عليه : أي لو أراد أن يبني عليهما لم يبن لئلا يبطل ما أدى من سجود السهو بلا ضرورة؛ لأنه يقع في وسط الصلاة، هذا ومع لو بني صح و وكره تحريماً ويعيد سجود السهو؛ لأنه بطل. (ط، ع) للقطع: أي ناوياً قطع الصلاة ما لم يتحول عن القبلة أو لم يتكلم لبطلان التحريمة؛ لأن هذا السلام غير قاطع لحرمة الصلاة، فلا ينقطع الإحرام، فلما نوى القطع كانت نيته تغييراً للمشروع فتلغو نيته. (فتح)
And if he performs sajdah al-sahw in a pair of supererogatory [rak'ahs]... for delaying the salam, the supererogatory [prayer] does not allow building another pair upon it. And if he performs sajdah al-sahw: meaning if he prays two rak'ahs as supererogatory and forgets in them and performs sajdah al-sahw, then wants to build another two upon them, he does not build because it invalidates his sajdah, since it occurs in the middle of it. And the prayer is restricted to supererogatory because if a traveler prays two rak'ahs and forgets and performs sajdah al-sahw, then intends to stay, he completes his prayer as four, and the previous sajdah does not benefit, so he must repeat it. (Miskin? For sajdah al-sahw for delaying salam, and they do not substitute for the sunnah of Zuhr according to the most sound. (Tah, Ayni) 'Supererogatory': meaning he prays a pair of nafl and forgets and performs sajdah al-sahw. (Ayni) 'Upon it': meaning if he wants to build upon them, he does not build so as not to invalidate the sajdah he performed without necessity, because it occurs in the middle of the prayer. Nevertheless, if he builds, it is valid but makruh tahrimi, and he must repeat the sajdah al-sahw because it became invalid. (Tah, Ayni) 'For cutting': meaning intending to cut the prayer, as long as he has not turned away from the qiblah or spoken, because the tahrimah would not be invalidated? Actually: because this salam is not decisive of the prayer's sacredness, so the ihram is not broken. When he intended cutting, his intention was a change of the prescribed act, so his intention is nullified. (Fath)
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage covers two separate rulings. First, concerning supererogatory (nafl) prayers: if one prays two rak'ahs and forgets, then performs sajdah al-sahw, he cannot later add two more rak'ahs to make it a four-rak'ah prayer because that would place the sajdah in the middle of the prayer, invalidating it. However, if he does build, it is valid but makruh tahrimi, and he must repeat the sajdah al-sahw. A special case: a traveler who prays two rak'ahs (as qasr) and performs sajdah al-sahw, then intends to stay (making it four), he must repeat the sajdah. Second, about salam intended to cut the prayer: if a person says salam with the intention to end the prayer (qat'), it does not actually exit him from the prayer as long as he has not turned away from the qiblah or spoken. His intention to cut is ineffective because salam is only legally cutting when done properly; the intention alone does not break the ihram.

Key Terms
التطوع (al-tatawwu'): Supererogatory prayer, also called nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
B) The prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi and sajdah must be repeated
C) The prayer is valid and no repeat of sajdah is needed
D) The prayer is invalid but sajdah is still valid

Key Takeaway
In a nafl prayer, building after sajdah al-sahw is not allowed, but if done, the prayer is valid with karahah and the sajdah must be repeated.

Salam Intended to Cut the Prayer
Ruling on salam intended to cut the prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi ruling on salam uttered with the intention to end the prayer and explain its effect.

Core Idea
Salam with intent to cut does not exit prayer until turning or speaking; intention alone is ineffective.

What if a person says the final salam but intends to cut the prayer early? Does that exit him from prayer? This lesson clarifies that the intention alone does not break the sacredness of prayer; a physical action is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its intended effect
The act is saying salam with the intention (niyyah) to terminate the prayer immediately.
Salam is normally the exit from prayer.
2
Understand why intention alone is insufficient
In Hanafi fiqh, the salam itself is decisive only when done properly; the intention to cut is not a valid exit because it changes the prescribed act.
The prayer's sacredness (hurmah) remains until a physical disruption.
3
Know the conditions for actual exit
Exiting the prayer requires either turning away from the qiblah or speaking, as these clearly indicate the end.
The text says: 'as long as he has not turned away from the qiblah or spoken.'

القطع (al-qat'): Intentionally ending the prayer by any means, but salam alone is insufficient without turning or speaking.

Ruling on Doubt about Rak'ahs for the First Time
Ruling on doubt about rak'ah count for the first time forgetfulness: must restart prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on doubt about the number of rak'ahs for the first time, identify the conditions (first-time occurrence, before finishing), and apply it to a scenario.

Core Idea
If doubt about rak'ahs is your first forgetfulness, you must restart; if habitual or after the prayer, you ignore it.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a specific scenario: a worshipper experiences doubt about the number of rak'ahs performed, and it is the first time such doubt occurs. The Hanafi school distinguishes between habitual and non-habitual forgetfulness. Here, the ruling is clear: if the doubt happens before finishing the prayer, the entire prayer must be restarted. The passage also explains the timing and the meaning of 'first time'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the doubt scenario
The passage applies to doubt about how many rak'ahs were prayed (one, two, three, or four) for the first time. 'First time' means this is not a habitual occurrence of forgetfulness.
The doubt must be about the number of rak'ahs, not other elements.
2
Determine the timing of the doubt
The ruling differs based on when the doubt occurs. If it occurs before finishing the prayer (before salam or before sitting for tashahhud), the prayer must be restarted. If after finishing or after sitting for tashahhud, the prayer is valid and no action is required.
The exception: if a trustworthy person informs after salam that the prayer was incomplete, and the worshipper is uncertain, he repeats as a precaution.
3
Understand the condition 'first time'
'First time' means the forgetfulness is not a habit. It could be the first such occurrence in his lifetime or in that specific prayer. The preferred interpretation is the first occurrence in his life (not habitual).
This distinguishes from the one who frequently forgets; such a person should not restart but should act on his predominant assumption.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a scenario, check: Is this the first time? Is the doubt before finishing? If yes to both, the ruling is to restart. If habitual or after finishing, the prayer is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(عيني، فتح)
And if he doubts how many he prayed for the first time, he restarts. That is, before finishing. As for after finishing or after he has sat the measure of tashahhud, there is nothing upon him even if before salam, except that if a trustworthy person informs him after salam that he did not pray Zuhr as four, and he doubts his truthfulness and falsehood, he repeats it as a precaution. 'Prayed': one, two, three, or four. (Tah, Ayni) 'First time' means that forgetfulness is not a habit for him, not that he has never forgotten in his life. It is said: the first forgetfulness that occurred to him in his life and he had not forgotten in his prayer at all after reaching puberty. And it is said: the first of the prayer, and the first is more correct. His statement 'restarts': meaning his mentioned prayer, due to his saying: 'When one of you doubts in his prayer about how many he prayed, let him restart the prayer.' And restarting is only conceivable by exiting the first, and that is by salam, speech, or an action contrary to prayer, and by salam while sitting is better because it is a legally permitted release. Mere intention is futile because one does not exit the prayer by it. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage deals with doubt about the number of rak'ahs performed when such doubt occurs for the first time in one's prayer life (i.e., the person is not habitually forgetful). The ruling is that he must restart the entire prayer (ista'naf). This is based on a hadith. The doubt must occur before finishing the prayer. If it occurs after completing the prayer or after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, it is disregarded. However, if a reliable person informs him after salam that he only prayed three, and he is uncertain, he should repeat as a precaution. The key condition: 'first time' means this is not his usual habit of forgetfulness. The commentator clarifies that exiting the prayer for restart requires salam, speech, or an action contrary to prayer; mere intention is insufficient.

Key Terms
أول مرة (awwal marrah): The first occurrence of forgetfulness in prayer, not habitual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Whenever doubt occurs
B) Only if the doubt occurs after finishing the prayer
C) Only if the doubt occurs for the first time (non-habitual) and before finishing
D) Only if the doubt is confirmed by another person

Key Takeaway
If you doubt the number of rak'ahs for the first time before finishing the prayer, you must restart the entire prayer.

Adding a Fifth Rak'ah Turns Fard to Nafl
Ruling on inadvertently adding a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah fard prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for adding a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah fard prayer, distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and apply the remedy of adding a sixth rak'ah.

Core Idea
Accidentally adding a fifth rak'ah does not invalidate prayer; it becomes nafl, requiring a sixth to form a pair.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a common mistake: standing for an extra rak'ah during a four-rak'ah fard prayer. The Hanafi school provides a clear remedy that preserves validity. The key insight is that the final sitting completes the fard, and the additional rak'ah transforms the intention to nafl. The passage also presents an intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Muhammad, who deems the prayer nullified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
A person praying a four-rak'ah fard (e.g., Zuhr) mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah.
This applies after the final sitting of the fourth rak'ah.
2
State the Ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
The prayer becomes nafl; the worshiper must complete the fifth rak'ah and add a sixth to form a pair (nafl is prayed in pairs). Then perform sujud al-sahw.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
3
Contrast with Imam Muhammad's Position
Imam Muhammad holds that the original fard prayer is nullified (batil) and no addition is possible; the prayer must be restarted.
Zufar also requires adding a sixth but considers the prayer still fard with the addition.
4
Analyze the Basis for the Difference
Abu Hanifa views the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) as a rukn that completes the fard; the extra rak'ah nullifies the intention for fard but does not invalidate the prayer. Nafl is valid in pairs, so a sixth is needed.
Muhammad considers the extra rak'ah an interruption that invalidates the original intention entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو
وصارت نفلاً فيضم سادسة، وإن قعد في الرابعة ثم قام عاد وسلّم، وإن سجد للخامسة إليها ركعة الركعات الخمس عندهما خلافا لمحمد [؟] سادسة: [ندبا، وقيل وجوباً ولو في العصر ورابعة في الفجر، وأما المغرب فتصير أربعاً فلا حاجة إلى الضم. (ط)]؛ لأن التنفل بالوتر غير مشروع بل مشروع شفعاً حتى لو لم يضم لا شيء عليه، وهذا عندهما، وعند محمد: بطل أصل الصلاة، فلا يضم إليها شيئاً، وعند زفر يضم. (فتح، عيني) ثم قام: ولم يقيد الخامسة بالسجود. وسلّم: ليخرج عن الفرض بالسلام؛ لأنه واجب، ولا يسلم قائماً؛ لأنه غير مشروع. [رمز الحقائق: ۸۸/۱] تم فرضه لأنه قد أتى بالقعدة الأخيرة، ولكنه أخر السلام فقط، وعند الشافعي لا يتم بل يعود إلى القعود ويسلم؛ لأن السلام فرض [رمز الحقائق: ۸۸/۱] سادسةً: ليصير شفعاً؛ إذ الركعة الواحدة غير مشروع ولو في العصر على الأصح. (ط، ع) وسجد للسهو
Chapter of Sujud al-Sahw. And it becomes nafl, so he adds a sixth. And if he sat in the fourth [rak'ah] then stood, he returns and says taslim. And if he prostrated for the fifth [he adds a rak'ah] ... the five rak'ahs according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) contrary to Muhammad. Sixth: [recommended, and it is said obligatory even in Asr, and fourth in Fajr. As for Maghrib, it becomes four, so no need to add. (T)] because supererogation with witr is not prescribed, rather prescribed in pairs, so if he does not add, nothing is upon him. This is according to them; according to Muhammad: the original prayer is nullified, so he does not add anything. According to Zufar: he adds. (Fath, Ayni) Then he stood: and he did not restrict the fifth to prostration. And he says taslim: to exit the fard by the taslim because it is obligatory, and he does not say taslim while standing because it is not prescribed. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/88] His fard is completed because he performed the final sitting, but he only delayed the taslim. According to al-Shafi'i, it is not completed; rather he returns to sitting and says taslim because taslim is fard. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/88] A sixth: to make it a pair, because a single rak'ah is not prescribed, even in Asr according to the soundest opinion. (T, A) And he prostrates for forgetfulness.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq begins the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). It addresses a common scenario: a person praying a four-rak'ah fard prayer (like Zuhr) mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah. According to Abu Hanifa and his two companions (the 'Sahibayn'), the prayer is not invalidated but becomes a nafl prayer because the original intention for fard is overridden by the additional rak'ah. To make the nafl valid, a sixth rak'ah must be added so that it forms a complete two-rak'ah unit (since nafl is prayed in pairs). This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). Imam Muhammad holds that the original fard prayer is nullified entirely, and no addition is possible. Imam Zufar also requires adding a sixth, but his reasoning differs—he likely considers the original prayer still fard with an addition. The text also discusses the case where the person sits after the fourth rak'ah (the final sitting) and then stands: he should return and say taslim, as he has already completed the fard. This shows that the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) is a rukn that completes the fard, and the taslim, though obligatory (wajib), is not a pillar. Hence, if one stands after the final sitting, the fard is technically complete, but returning to perform taslim is necessary. The passage also notes a difference with the Shafi'i school, where taslim is considered a fard (pillar). Finally, the prostration for forgetfulness (sujud al-sahw) is required in these cases.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors or omissions in prayer.
نفلاً (naflan): Supererogatory (voluntary) prayer; here it indicates the fard prayer has been transformed into nafl.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; the minimum unit for nafl prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if someone mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah in Zuhr prayer, what should he do?
A) He should return to sitting and say taslim immediately.
B) He should complete the fifth rak'ah and then add a sixth, performing sujud al-sahw.
C) He should abandon the prayer and restart.
D) He should complete the fifth rak'ah and then say taslim without adding a sixth.

Key Takeaway
When a fifth rak'ah is added inadvertently in a four-rak'ah fard, the Hanafi school salvages it by adding a sixth and treating the whole as nafl.

Sujud al-Sahw in Voluntary Prayer and Related Rulings
Rulings on sujud al-sahw in voluntary prayer, following a forgetful imam, and cutting prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on sujud al-sahw in voluntary prayer, the effect of following a forgetful imam, the legal exit from prayer via taslim, and the correct response to first-time doubt about rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Once sujud al-sahw is performed, you cannot add more rak'ahs; taslim alone does not exit prayer unless combined with turning or speaking.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents several connected rulings about sujud al-sahw in voluntary prayers, the effect of a forgetful imam on followers, the legal exit from prayer, and the correct response to doubt. We will parse each ruling, understand its conditions, and note the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Analyze adding rak'ahs after sujud al-sahw in nafl
If you perform sujud al-sahw during a pair of voluntary rak'ahs, you cannot build another pair onto it. If you do, the sujud becomes invalid and must be repeated. Note the exception for a traveler who later intends to stay.
The prayer itself is valid but makruh tahrimi if added.
2
Evaluate follower's prayer when imam forgets
If a forgetful imam says taslim erroneously, and a follower joins, the follower's prayer depends on whether the imam later performs sujud al-sahw. If yes, the follower's prayer is valid; if not, it is invalid.
Follower's prayer is linked to the imam's prayer.
3
Examine taslim with intention to cut the prayer
Saying taslim with the intention of cutting the prayer does not actually exit the prayer unless the person also turns away from the qibla or speaks. Mere intention is insufficient; an external action is required.
This ruling prevents inadvertent nullification.
4
Determine rule for doubt on first occurrence
If a person doubts the number of rak'ahs for the first time (not habitual), he must restart the prayer. He cannot rely on the majority. Exiting the current prayer requires an overt act like taslim or speech.
Hanafi position: certainty is required for continuation.

التطوع : بأن تنفل شفعا وسها فيهما وسجد للسهو . (ع)
عليه : أي لو أراد أن يبني عليهما لم يبن لئلا يبطل ما أدى من سجود السهو بلا ضرورة؛ لأنه يقع في وسط الصلاة، هذا ومع لو بني صح و وكره تحريماً ويعيد سجود السهو؛ لأنه بطل. (ط، ع)
للقطع: أي ناوياً قطع الصلاة ما لم يتحول عن القبلة أو لم يتكلم لبطلان التحريمة؛ لأن هذا السلام غير قاطع لحرمة الصلاة، فلا ينقطع الإحرام، فلما نوى القطع كانت نيته تغييراً للمشروع فتلغو نيته. (فتح)
وإن شك إلخ: أي قبل الفراغ، أما بعد الفراغ منها أو بعد ما قعد قدر التشهد فلا شيء عليه وإن كان قبل السلام، إلا أنه لو أخبره عدل بعد السلام أنه ما صلى الظهر أربعاً وشك في صدقه وكذبه أعادها احتياطاً. صلى: واحدة أم ثنتين أم ثلاثاً أم أربعاً. (ط، ع)

(عيني، فتح)
And if he prostrates for forgetfulness in a pair of voluntary prayer, he does not intend [to build] another pair upon it. And if the forgetful one says taslim, and another follows him in prayer, then if he prostrates [sujud al-sahw], it is valid; otherwise no. And he prostrates for forgetfulness. And if he says taslim for cutting [the prayer], ... And if he doubts how many he prayed: the first time, he starts anew ... [commentary]
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This section covers several distinct rulings related to sujud al-sahw. First, if a person prays two rak'ahs of voluntary prayer (nafl) and commits an error requiring sujud al-sahw, he performs the sujud. After that, he cannot add another two rak'ahs to the same prayer, because adding more would place the sujud in the middle of the prayer (invalidating it). However, a traveler who prays two rak'ahs, forgets, does sujud, then intends to stay (thus completing the prayer as four) must repeat the sujud because the original sujud was done before the completion. Second, if a forgetful imam says taslim erroneously, a follower who joins him: if the imam later performs sujud al-sahw (after realizing), the follower's prayer is valid; otherwise, the follower's prayer is invalid. Third, if a person says taslim with the intention of cutting the prayer (i.e., ending it deliberately), the taslim does not actually cut the prayer unless he also turns away from the qibla or speaks, because the taslim without a valid reason is not considered a legal exit. Fourth, if a person doubts the number of rak'ahs for the first time (i.e., it is not a habitual forgetfulness), he must restart the prayer (istinaf) based on the hadith: 'If one doubts in his prayer, he should start over.' Exiting the first prayer requires a physical action like salam or speech; mere intention is insufficient.

Key Terms
شفع التطوع (shaf' al-tatawwu'): Two rak'ahs of voluntary prayer, the basic unit for nafl.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer.
استأنف (ista'nafa): To start the prayer anew from the beginning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a forgetful imam erroneously says taslim but later performs sujud al-sahw, what is the ruling for a follower who joined him after the taslim?
A) The follower's prayer is invalid because the imam's taslim ended the prayer.
B) The follower's prayer is valid because the imam's sujud al-sahw corrects the error.
C) The follower must also perform sujud al-sahw individually.
D) The follower's prayer is valid only if he also forgot.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, sujud al-sahw fixes forgetfulness in nafl but prevents adding rak'ahs; taslim alone does not exit prayer; and first-time doubt requires restarting the prayer.
