Frequent Doubt and Estimation in Prayer
Ruling on frequent doubt in prayer and method of taharri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for frequent doubt in prayer, apply the method of taharri or taking the lesser number, and identify when sujud al-sahw is wajib.

Core Idea
Frequent doubt is relieved by estimation (taharri); otherwise certainty demands the lesser number, but sujud al-sahw is always wajib.

This lesson addresses how to handle recurring doubt about the number of rak'ahs during prayer. The Hanafi school provides relief from hardship through estimation (taharri) or relying on the lesser number, with the obligation of sujud al-sahw in every case. The ruling is supported by a hadith and the principle of avoiding undue repetition.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish first-time vs. frequent doubt
The passage clarifies that first-time doubt (once) requires restarting the prayer (ista'nafa), while frequent doubt (occurring more than once) permits taharri or taking the lesser. Understand which rule applies.
First-time doubt ruling is from another text; this lesson focuses on frequent doubt.
2
Apply taharri when possible
If doubt is frequent, the person should estimate (taharri) based on their stronger opinion. For example, if unsure between 3 and 4, choose the one he feels is more likely.
Taharri means using his best judgment (bi akbar ra'ihi).
3
Take the lesser when no estimation is possible
If he cannot estimate, he must take the lower number (al-aqall) because it is certain. Build the prayer on that.
This applies even if he did not have any estimation.
4
Perform sujud al-sahw in all cases
Regardless of whether he used taharri or the lesser, sujud al-sahw is wajib. It is conditioned upon the doubt occupying him for at least the duration of a rukn and not engaging in recitation during doubt.
Sujud al-sahw must be performed after the prayer.
5
Distinguish deliberate mistaken taslim
If a person deliberately says taslim due to a wrong belief (e.g., thinking he is a traveler), the prayer is invalid and cannot be fixed by sujud al-sahw because the error was intentional, not forgetful.
This is an exception to the general rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كثر تحرى، وإلا أخذ الأقل. توهم مصلي الظهر أنه أتمها فسلم، ثم علم أنه صلى ركعتين أتمها وسجد للسهو.
وإن كثر تحرى لقوله عليه السلام "من شك في صلاته فليتحر الصواب" ولا معارضة بين الحديثين؛ لأن ذلك محمول على ما إذا وقع له أول مرة، وهذا على ما إذا وقع له غير مرة ولم يجعل الأمر بالعكس؛ لأنه يوجب ترك العمل بأحدهما. [رمز الحقائق: ۸۹/۱] وقال في "الفتح": ولأنه يقع الحرج بالإعادة في كل مرة. تحرى: أي أخذ بالأحرى وهو بأكبر رأيه. (ط) وإلا أخذ الأقل وإن لم يكن وقع له تحر على شيء. [رمز الحقائق: ۸۹/۱] و لم يذكر المصنف سجود السهو في جميع صور الشك، وهو مما لا ينبغي إغفاله فإنه واجب سواء عمل بالتحري أو بنى على الأقل، وهو مقيد بما إذا أشغله الشك قدر ركن ولم يشتغل حالة الشك بقراءة أو تسبيح. (فتح) الأقل لتيقنه، وبنى عليه ويقعد في كل موضع يتوهم أنه موضع قعود، ويسجد للسهو في جميع صور الشك. (ط) أتمها: لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام صلى إحدى العشائين فسلم على رأس الركعتين، فقام ذو اليدين، فقال: أقصرت الصلاة أم نسيت يا رسول الله، فقال له: كل ذلك لم يكن، فقال: بعض ذلك قد كان، فأقبل على القوم وفيهم أبو بكر وعمر، فقال: أحق ما يقوله ذو اليدين، فقالا: نعم فقام وصلى ركعتين، وكان ذلك قبل تحريم الكلام في الصلاة وفي الحديث ما يدل على جواز السهو على الأنبياء، وهو يجوز فيما ليس سبيله البلاغ، والسهو الممتنع عليهم في الأخبار عن الله تعالى بالأحكام وغيرها ولقد أحسن من قال: يا سائلي عن رسول الله كيف سها والسهو عن كل قلب غافل لاه
قد غاب عن كل شيء سره فسها عما سوى الله في التعظيم الله (فتح)
وسجد للسهو بخلاف ما لو ظن أنه مسافر أو أنها الجمعة أو التراويح وهو في الظهر أو العشاء أو كان قريب عهد بالإسلام وظن الفرض ركعتين فسلم حيث تفسد صلاته؛ لأنه سلم عامدا. (ط،ع)
And if doubt is frequent, he estimates (taharri), otherwise he takes the lesser. [Example:] A Zuhr prayer imagined he completed it and said taslim, then knew he prayed two rak'ahs, so he completes it and prostrates for forgetfulness. And if frequent, he estimates due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever doubts in his prayer, let him estimate the correct.' There is no contradiction between the two hadiths; because that [first hadith about restart] is understood for when it happens the first time, and this [taharri] for when it happens more than once. And it is not made the opposite, because that would lead to abandoning one of them. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/89] And in al-Fath: because hardship would occur in repeating every time. Taharri: he takes the more likely, which is his stronger opinion. (T) Otherwise he takes the lesser, even if he did not have an estimation on anything. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/89] The author did not mention sujud al-sahw in all cases of doubt, but it should not be omitted; it is obligatory whether he acts on estimation or takes the lesser, and it is conditioned by doubt occupying him for the duration of a rukn and he does not engage in recitation or tasbih during doubt. (Fath) The lesser is certainty; he builds upon it and sits in every place he thinks is a sitting place, and prostrates for forgetfulness in all cases of doubt. (T) [Example:] He completed it: based on what is narrated that he (peace be upon him) prayed one of the two evening prayers and said taslim after two rak'ahs. Dhul-Yadain stood and said: 'Has the prayer been shortened or have you forgotten, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'Neither happened.' He said: 'Some of that did happen.' So he turned to the people, among them Abu Bakr and Umar, and said: 'Is what Dhul-Yadain says true?' They said: 'Yes.' So he stood and prayed two rak'ahs. This was before speech in prayer was prohibited. In the hadith is evidence for the permissibility of forgetfulness for prophets, and it is allowed in matters not related to delivering revelation. Forgetfulness is impossible for them in conveying news from Allah about rulings etc. And he prostrates for forgetfulness. Unlike if he thinks he is a traveler or that it is Friday or Tarawih while he is in Zuhr or Isha, or a new Muslim who thinks the fard is two rak'ahs and says taslim, then his prayer is invalidated because he deliberately said taslim. (T, A)
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage addresses how to handle doubt in the number of rak'ahs during prayer, distinguishing between first-time doubt (which requires restarting, as in the previous lesson) and frequent doubt. If a person frequently experiences doubt (e.g., he often cannot remember how many rak'ahs he has prayed), the law relieves him by allowing him to estimate (taharri) based on his stronger opinion. This is derived from a hadith: 'Whoever doubts in his prayer, let him estimate the correct.' If he cannot form an estimation, he should take the lower number (e.g., if he thinks it might be three or four, he takes three). In all cases of doubt, sujud al-sahw is obligatory at the end, provided the doubt occupied him for at least the duration of a rukn (e.g., a prostration) and he did not engage in other acts like recitation during the doubt. The text provides a practical example: someone prays Zuhr, mistakenly thinks he completed it, says taslim, then realizes he only prayed two rak'ahs. He stands and completes the remaining two, then performs sujud al-sahw. This is based on the well-known hadith of Dhul-Yadain (the Companion who informed the Prophet of his forgetfulness). The passage also clarifies that if a person deliberately says taslim based on a mistaken assumption (e.g., thinking he is a traveler or that it's Friday), the prayer is invalid because the taslim was intentional, not due to forgetfulness. This highlights the principle that the rulings on sujud al-sahw apply only to genuine forgetfulness, not to willful mistakes.

Key Terms
تحرى (taharri): Estimation based on one's stronger opinion to determine the correct number of rak'ahs in case of doubt.
شك (shakk): Doubt in the number of rak'ahs performed.
الأقل (al-aqall): The lesser number; taken when no estimation is possible, as it is certain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person frequently doubts whether he prayed three or four rak'ahs in Zuhr. He cannot estimate. What should he do?
A) He should restart the prayer.
B) He should take the lower number (three) and perform sujud al-sahw.
C) He should take the higher number (four) and perform sujud al-sahw.
D) He should continue based on his last certainty and not perform sujud al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, frequent doubt in prayer is resolved by estimation (taharri) or taking the lesser number, and sujud al-sahw is always wajib.

Dealing with Doubt in Prayer: Taharrī versus the Lesser
Explains rulings on doubt and sujud al-sahw in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for doubt in prayer, distinguish between frequent and infrequent doubt, and apply the obligation of sujud al-sahw.

Core Idea
For occasional doubt, take the lesser; for frequent doubt, use taharrī; sujud al-sahw is wajib in all cases.

During prayer, uncertainty about the number of rak'ahs is common. The Hanafi school provides a clear method: if doubt occurs frequently, one relies on taharrī (best judgment); otherwise, one bases the prayer on the lesser number. This lesson unpacks the textual evidence, the reconciliation of apparent conflicting hadiths, and the essential role of sujud al-sahw.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the passage deals with doubt (shakk) in the number of rak'ahs. The ruling hinges on whether the doubt is frequent or infrequent.
The act being ruled on is how to proceed when in doubt.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Whoever has doubt in his prayer, let him act on what he thinks is correct.' This is cited in the commentary to support taharrī.
The hadith is ahad, but considered sufficient for obligation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the imperative form 'falyataharrā' indicates obligation (wujub). Thus, taharrī is not merely a recommendation but required when doubting frequently.
This is a key distinction from schools that see it as sunnah.
4
Reconcile the hadiths
The commentary notes another hadith that seems to command taking the lesser. The reconciliation: the first hadith applies to repeated doubt (taharrī), the second to first-time doubt (take the lesser).
This shows the principle of jam' (reconciliation) over tarjīḥ (preference) when possible.
5
Evaluate the thamarah
The practical consequence: in all cases of doubt during prayer, sujud al-sahw is wajib. This is true whether one performs taharrī or builds on the lesser.
The passage emphasizes that sujud al-sahw must not be neglected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو
وإن كثر تحرى، وإلا أخذ الأقل. توهم مصلي الظهر أنه أتمها فسلّم، ثم علم أنه صلى الشك. ركعتين أتمها وسجد للسهو. فقط أي أتم الظهر أربعاً مثلاً على الوهم وإن كثر تحرى لقوله علي "من" شك في صلاته فليتحر الصواب، ولا معارضة بين الحديثين؛ لأن ذلك محمول على ما إذا وقع له أول مرة، وهذا على ما إذا وقع له غير مرة ولم يجعل الأمر بالعكس؛ لأنه يوجب ترك العمل بأحدهما. رمز الحقائق: ۸۹/۱] وقال في "الفتح": ولأنه يقع الحرج بالإعادة في كل مرة. تحرى: أي أخذ بالأحرى وهو بأكبر رأيه. (ط) وإلا أخذ الأقل وإن لم يكن وقع له تحر على شيء. [رمز الحقائق: ۸۹/۱] و لم يذكر المصنف سجود السهو في جميع صور الشك، وهو مما لا ينبغي إغفاله فإنه واجب سواء عمل بالتحري أو بنى على الأقل، وهو مقيد بما إذا أشغله الشك قدر ركن ولم يشتغل حالة الشك بقراءة أو تسبيح. (فتح) الأقل لتيقنه، وبنى عليه ويقعد في كل موضع يتوهم أنه موضع قعود، ويسجد للسهو في جميع صور الشك. (ط) أتمها: لما روي أنه عليه صلى إحدى العشائين فسلم على رأس الركعتين، فقام ذو اليدين، فقال: أقصرت الصلاة أم نسيت يا رسول الله، فقال له: كل ذلك لم يكن، فقال: بعض ذلك قد كان، فأقبل على القوم وفيهم أبو بكر الله وعمر الله، فقال: أحق ما يقوله ذو اليدين، فقالا: نعم فقام وصلى ركعتين، وكان ذلك قبل تحريم الكلام في الصلاة وفي الحديث ما يدل على جواز السهو على الأنبياء، وهو يجوز فيما ليس سبيله البلاغ، والسهو الممتنع عليهم في الأخبار عن الله تعالى بالأحكام وغيرها ولقد أحسن من قال: يا سائلي عن رسول الله كيف سها والسهو عن كل قلب غافل لاه قد غاب عن كل شيء سره فسها عما سوى الله في التعظيم لله (فتح) وسجد للسهو بخلاف ما لو ظن أنه مسافر أو أنها الجمعة أو التراويح وهو في الظهر أو العشاء أو كان قريب عهد بالإسلام وظن الفرض ركعتين فسلم حيث تفسد صلاته؛ لأنه سلم عامدا. (ط،ع)
Chapter on the Prostration of Forgetfulness. And if he frequently [has doubt], he does taharrī, otherwise he takes the lesser. A person praying Zuhr imagined that he completed it and said the salam, then he knew that he had prayed only two rak'ahs: he completes it and performs sujud al-sahw. [Commentary:] i.e., he completes Zuhr as four rak'ahs based on his imagination. And if frequently [has doubt], he does taharrī because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever doubts in his prayer, let him act on what he thinks is correct.' There is no contradiction between the two hadiths, because that [first hadith about taking the lesser] is carried upon the first occurrence, and this [taharrī] upon repeated occurrence, and it is not reversed because that would require abandoning one of them. In al-Fath: because hardship would occur from repeating every time. Taharrī: i.e., he takes the more likely, which is his best judgment. (t) Otherwise, he takes the lesser even if no preference occurred. (f) The author did not mention sujud al-sahw in all cases of doubt, which should not be neglected, for it is obligatory whether he acts by taharrī or builds upon the lesser, and it is restricted to when the doubt occupies him for the duration of a pillar and he does not engage in recitation or tasbih during the state of doubt. (f) The lesser is certain; he builds upon it and sits in every place where he imagines it is a place of sitting, and performs sujud al-sahw in all cases of doubt. (t) He completes it: because it is reported that he (peace be upon him) prayed one of the two evening prayers and said salam after two rak'ahs, so Dhu al-Yadayn stood up and said: 'Has the prayer been shortened or did you forget, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'Neither happened.' He said: 'But some of that did happen.' So he turned to the people, including Abu Bakr and Umar, and said: 'Is what Dhu al-Yadayn says true?' They said: 'Yes.' So he stood and prayed two rak'ahs, and that was before speech was prohibited in prayer. In the hadith is evidence for the permissibility of forgetfulness for prophets, which is permissible in matters not involving conveying, but forgetfulness is prevented in matters of conveying from Allah regarding rulings and other matters. And excellent is the one who said: 'O you who ask about the Messenger of Allah, how did he forget? Forgetfulness is from every heart that is heedless and negligent. He became oblivious to all things except Allah, so he forgot only what is besides Allah in glorification of Allah.' (f) And he performs sujud al-sahw, unlike the case where he thinks he is a traveler or that it is Friday or Tarawih while he is in Zuhr or Isha, or he is new to Islam and thinks the obligatory is two rak'ahs and says salam, for his prayer becomes invalid because he intentionally said salam. (t, a)
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary explains the rules for dealing with doubt in prayer. The chapter begins with the general rule: if a person experiences doubt frequently (i.e., it becomes a habitual problem), he should act on what seems most likely to him (taharrī). If the doubt is occasional, he must base his action on the lesser number (take the certainty). Then a specific example is given: a person praying Zuhr mistakenly thinks he has completed four rak'ahs and says the salam, but then realizes he only performed two. He should add the remaining two and perform sujud al-sahw. The commentary discusses the evidence, including the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who, when asked about forgetfulness, told the person to act on what he believes to be correct. The commentary clarifies that there is no contradiction between the hadiths; one applies to first-time doubt, the other to repeated doubt. The author then explains that sujud al-sahw is obligatory in all cases of doubt, provided that the doubt occurs for the duration of a pillar and the person does not engage in extra recitation or tasbih during the doubt. The passage also distinguishes this case from someone who mistakenly believes he is a traveler and shortens the prayer, etc., in which case the prayer is invalid due to intentional salam.

Key Terms
تحرى (taharrī): Acting on one's best judgment when in doubt between two possibilities.
شك (shakk): Doubt between two possibilities in prayer (e.g., number of rak'ahs).
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness or doubt in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a person do if he has frequent doubt in prayer?
A) Always take the lesser number.
B) Perform taharrī (act on best judgment).
C) Repeat the entire prayer.
D) Ignore the doubt and continue.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on doubt in prayer is to either perform taharrī (for frequent doubt) or build on the lesser (for infrequent doubt), with sujud al-sahw being wajib in both cases.

Prayer of the Sick: Sitting and Gestures
Ruling with proof for sick prayer adjustments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a sick person who cannot stand, including the conditions for sitting and gesture prayer, and identify the evidence from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Prayer remains obligatory; the manner adapts from standing to sitting to gesture, each with distinct rules.

In this lesson, we explore the classical Hanafi rulings on how a sick person performs prayer. The central principle is that the obligation of prayer is not waived, but its form is adjusted to the person's capacity. We will work through the conditions that allow sitting, the requirement to stand partially when possible, and the rules for gesture prayer (īmā'). The commentary expands on the evidence from the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn and the Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the obligatory prayer of a sick person. The ruling is fard 'ayn, but the manner depends on ability.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is the hadith 'Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side gesturing.' Also Quran 3:191 is cited.
The hadith is narrated by Imran ibn Husayn.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'salli qā'iman' shows obligation of standing; the conditional clauses show permissibility of sitting and gesturing when unable.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on leaning on a person for support. Abu Hanifa invalidates, Sahibayn accept if necessary.
The text says 'especially according to them (the two companions).'
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi is that if harm is not certain, standing is required even with hardship; the position on harm is the relied upon.
The text says 'on the most correct view, and upon that is the fatwa.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة المريض
باب صلاة المريض
من تعذر عليه القيام أو خاف زيادة المرض صلّى قاعداً يركع ويسجد، أو مومياً إن تع عايذرا، وجعل سجوده أخضر كيف شاء على المذهب أي صلى حال كونه قاعداً باب صلاة المريض [ أي هذا باب في بيان أحكامها والمرض معنى يزول بحلوله في بدن الحي اعتدال الطبائع الأربع. (ع)] اعلم أن للإنسان حالتين: الصحة، والمرض، فلما فرغ من الأولى شرع في الثانية، وكل من السهو والمرض عارض سماوي، إلا أن السهو أعم موقعاً لتناوله حالة المرض أيضاً فقدم وإضافة الصلاة إلى المريض من إضافة الفعل إلى فاعله. (فتح)
تعذر عليه القيام: قيد بتعذر القيام؛ لأنه لو قدر عليه متكنا أو متعمداً على عصا أو حائط لا يجزئه إلا كذلك خصوصاً على قولهما، فإنهما يجعلان قدرة الغير قدرة له، فإن لحقه نوع من المشقة لم يجز ترك القيام؛ لأنه إنما يجوز تركه إذا كان يلحق به ضرر على الأصح، وعليه الفتوى، فإن قدر على بعض القيام يقوم بقدر ما يقدر حتى لو كان قادراً على التكبير قائماً فقط يكبر قائماً؛ وكذا لو كان قادراً على بعض القراءة قائماً ولو آية يقوم بقدره، وقوله: "يركع ويسجد"؛ لقوله عليها العمران بن حصين: "صل قائماً، فإن لم تستطع فقاعداً، فإن لم تستطع فعلى الجنب تومئ إيماء". تتمة: وفي البحر الدليل على صلاة المريض قاعداً أو مستلقيا قوله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِينَ يَذْكُرُونَ اللَّهَ قِيَاماً وَقُعُوداً وَعَلَى جنوبهم (آل عمران:۱۹۱) قال ابن عباس وجابر وابن عمر الله إن الآية نزلت في الصلاة أي قياماً إن قدروا، وقعودا إن عجزوا عن القيام وعلى جنوبهم إن عجزوا عن القعود. (فتح) القيام: في الفرائض بحيث لو قام يسقط فهو المرض الحقيقي. (ع) المرض: وهو المرض الحكمي أو إبطاء البرء أو دوران الرأس أو كان يجد ألماً شديداً للقيام. [رمز الحقائق: ۸۹/۱]
ويسجد فالأول تعذر حقيقي والثاني حكمي. (مسكين) إن تعذرا أي كل واحد من الركوع والسجود، فإنه ليس تعذرهما معاً شرطاً؛ لأن من بحلقه خراج لا يقدر على السجود ويقدر على غيره يصلي قاعداً بالإيماء، ولو قدر على الركوع دون السجود سقط الركوع، ولو أخذته شقيقة ولا يمكنه السجود يومي وفي الاقتصار على بيان البدل للأركان الثلاثة أعني القيام والركوع والسجود إشارة إلى أن القراءة لا بدل لها عند العجز عنها، فيصلي بغير قراءة. وجعل سجوده إشارة إلى حذف مضاف أي إيماء سجوده أخفض من إيماء الركوع؛ لأن الإيماء قائم مقامهما فيأخذ حكمهما، ولا يلزمه في الإيماء تقريب الجبهة إلى الأرض بأقصى ما يمكن بل إذا أخفض رأسه لركوعه شيئاًما ثم للسجود أخفض منه جاز حتى لو سوى بينهما لا يجوز، ويكفيه أدنى الانحناء فيهما على وجه يقع التمييز بينهما بأن يكون الانحناء في إيماء السجود أحط منه في إيماء الركوع. ( فتح، مستخلص) أخفض: أي إيماء سجوده أخفض من إيماء ركوعه. (ط)
Chapter on the Prayer of the Sick. If standing is impossible or he fears increase of illness, he prays sitting, making ruku' and sujud, or by gestures if both are impossible, and makes his sujud gesture lower. [Commentary:] i.e., it is a dispensation for the sick. On the relied upon view, he prays however he wants. (a) i.e., he prays while sitting. Chapter on the Prayer of the Sick [This is a chapter explaining its rulings, and illness is a meaning whose entry into the living body removes the balance of the four humors. (a)] Know that a person has two states: health and illness. Since he finished the first, he begins the second, and both forgetfulness and illness are heavenly accidents, except that forgetfulness is more general because it encompasses illness as well, so it was presented first. Adding 'prayer' to 'the sick' is an addition of the action to its doer. (f) 'Standing impossible': it is conditioned by the impossibility of standing, because if he is able to stand by leaning [on something] or by supporting himself on a stick or wall, it is not sufficient for him except to do so, especially according to them (the two companions), for they consider the ability of others as his ability. If a type of hardship befalls him, it is not permissible to abandon standing, because abandonment is only permissible if it causes him harm according to the most correct view, and upon that is the fatwa. If he is able to stand partially, he stands to the extent he is able, such that if he is able to stand only for the takbir, he says the takbir standing. Likewise, if he is able to recite some verses while standing, he stands for that. And his statement: 'He makes ruku' and sujud' because of his statement (peace be upon him) to Imran ibn Husayn: 'Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side gesturing.' A supplement: In al-Bahr, the evidence for a sick person praying sitting or lying on his side is the statement of Allah: 'Those who remember Allah standing and sitting and on their sides' (3:191). Ibn Abbas, Jabir, and Ibn Umar said that the verse was revealed about prayer: i.e., standing if able, sitting if unable to stand, and on their sides if unable to sit. (f) 'Standing': in obligatory prayers such that if he stands, he falls, that is real illness. (a) 'Illness': which includes legal illness, or delay of cure, or dizziness, or severe pain when standing. (a) 'And he prostrates' – so the first is real impossibility, and the second is legal. (miskayn) If both [ruku' and sujud] are impossible, it is not a condition that both are impossible together, because one who has a boil on his throat cannot prostrate but can do other actions – he prays sitting with gestures. If he can do ruku' but not sujud, the ruku' is omitted and he gestures. If he suffers from migraine and cannot prostrate, he gestures. In restricting the mention of substitutes for the three pillars, i.e., standing, ruku', and sujud, there is an indication that recitation has no substitute when unable, so he prays without recitation. And his statement 'makes his sujud gesture lower' indicates an omitted word: i.e., the gesture of sujud is lower than the gesture of ruku', because the gesture stands in their place, so it takes their ruling. He is not required in gesture to bring the forehead close to the ground to the utmost extent; rather, if he lowers his head for ruku' a little, and then for sujud lowers it more, it is valid. Even if he makes them equal, it is not valid. It suffices for him the slightest bending in both in a way that distinguishes between them, such that the bending in sujud gesture is lower than in ruku' gesture. (f, mustakhlas) 'Lower': i.e., his sujud gesture is lower than his ruku' gesture. (t)
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the rules for the prayer of a sick person. It begins by establishing the principle that prayer is obligatory according to one's ability. The first ruling: if standing is genuinely impossible or would cause harm, one may pray sitting but still performs ruku' and sujud normally. If even that is impossible (e.g., cannot bend), one prays by gestures (īmā'), with the sujud gesture lower. The commentary explains that the condition for sitting is the inability to stand without harm, and if one can stand with support (like a stick), he must stand. There is a distinction between real and legal illness. The proof comes from the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn and the Quranic verse. The passage also discusses partial ability: one must stand for as much as he can. The text further clarifies that if only one of ruku' or sujud is possible, the other is waived and one gestures for it. Recitation has no substitute; if unable to read, one prays without recitation. The key detail is that the gesture for sujud must be lower than for ruku' to distinguish, but only a minimal difference is required.

Key Terms
مومياً (mūmi'an): One who gestures (with head) in place of bowing and prostrating.
إيماء (īmā'): Gesture used in prayer when one cannot perform ruku' or sujud physically.
مرض حقيقي (marad haqīqī): Actual illness where standing causes falling or severe harm.
مرض حكمي (marad hukmī): Legal illness such as fear of delayed recovery or severe pain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding a sick person who can only stand for part of the prayer?
A) He may pray entirely sitting.
B) He must stand for as much as he can.
C) He must pray lying on his side.
D) He must pray in a chair.

Key Takeaway
A sick person must pray according to ability, progressing from standing to sitting to gesture; the sujud gesture must be lower than the ruku' gesture.

Prostration on a Raised Object for the Sick
Ruling on validity of prostration on a raised object for the sick

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sick person prostrating on a raised object and explain the condition for its validity.

Core Idea
A sick person's prostration on a raised object is valid only if he actively lowers his head onto it.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a common concern for those praying while ill: when gesturing rather than actual prostration, can an object be raised to the face? The Hanafi ruling is nuanced: it depends on whether the person lowers his head onto the object or the object is placed on his forehead. A prophetic hadith guides the permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'raising something to the face to prostrate on it' for a sick person who prays with gestures. The ruling: if the person lowers his head onto the object, the prostration is valid; otherwise it is invalid.
The act of raising itself is considered makruh tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the Prophet's hadith: 'If you are able to prostrate on the ground, prostrate; otherwise, gesture with your head.' The hadith is cited to show that gesture must be by head movement.
The hadith is ahad and considered strong enough for prohibition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'gesture with your head' implies that the gesture must be performed by lowering the head. Raising an object to the face contradicts this command. Thus, raising is prohibited (makruh tahrimi).
The prohibition applies to the attendant who raises the object, not the patient.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may have different conditions. For instance, some allow passive placement if the person cannot lower his head. The Hanafi position is stricter: active lowering is required.
The Hanafi ruling is relied upon (mufta bihi) in this text.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is that raising is makruh tahrimi, but if done with active lowering, the prostration is valid. Al-Zayla'i's commentary clarifies the conditions, such as the object being on the ground and the person feeling its volume.
This ruling applies specifically when the sick person has reached the stage of gestures (ima').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة المريض
ولا يرفع إلى وجهه شيء يسجد عليه، فإن فعل وهو يخفض رأسه صح، وإلا لا، دف - أي والحال أنه لا يرفع الرواية في "يرفع" بضم الياء التحتية وفتح الفاء على بناء المجهول؛ لأن الظاهر أن المريض الذي بلغ حد الإيماء لا يقدر على رفع شيء إلى وجهه بل أن يرفع له غيره، والدليل على عدم جواز الرفع قوله : " إذا قدرت أن تسجد على الأرض فاسجد، وإلا فأوم برأسك. فلو رفع كان مكروهاً تحريماً [تبيين الحقائق: ٤٨٩/١] (مستخلص) عليه على ذلك الشيء الذي يرفع لورود النهي عن ذلك. (ع) فعل: على صيغة المجهول أي فعل الرفع المذكور. (ع) رأسه أي وإن لم يخفض رأسه هل وضع المرفوع على وجه (ط) صح أي بالإجماع، وقيل: هو سجود، قال الزيلعي [٤٨٩/١] وكان ينبغي أن يقال: لو كان الشيء الموضوع بحال لو سجد عليه الصحيح يجوز جاز للمريض على أنه سجود، وإن لم يجز للصحيح أن يسجد عليه فهو إيماء، فيجوز للمريض إن لم يقدر على السجود، وقوله: " وإلا لا" أي وإن لم يخفض رأسه ولكن وضع شيئاً على جبهته لم يجز، وإن كانت الوسادة موضوعة على الأرض وهو يسجد عليها جاز أي من حيث إنه إيماء في السجود، ويشترط أن يجد حجم الأرض حتى لو سجد على ما يجد حجمه من وسادة لم يكن ارتفاعها قدر لبنة أو لبنتين جاز على أنها بركوع وسجود. (فتح)
Chapter of the Sick Person's Prayer: And he should not raise something to his face to prostrate on it. If he does so and he lowers his head, it is valid; otherwise, no. Explanation: The narration is 'yurfa' with damma on the ya and fatha on the fa in the passive voice, because it is apparent that the sick person who has reached the stage of gestures cannot raise something to his face, rather someone else raises it for him. The evidence for the impermissibility of raising is his statement: 'If you are able to prostrate on the ground, prostrate; otherwise, gesture with your head.' So if he raises, it is makruh tahrimi. The prohibition is due to the forbiddance of that. 'Fa'ala' (he did) in the passive voice means the mentioned raising. 'His head' meaning even if he did not lower his head, but placed the raised thing on his face. 'Valid' meaning by consensus. It is said it is prostration. Al-Zayla'i said: It should be said: If the thing placed is such that a healthy person may prostrate on it, then for the sick person it is permissible as prostration; if not permissible for the healthy, then it is gesture, permissible for the sick if unable to prostrate. 'Otherwise no' meaning if he did not lower his head but placed something on his forehead, it is not valid. If the pillow is placed on the ground and he prostrates on it, it is valid in that it is a gesture in prostration. It is also stipulated that he feels the volume of the ground, so if he prostrates on something that he feels the volume of, like a pillow not higher than one or two bricks, it is valid as bowing and prostration.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on the sick person's prayer gives a ruling about prostration on a raised object. The ruling is part of the matn (base text) of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and the commentary expands with proofs and conditions. The core ruling: a sick person who prays with gestures (ima') should not have someone raise an object to his face to prostrate on it. If he does so and he lowers his head onto it (i.e., he actively lowers his head to the object), the prostration is valid. But if he does not lower his head and instead the object is placed on his forehead, it is not valid. The reason is that the gesture of prostration requires lowering the head, as in normal prostration. The hadith cited: 'If you can prostrate on the ground, do so; otherwise gesture with your head.' Raising an object to the face contradicts this command. The commentary clarifies that if the object is on the ground (like a pillow) and the sick person prostrates by lowering his head onto it, it is valid as a gesture, provided the height is not excessive (up to one or two bricks). This is a nuance of the Hanafi school: even in gesture prayer, the form of prostration should be approximated as much as possible.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing with the head to replace bowing and prostration when unable
المكروه تحريماً (al-makruh tahriman): An act prohibited by a strong but non-definitive evidence, close to haram

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What makes a sick person's prostration on a raised object valid?
A) The object is placed on his forehead
B) He actively lowers his head onto the object
C) The object is exactly the size of a brick
D) He does not move at all

Key Takeaway
For a sick person's gesture prayer, prostration on a raised object is valid only if he actively lowers his head onto it.

Gesturing Sitting vs Standing for the Sick in Prayer (Hanafi vs Shafi'i/Zufar)
Inter-madhhab dispute on posture for sick prayer plus ruling on continuity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prefers sitting gestures for the sick who can stand but cannot bow or prostrate, and distinguish this from the Shafi'i/Zufar position requiring standing gestures.

Core Idea
Gesturing sitting resembles prostration; the rukn of standing depends on achieving prostration.

When a person can stand but cannot bow or prostrate, should they gesture sitting or standing? The Hanafi school, based on the purpose of standing (to reach prostration), recommends sitting. This lesson unpacks the proof, the opposing view, and the practical consequence. We also cover what to do if one falls ill during prayer: complete what you can rather than restart.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two positions
The act: a sick person who can stand but cannot bow or prostrate. Hanafi position: gesture sitting (recommended). Opposing position (Zufar al-Shafi'i, Abu Yusuf in one narration): gesture standing.
The key difference is whether standing remains an integral (rukn) when prostration is impossible.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi dalil: the purpose of standing is to reach prostration (wasilah). If prostration cannot follow, standing loses its status as a rukn. Gesturing sitting is more similar to prostration (head lower), achieving the goal of humility.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) based on the meaning of the act.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
Zufar and al-Shafi'i argue that standing is a rukn in itself and does not fall due to inability to perform another rukn (bowing/prostration). They require gestures while standing.
Their view is based on the literal classification of standing as an integral regardless of subsequent actions.
4
Determine the Hanafi response and tarjih
The Hanafi response: standing's integrality is conditional on being followed by prostration. The text states 'standing is a means to prostration, so it falls with its fall.' The tarjih (preference) is for sitting gestures.
The madhhab dispute map highlights that the ikhtilaf is over preference (afdaliyya), not validity.
5
Apply the continuation principle (bina')
If a person falls ill during prayer, the correct view is to complete as much as possible (bina') rather than restart. This is based on the principle that performing part properly and part with gestures is better than all with gestures.
Contrary to a narration from Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa. The matn adopts the preferred view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يوم بعينه وقلبه وحاجبيه، وإن عذر الركوع والسجود لا القيام أوما قاعداً، ولو مرض في صلاته يتم بما قدر، 
 ... (مستخلص، فتح) وحاجبيه: خلافاً لزفر والشافعي وأبي يوسف في رواية. (ع) أومأ قاعداً وهو المستحب؛ لأنه أشبه بالسجود؛ لكون رأسه فيه أخفض وأقرب إلى الأرض، وهو المقصود، وقوله: "أوماً قاعداً" أولى من قولهم: "صلى قاعداً؛ إذ يفترض عليه أن يقوم، فإذا جاء أوان الركوع والسجود أومأ قاعداً، وإنما لم يلزمه القيام عند الإيماء للركوع والسجود؛ لأن المقصود من الصلاة الخضوع وا والخشوع، ويحصل ذلك بالركوع والسجود؛ لأن التواضع يوجد في الركوع ونهايته في السجود، والقيام وسيلة إلى السجود فيسقط بسقوطه، وقال زفر والشافعي يومئ قائماً؛ لأن القيام ركن فلا يسقط بالعجز عن أداء ركن آخر، ولنا: أن ركنية القيام ليتوسل به إلى السجدة؛ لما فيها من نهاية التعظيم، فإذا كان لا يعقبه السجود لا يكون ركنا، فالخلاف في الأفضلية وما قلناه أولى؛ لأن القعود أشبه بالسجود. (فتح، مستخلص) يتم بما قدر : بما قدر بحسب طاقته، فإن قدر على الركوع والسجود فعلهما، وإلا يؤمئ، فإن لم يقدر فيستلقى على الأصح، وقيل: يستأنف رمز الحقائق: ۹۰/۱] وروى أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة أنه يستقبل؛ لعدم جواز البناء؛ لأن تحريمته انعقدت موجبة للركوع والسجود، فلا يجوز بدونهما، ولهذا لزم الاستقبال، لكن قول المصنف: "يتم بما قدر" الأصح؛ لأن أداء بعض صلاته بركوع وسجود وبعضها بالإيماء أولى من أن يؤدى الكل بالإيماء. (فتح)
And if he does not gesture with his eye, heart, and eyebrows; and if he is excused from bowing and prostration but not from standing, he gestures while sitting. And if he falls ill during his prayer, he completes as much as he is able. ... And his eyebrows: contrary to Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and Abu Yusuf in one narration. He gestures sitting, and that is recommended because it resembles prostration since his head is lower and closer to the ground, which is the purpose. His statement 'gestures sitting' is better than saying 'prays sitting' because it is obligatory for him to stand, so when the time for bowing and prostration comes, he gestures sitting. The reason he is not obligated to stand during gestures for bowing and prostration is that the purpose of prayer is humility and reverence, and that is achieved through bowing and prostration; humility occurs in bowing and its peak in prostration. Standing is a means to prostration, so it falls with the fall of prostration. Zufar and al-Shafi'i say he gestures standing because standing is an integral (rukn) and does not fall due to inability to perform another integral. Our evidence: the integral of standing is for the sake of reaching prostration due to the ultimate glorification in it, so if it is not followed by prostration, it is not an integral. The disagreement is over preference, and what we say is better because sitting resembles prostration. 'Completes as able' according to his ability: if he is able to bow and prostrate, he does them; otherwise he gestures; if unable, he lies on his back according to the correct view. Some say he starts anew. Abu Yusuf narrated from Abu Hanifa that he begins anew because the validity of building (completing the prayer) is not permissible; his tahrimah (prohibition) was concluded requiring bowing and prostration, so it is not valid without them. But the author's statement 'completes as able' is more correct because performing part of his prayer with bowing and prostration and part with gestures is better than performing all with gestures.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage addresses two remaining issues: (1) when the sick person cannot even gesture with the head, what body parts may substitute? (2) if a person becomes unable to perform bowing and prostration during prayer but can still stand, should he gesture sitting or standing? On the first issue, the text mentions eye, heart, and eyebrows, noting disagreement with Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and a narration from Abu Yusuf. The Hanafi position (according to the matn) allows gesturing with the heart when others are impossible, but some imams allow eyes and eyebrows. On the second issue, if one can stand but cannot bow or prostrate, the preferred Hanafi view is to gesture while sitting, because sitting is more similar to prostration (head closer to ground). Zufar and al-Shafi'i require standing gestures because standing is an integral. The Hanafi response argues that standing's purpose is to reach prostration; if prostration cannot be done, standing loses its integral nature. Finally, if a person falls ill during prayer, he should complete what he can (continue with gestures) rather than restart, contrary to a narration from Abu Yusuf. This is based on the principle that performing part of the prayer properly and part with gestures is better than all with gestures.

Key Terms
الإيماء بالقلب (al-ima' bi al-qalb): The gesture of prostration by intention and mental representation when physical movement impossible
البناء (al-bina'): Continuing the prayer after interruption or change of ability

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a sick person can stand but cannot bow or prostrate, what is the preferred Hanafi position?
A) He gestures while standing
B) He gestures while sitting
C) He prays lying down
D) He postpones the prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers sitting gestures for the sick who can stand but cannot bow/prostrate, based on the purpose of standing as a means to prostration.

Limbs for Gesturing in Sick Person's Prayer
Ruling on permissible limbs for ima' with disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on permissible limbs for ima' and evaluate the opposing views based on textual and linguistic evidence.

Core Idea
Only the head may be used for gesturing in prayer; all other limbs are invalid substitutes.

When a person is too ill to bow and prostrate, they are allowed to gesture (ima') to fulfill these pillars. However, a key question arises: which parts of the body can be used for this gesturing? The Hanafi school, relying on the linguistic meaning of ima' and explicit hadith, restricts it to the head alone. Other scholars and even some Hanafi narrations allow other limbs, leading to a clear disagreement. In this lesson, we will trace the proof and understand why the relied-upon position insists on head-only gesturing.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core Hanafi ruling: gesturing (ima') is performed only with the head; the eyes, heart, and eyebrows are not substitutes.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opposing views
List the scholars who allow other limbs: Zufar (eyes, then heart), al-Shafi'i (heart and eyes), Hasan ibn Ziyad (eyebrows and heart with repetition), and Abu Yusuf in one narration (eyes, then heart).
Al-Shafi'i and Zufar are from outside the Hanafi school; Hasan ibn Ziyad and the Abu Yusuf narration are intra-Hanafi differences.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the reasoning of those who allow non-head gesturing: eyes are part of the head and can indicate lowering; the heart is the seat of intention and thus can substitute.
The opponents argue by analogy or by expanding the definition of ima'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the texts (hadith) are specific to the head, and substitution by opinion (ra'y) is impermissible. The hadith of Imran ibn Husayn shows that no further obligation exists beyond head gesturing.
The Hanafi response relies on the principle that substitutes (abdāl) are fixed by nass, not qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: if a sick person gestures with eyes or heart, according to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, their prayer is invalid and must be repeated upon recovery (if possible).
This contrasts with views that consider such gestures sufficient, at least provisionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يوم بعينه وقلبه وحاجبيه، وإن عذر الركوع والسجود لا القيام أوما قاعداً، ولو مرض في صلاته يتم بما قدر، ول و الارض محمد ما شرع صلاته قاعداً أي المصلى بعد أن عليه الصلاة وليلة لا يلزمه القضاء، وإن كان دون ذلك يلزمه؛ لأن مجرد العقل لم يكف لتوجه الخطاب، فقد ذكر محمد قطعت يداه من المرفقين وقدماه من الساقين لا صلاة عليه. (فتح، عيني) من ولم يؤم بعينه عند عدم القدرة على الإيماء برأسه. (ط)] بناء على أن مسمّى الإيماء لغة خاص بالرأس، وأنه بغيرها إشارة، وقد جاء مفسراً في قوله عليه السلام لذلك المريض: "وإلا فأوم برأسك ، واجعل سجودك أخفض"، ولا تتحقق زيادة الخفض بالعين ونحوها وقال زفر يؤمئ بعينيه، فإن عجز فبقلبه، وقال الشافعي: ينبغي أن يؤمئ بقلبه وبعينه، وقال الحسن بن زياد يؤمئ بحاجبه ،وبقلبه ويعيد متى قدر على الأركان، وفي رواية عن أبي يوسف يومئ بعينيه؛ لأنهما في الرأس فيأخذان حكمها، وإن عجز فبقلبه؛ لأن النية التي لا تصح بدونها إنما تقوم به، فتقام به الصلاة عند العجز ولنا أن نصب الأبدال بالرأي ممتنع والنص ورد بالإيماء بالرأس على خلاف القياس، فلا يمكن القياس على الرأس؛ لأنه يتأدى به ركن الصلاة أي السجدة دون هذه الأشياء، والحسن يقول: إن أركان الصلاة تؤدى بالأعضاء الظاهرة، أما الباطن فليس بذي حظ من أركانها، فلا يجوز الإيماء بالقلب، ولنا ما مرّ في حديث عمران بن الحصين فالله أحق بقبول العذر منه، أخبر النبي عليه السلام: "أنه معذور عند الله" في هذه الحالة، ولو كان عليه الإيماء بما ذكروا لذكره. (مستخلص، فتح) وحاجبيه: خلافاً لزفر والشافعي وأبي يوسف في رواية. (ع)
He does not gesture with his eye, his heart, or his eyebrows. If he is excused from bowing and prostration but not standing, he gestures sitting. If he falls ill during his prayer, he completes it with whatever he is able. ... And [gesturing] with his eyebrows: contrary to Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and Abu Yusuf in one narration.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the permissible limbs for gesturing (ima') in prayer when one cannot bow or prostrate. The Hanafi position is that only the head can be used for ima'; gestures with the eyes, eyebrows, or heart are insufficient. The proof is linguistic: ima' specifically means head movement, and the hadith instructs the sick person to 'gesture with your head' and make the prostration lower. The text presents the views of Zufar (gesturing with eyes, then heart), al-Shafi'i (with heart and eyes), Hasan ibn Ziyad (with eyebrows and heart, with repetition when able), and a narration from Abu Yusuf (with eyes, then heart). The Hanafi response is that substitution by opinion is impermissible; the text came with head gesturing contrary to analogy, so analogy cannot be extended to other limbs. Additionally, the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn shows that one is excused without mentioning these alternatives.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-imā’): Gesturing with the head in place of bowing and prostration when unable.
الأبدال (al-abdāl): Substitutes for the actual pillars of prayer (like ima' for sujud).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, which limb alone is used for gesturing (ima') in prayer?
A) The eyes
B) The heart
C) The head
D) The eyebrows

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, ima' in prayer is restricted to the head; other limbs do not substitute, as established by the explicit text and linguistic usage.

Preferred Posture for Gesturing: Sitting vs Standing
Determining whether to gesture while sitting or standing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the preferred posture for gesturing in prayer and explain the ratio legis (ta'lil) that supports it, distinguishing it from the opposing view.

Core Idea
Sitting to gesture is recommended because the goal is humility and prostration – standing is merely a means.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a practical question for the sick: when gesturing replaces bowing and prostration, should one sit or stand? The Hanafi school answers that sitting is preferable, and the reasoning reveals a deeper principle about the instrumental nature of standing in prayer. By studying this ruling, you will learn how Hanafi usul al-fiqh evaluates the relationship between means and ends in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its legal category
Determine the act under discussion (gesturing for ruku and sujud) and its hukm level. The text states it is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.
Mustahabb in Hanafi terminology is between sunnah and mubah – omission is not sinful.
2
Extract the Hanafi proof (ta'lil)
Find the reason given: standing is a means (wasila) to prostration; when prostration is replaced by gesture, the means falls. Sitting is recommended because it brings the head lower, better resembling prostration.
The proof is based on the purpose (maqsad) of the act: humility achieved through prostration.
3
Identify the opposing school and their proof
Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold that the sick should gesture while standing because standing is a pillar (rukn) that cannot be abandoned due to inability to perform another pillar.
This view emphasizes the independent obligatory nature of qiyam.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and the key principle
The Hanafi response affirms that the pillar status of standing is conditional upon being followed by actual prostration; without it, standing loses its obligatory character. The dispute is about optimality, not validity.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle that the purpose of a rukn may determine its necessity.
5
Determine the practical consequence and the mufta bihi
If one gestures while standing, the prayer is valid according to all, but the Hanafi position (sitting) is superior and relied upon for fatwa.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is which posture is preferred, not validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أومأ قاعداً وهو المستحب؛ لأنه أشبه بالسجود؛ لكون رأسه فيه أخفض وأقرب إلى الأرض، وهو المقصود، وقوله: "أوماً قاعداً" أولى من قولهم: "صلى قاعداً؛ إذ يفترض عليه أن يقوم، فإذا جاء أوان الركوع والسجود أومأ قاعداً، وإنما لم يلزمه القيام عند الإيماء للركوع والسجود؛ لأن المقصود من الصلاة الخضوع والخشوع، ويحصل ذلك بالركوع والسجود؛ لأن التواضع يوجد في الركوع ونهايته في السجود، والقيام وسيلة إلى السجود فيسقط بسقوطه، وقال زفر والشافعي يومئ قائماً؛ لأن القيام ركن فلا يسقط بالعجز عن أداء ركن آخر، ولنا: أن ركنية القيام ليتوسل به إلى السجدة؛ لما فيها من نهاية التعظيم، فإذا كان لا يعقبه السجود لا يكون ركنا، فالخلاف في الأفضلية وما قلناه أولى؛ لأن القعود أشبه بالسجود. (فتح، مستخلص)
He gestures while sitting, and that is recommended, because it more closely resembles prostration, due to his head being lower and closer to the ground, which is the objective. His saying: 'he gestures while sitting' is preferable to their saying: 'he prays sitting' since he is obligated to stand. Then when the time for bowing and prostration comes, he gestures while sitting. Standing is not required upon him when gesturing for bowing and prostration because the purpose of prayer is humility and submissiveness, and that is achieved by bowing and prostration. ... Zufar and al-Shafi'i say he gestures while standing because standing is a pillar and does not fall due to inability to perform another pillar. Our response: the pillar-status of standing is to serve as a means to prostration; if prostration does not follow, it is not a pillar. The dispute is about preference, and our view is more correct because sitting resembles prostration more.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on the preferred posture for gesturing in place of bowing and prostration. The Hanafi position is that one should sit and gesture, because this brings the head lower and closer to the ground, resembling the actual posture of prostration. The standing posture is not required when gesturing because the purpose of standing is to enable prostration; when prostration is substituted by gesture, the need for standing falls away. Zufar and al-Shafi'i argue that since standing is a pillar, it cannot be abandoned. The Hanafi response is that the pillar-status of standing is conditional upon being followed by actual prostration; without it, standing loses its obligatory character. Thus, the dispute is about optimality, and the Hanafi view is preferred because sitting is more similar to prostration.

Key Terms
القيام (al-qiyām): Standing in prayer; a pillar that is a means to prostration.
الاستحباب (al-istiḥbāb): Preferable or recommended, not obligatory.
الإيماء (al-īmā'): Gesturing with the head or body to indicate bowing or prostration when unable to perform them fully.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis recommend that the sick person gesture while sitting rather than standing?
A) Because sitting is more comfortable
B) Because standing is not a pillar for the sick
C) Because sitting makes the head lower, better resembling prostration
D) Because the hadith only mentions sitting

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that the means (standing) falls when the end (prostration) is impossible, making sitting the recommended posture for gesturing in prayer.

Completing Prayer When Illness Strikes Mid-Prayer
Ruling on continuing prayer when illness strikes during salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling when a person becomes ill during salah and explain why continuation is preferred over restarting.

Core Idea
Performing part of the prayer with actual movements and part with gestures is better than all gestures.

Imagine a person who starts the Fajr prayer in perfect health, but during the second rakʿah suddenly becomes dizzy and cannot bow. Should he continue with gestures or restart the entire prayer? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on this very question. Understanding the reasoning behind the relied-upon view will help you apply the principle of necessity in acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling from the text: the person completes the prayer according to his ability, using gestures if necessary, and even lying on his back if completely incapacitated.
This is the author's view, considered sounder.
2
Identify the opposing view
The minority view, narrated from Abu Hanifa via Abu Yusuf, holds that the prayer must be restarted. Understand their reasoning: the opening takbir (taḥrīmah) obligated actual bowing and prostration, and substitution is not permitted mid-prayer.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilāf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent argues that since the taḥrīmah created an obligation for actual rukūʿ and sujūd, these cannot be replaced by gestures. Any deviation would invalidate the original intention.
Their dalīl is based on the binding nature of the initial obligation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The author favours continuation because performing part of the prayer with actual movements and part with gestures is better than performing the entire prayer with gestures (if restarted). This is an application of the principle that when partial performance of an obligation is possible, it should be done rather than abandoning the entire act.
The response emphasises practicality and achieving more of the prescribed form.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under the mufta bihi view, the person finishes the current prayer quickly; under the minority view, he must restart and may miss the time or exert unnecessary effort.
This shows how the ruling affects real worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يتم بما قدر : بما قدر بحسب طاقته، فإن قدر على الركوع والسجود فعلهما، وإلا يؤمئ، فإن لم يقدر فيستلقى على الأصح، وقيل: يستأنف رمز الحقائق: ۹۰/۱] وروى أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة أنه يستقبل؛ لعدم جواز البناء؛ لأن تحريمته انعقدت موجبة للركوع والسجود، فلا يجوز بدونهما، ولهذا لزم الاستقبال، لكن قول المصنف: "يتم بما قدر" الأصح؛ لأن أداء بعض صلاته بركوع وسجود وبعضها بالإيماء أولى من أن يؤدى الكل بالإيماء. (فتح)
He completes it according to his ability: according to his capacity. If he can manage bowing and prostration, he does them; otherwise he gestures. If he is unable even to gesture, he lies on his back according to the soundest opinion. And it is said he starts over. Abu Yusuf narrated from Abu Hanifa that he should start over because continuation is not valid, since his opening takbir obligated bowing and prostration, so it is not permissible without them, thus restarting is necessary. But the author's statement "he completes it according to his ability" is sounder because performing part of his prayer with bowing and prostration and part with gesturing is better than performing the entire prayer with gesturing.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who becomes ill during prayer. The author states the relied-upon view (yatimmu bima qadar) that he continues with whatever he can manage: if he can bow and prostrate, he does so; if not, he gestures; if even that is impossible, he lies on his back. A contrary view is transmitted from Abu Hanifa via Abu Yusuf that he must start over, because the opening takbir obligated actual bowing and prostration which cannot be substituted mid-prayer. The author favors the first view because it is better to have some proper movements than all gestures. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that when partial performance of an obligation is possible, it should be done rather than abandoning the entire act.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-taḥrīmah): The opening takbir that renders the prayer initiated and prohibits outside actions.
البناء (al-binā’): Continuation of the prayer upon a foundation laid before, even if a change occurs.
الإيماء (al-īmā’): Gesturing with the head or body in place of actual bowing and prostration when one is unable to perform them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling when a person becomes ill during prayer and cannot bow or prostrate?
A) He must start the prayer all over
B) He completes the prayer with gestures
C) He abandons the prayer
D) He waits until he recovers

Key Takeaway
When illness strikes during prayer, the relied-upon Hanafi view is to complete the prayer with whatever ability remains, even if only gestures.

Building Prayer After Recovery: Gesturing vs Actual Bowing
Ruling on whether a recovered sick person builds or restarts prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a recovered sick person may continue (build) his prayer and when he must restart, applying the Hanafi principle that building strong upon weak is invalid.

Core Idea
Building strong upon weak is invalid: gesturing is too weak a base for actual bowing.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa’iq addresses a common scenario: a sick person begins prayer in a state of concession (sitting, gesturing) and then recovers the ability to bow and prostrate. The ruling depends on whether the earlier part involved actual bowing or mere gestures. Imam Abu Hanifa and his students distinguish between these two cases, and a minority opinion (Zufar) contests the rule. This lesson clarifies the principle and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage describes two cases: (1) the sick person prays sitting with actual ruku' and sujud, then recovers; (2) he gestures (mu'miyan), then recovers. Note the different rulings for each.
The key difference is whether the early part of prayer included actual physical movements (bowing, prostrating) or only head gestures.
2
Extract the ruling for each scenario
For case 1: he 'builds' (yabni) upon the prayer – continues. For case 2: he does not build but 'starts over by agreement' – must restart. Write down the two rulings.
The term 'by agreement' (ittifāqan) refers to the consensus among the three senior Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) against Zufar's view.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The reason given is 'building the strong upon the weak is not valid' (luzūm binā' al-qawī ‘alā al-ḍa‘īf). Actual bowing/prostration (strong) cannot be based on gestures (weak). The earlier part must be at least as 'strong' as the later part for continuation to be valid.
This is a qiyās khafī (subtle analogy) – the principle is derived from the prohibition of building the stronger on the weaker.
4
Analyze Zufar's objection and the Hanafi response
Zufar analogizes to the case of a gesturing imam being followed by a healthy follower who bows and prostrates. He argued that if that is permissible, then building should also be permissible. The Hanafi mashayikh reject the analogy because they do not permit following a gesturing imam for one who can bow – the premise is false.
This step shows how usul al-fiqh (specifically qiyās) is used to evaluate competing analogies.
5
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical
Given a scenario: A sick man begins 'Isha prayer by gesturing due to weakness, then after one rak'ah he recovers strength. According to the muftā bihi (operative) position, he must restart the entire prayer. Confirm the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
The difference matters: one must restart, which may affect the time of prayer or congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو صلى قاعداً يركع ويسجد فصح بنى، ولو كان مؤميا لا. ولو كان: أي المريض صلّى بعض صلاته. (ط) مؤمياً : ثم صح حتى قدر على الركوع. (ط) لا: أي لا يبنى بل يستأنف اتفاقاً للزوم بناء القوي على الضعيف، وقال زفر يبني بناء على اختلافهم في جواز الاقتداء بالمومي للراكع والساجد، فلا يجوز عند المشايخ ويجوز عند زفر. (فتح)
If he prayed sitting, bowing and prostrating, and then recovered, he builds upon it. But if he was gesturing (mu'miyan) and then recovered, he does not build. 'He was gesturing' meaning he prayed some of his prayer with gestures, then recovered and was able to bow and prostrate. 'No' meaning he does not build but rather starts over by agreement, because of the necessity of building the strong upon the weak. Zufar says he builds, based on their dispute regarding the permissibility of a mu'mi (gesturer) being followed by one who bows and prostrates; the mashayikh say it is not permissible, but Zufar permits it.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage rules on a sick person who prayed sitting with actual bowing and prostration, then recovers: he continues (yabni) on that prayer. However, if he was only gesturing (mu'miyan) due to inability, and then recovers the ability to bow and prostrate, he cannot continue; he must start over. The reason is that building a stronger state (actual bowing) upon a weaker state (gesturing) is not valid. Zufar disagrees and analogizes to the permissibility of a gesturing imam being followed by a praying follower who bows and prostrates. The Hanafi mashayikh reject this analogy, maintaining that the building is disallowed because the latter part of the prayer would be stronger than the former, which is impermissible.

Key Terms
البناء على الضعيف (al-binā’ ‘alā al-ḍa‘īf): Continuation of an act (prayer) upon a weaker foundation, which is invalid in Hanafi fiqh.
المؤمي (al-mu’mī): One who gestures with his head in place of bowing and prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a sick person begins prayer by gesturing (ima') and then recovers mid-prayer, what must he do?
A) Continue with the same prayer
B) Start the prayer over
C) He may choose
D) He must prostrate twice at the end

Key Takeaway
A recovered sick person may only continue (build) if his earlier prayer included actual ruku' and sujud; if he gestured, he must restart.

Leaning in Nafl Prayer
Ruling on leaning in nafl prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on leaning in nafl prayer and identify when it is permissible or disliked.

Core Idea
Leaning in nafl prayer is allowed only when tired; without excuse it is disliked.

In voluntary prayer, the Hanafi school permits relaxation of posture when needed. This lesson clarifies that a worshipper who becomes weary may lean on something or even sit without invalidating the prayer, while leaning without necessity is discouraged.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leaning (al-ittika') during voluntary (nafl) prayer. The ruling is permissible (ja'iz) when the person is tired.
The text uses 'matawwi‘' meaning the volunteer prayer offerer.
2
Analyze the condition for the concession
The condition is being tired (i'ya'). The text interprets 'i'ya' as exhaustion, which is a valid excuse. Without this excuse, leaning is disliked (makruh).
The word 'kariha' indicates it is makruh; the soundest opinion holds this.
3
Note the graded concession
If no object to lean on is available, the person should sit. This shows a progressive relaxation: first lean, then sit if needed.
The text does not specify that sitting is disliked; it is the logical alternative.
4
Determine the epistemological weight
The ruling is from the soundest opinion (al-sahih) within the Hanafi school, indicating it is a well-established view.
No major dispute is reported on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمتطوع أن يتكئ على شيء إن أعيى ولو صلى في فلك قاعداً بلا عذر صح. إن أعيي: أي تعب؛ لأنه عذر، فإن لم يجد شيئاً قعد، وكره الاتكاء بلا عذر في الصحيح. (ط،ع) بلا عذر : ولو مع القدرة على الخروج ويلزمه التوجه إلى القبلة عند افتتاح الصلاة وكلما دارت به السفينة؛ لأنها في حقه كالبيت ولا تجوز الصلاة فيها بالإيماء اتفاقاً. (ط، ع) صح: عند أبي حنيفة وقالا: لا يجوز إلا من عذر؛ لأن القيام ركن فلا يترك إلا من عذر وله أن الغالب دوران الرأس فصار كالمتحقق، والأولى أن يخرج استطاع الخروج منها، والخلاف في غير المربوطة، ولو كانت مربوطة لم يجز إجماعاً، وقيل: يجوز عنده في حالتي الإجراء والإرساء، فإن كانت موثقة بالبحر في لجة البحر وهي تضطرب قيل: يحتمل وجهين، والأصح إن كان الريح يحركها تحريكا شديداً . کالسائرة، وإن حركها قليلاً فهي كالواقفة. (عيني، مسكين)
It is permissible for the volunteer prayer offerer to lean on something if he is tired. If he prays in a ship sitting without excuse, it is valid. 'If tired' meaning he is exhausted; because it is an excuse. If he finds nothing to lean on, he sits. Leaning without an excuse is disliked according to the soundest opinion. 'Without excuse' even if he is able to go out (of the ship); he is obligated to face the qibla at the beginning of prayer and every time the ship turns, because for him it is like a house. It is not permissible to pray in a ship by gesture (ima') by agreement. 'Valid' according to Abu Hanifa; the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is not permissible except for an excuse, because standing is a pillar and cannot be abandoned except for an excuse. He argues that dizziness is generally prevalent and thus is considered certain. It is better to leave the ship if one is able. The dispute is about a ship that is not tied. If the ship is tied, it is not permissible by consensus. ... If it is anchored in the open sea and swaying, there are two views; the soundest is that if the wind moves it strongly, it is like a moving ship; if it moves it slightly, it is like a stationary one.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings: (1) A volunteer (mutatawwi') may lean on something during prayer if he becomes tired. This is an excuse; leaning without excuse is disliked. (2) Praying in a ship while sitting without an excuse: Abu Hanifa rules it valid, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require an excuse because standing is a pillar. The reasoning for Abu Hanifa's view is that dizziness (dawaran al-ra's) is a common occurrence and thus treated as a virtual excuse. The text also discusses the obligation to face qibla in a moving ship and the impermissibility of gesturing in a ship by agreement. The details about anchored vs. moving ships provide further nuance.

Key Terms
المتطوع (al-mutaṭawwi‘): One who performs voluntary (nafl) prayer.
أعيى (a‘yā): He became tired/exhausted.
الاتكاء (al-ittikā’): Leaning or supporting oneself on something.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the soundest opinion in the Hanafi school, leaning in nafl prayer without an excuse is:
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Leaning in nafl prayer is a concession for tiredness; without excuse it is disliked but not invalid.

Praying Sitting in a Ship
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting prayer in a ship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on praying sitting in a ship and state the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits sitting without an excuse; the Sahibayn require an excuse.

When praying on a ship, maintaining the standing posture may be difficult due to motion or dizziness. The Hanafi school has an internal difference: Abu Hanifa considers dizziness a prevalent occurrence that serves as a virtual excuse, while his two main students insist on an actual excuse. This lesson unpacks their arguments and the practical implications for the traveller.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa rules that praying sitting in a ship without an excuse is valid (صح).
The text says 'sahh' indicating validity.
2
Identify the opponent within the Hanafi school
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Sahibayn) hold that it is not permissible except with an excuse.
They argue that standing is a pillar (rukn) and cannot be abandoned without genuine necessity.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Their proof: standing is a rukn for prayer, so it can only be omitted due to an actual excuse (like fear or illness).
This is based on the general rule that arkan are obligatory.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa argues that dizziness (dawaran al-ra's) is prevalent in ships, so it is treated as a virtual certainty (ka al-muhaqqiq).
Thus, the excuse is considered present even if not overtly expressed.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practical difference: A person can pray sitting without concern under Abu Hanifa's view; under the Sahibayn's view he must strive to stand or seek an excuse. The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's, but it is better to leave the ship if possible.
The text also discusses tied ships and anchored ships, further nuancing the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمتطوع أن يتكئ على شيء إن أعيى ولو صلى في فلك قاعداً بلا عذر صح. إن أعيي: أي تعب؛ لأنه عذر، فإن لم يجد شيئاً قعد، وكره الاتكاء بلا عذر في الصحيح. (ط،ع) بلا عذر : ولو مع القدرة على الخروج ويلزمه التوجه إلى القبلة عند افتتاح الصلاة وكلما دارت به السفينة؛ لأنها في حقه كالبيت ولا تجوز الصلاة فيها بالإيماء اتفاقاً. (عيني، مسكين)
It is permissible for the volunteer prayer offerer to lean on something if he is tired. If he prays in a ship sitting without excuse, it is valid. 'If tired' meaning he is exhausted; because it is an excuse. If he finds nothing to lean on, he sits. Leaning without an excuse is disliked according to the soundest opinion. 'Without excuse' even if he is able to go out (of the ship); he is obligated to face the qibla at the beginning of prayer and every time the ship turns, because for him it is like a house. It is not permissible to pray in a ship by gesture (ima') by agreement. 'Valid' according to Abu Hanifa; the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is not permissible except for an excuse, because standing is a pillar and cannot be abandoned except for an excuse. He argues that dizziness is generally prevalent and thus is considered certain. It is better to leave the ship if one is able. The dispute is about a ship that is not tied. If the ship is tied, it is not permissible by consensus. ... If it is anchored in the open sea and swaying, there are two views; the soundest is that if the wind moves it strongly, it is like a moving ship; if it moves it slightly, it is like a stationary one.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings: (1) A volunteer (mutatawwi') may lean on something during prayer if he becomes tired. This is an excuse; leaning without excuse is disliked. (2) Praying in a ship while sitting without an excuse: Abu Hanifa rules it valid, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require an excuse because standing is a pillar. The reasoning for Abu Hanifa's view is that dizziness (dawaran al-ra's) is a common occurrence and thus treated as a virtual excuse. The text also discusses the obligation to face qibla in a moving ship and the impermissibility of gesturing in a ship by agreement. The details about anchored vs. moving ships provide further nuance.

Key Terms
الفلك (al-fulk): A ship or vessel.
الإيماء (al-īmā’): Gesturing with the head or eyes instead of actual physical movements in prayer.
الغالب دوران الرأس (al-ghālib dawarān al-ra’s): The prevalent occurrence of dizziness (vertigo).

C) Only if the ship is moving fast.

Abu Hanifa permits sitting in a ship without excuse due to prevalent dizziness, and this is the operative ruling, though standing is better.
