Qada' for Fainted or Insane Persons: The Five-Prayer Limit
Ruling on making up missed prayers due to fainting or insanity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for making up missed prayers due to fainting or insanity, explain the five-prayer limit, and distinguish the positions of the Sahibayn and Muhammad on building during prayer.

Core Idea
If you faint or go insane for five prayers or less, make them up; if more, none — based on Companion practice.

This lesson examines the Hanafi school's unique ruling on qada' for periods of unconsciousness. Unlike the Shafi'i school, which exempts all missed prayers during unconsciousness, the Hanafis distinguish based on duration and cause. We will explore the textual evidence, the intra-Hanafi disagreement on building during prayer, and the implications of sinful vs. heavenly affliction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is missing prayers due to fainting or insanity. The Hanafi ruling: qada' is wajib for up to five prayers; if more than five, no qada' at all.
The 'five prayers' refers to the number of prayer times missed, not necessarily five individual prayers.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The evidence is the actions of the Companions: ‘Ali fainted for four prayers and made them up; Ibn ‘Umar fainted for more than a day and night and did not make up any.
This establishes the threshold.
3
Understand the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that no qada' is required if one misses a complete prayer time while unconscious, reasoning that unconsciousness removes the obligation entirely.
The Hanafi response: the Companion practice shows a distinction, and the limit of five is established.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on building during prayer
If one faints during prayer, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that building is allowed; Muhammad (al-Shaybani) requires starting over. The analogy: building is like following an imam.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's view.
5
Consider the cause of unconsciousness
Abu Hanifa: if the fainting is due to sin (e.g., wine), qada' is required even if prolonged. Muhammad: if the substance is permissible (e.g., certain drugs), it is excused like illness.
This distinction applies to the five-prayer limit: heavenly affliction triggers the limit; sinful cause does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أغمي عليه أو جن خمس صلوات قضى ولو أكثر لا. أي سلب عقله بقدر أو دونها إذا أفاق أي صار عقله مغلوبا بنى عندهما، وقال محمد يستقبل، والأصل أن بناء آخر الصلاة على أولها بمنزلة صلاة المقتدي على صلاة الإمام، فكل موضع يصح الاقتداء صح البناء، وما لا فلا، واقتداء القائم بالقاعد صحيح عندهما بناء على فعل في الإمامة، وعند محمد لا يجوز؛ لأن حالة المقتدي أقوى من حالة الإمام. (فتح، مستخلص) ومن أغمي عليه قيد بالإغماء؛ لأنه لو زال عقله بالخمر يلزمه القضاء وإن طال؛ لأنه حصل بما . يوجب التخفيف؛ ولهذا يقع طلاقه، وكذا إذا زال بالبنج أو الداء عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن سقوط القضاء عرف بالأثر إذا حصل بآفة سماوية، فلا يقاس عليه ما حصل بفعل، وعند محمد يسقط؛ لأنه مباح، فصار كالمرض، وأطلق في الإغماء فعم ما لو حصل بفزع من سبع أو آدمي؛ لأن الخوف بسبب ضعف قلبه وهو مرض، وقال الشافعي: لا يقضي إذا أغمي عليه أو جن في وقت صلاة كامل، ولنا ما روي أن علياً له أغمى عليه أربع صلوات فقضاهن وابن عمر لما أغمي عليه أكثر من يوم وليلة فلم يقض. (فتح، عيني) ولو أكثر لا: أي لو زاد الإغماء أو الجنون أكثر من الخمس لا يقضي مطلقاً سواء كان بالساعات أو بالأوقات وعند محمد: إن كثر بالأوقات بأن تفوته السادسة أيضاً لا يقضي فلو جن قبل الزوال ودام إلى ما بعد الزوال من اليوم الثاني، وأفاق قبل دخول وقت العصر لم يقض عندهما؛ لأنه من حيث الساعات أكثر من يوم وليلة، وعند محمد: يقضي ما لم يمتد إلى وقت العصر حتى يصير الصلوات ستاً. (عيني، مسكين)
Whoever faints or becomes insane (for) five prayers makes them up, but if more, he does not. That is, if his mind is taken away for a day or less, upon recovery he makes them up; if more than that, he does not. ... They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that he builds upon his prayer (if faints during prayer), and Muhammad says he starts over. The principle is that building the latter part of prayer upon the former is like the prayer of a follower upon the prayer of an imam: wherever following is valid, building is valid; where not, not. ... Regarding fainting: the cause is considered; if it occurs by wine, he must make up even if prolonged, because it is sinful; similar for narcotics or disease according to Abu Hanifa. Al-Shafi'i says he does not make up if he faints during a complete prayer time. Our evidence: it is narrated that ‘Ali fainted for four prayers and made them up, and Ibn ‘Umar fainted for more than a day and night and did not make up. 'If more' meaning if the fainting or insanity exceeds five prayers, he does not make up absolutely, whether measured in hours or times. According to Muhammad: if it exceeds in times (i.e., the sixth is also missed), then he does not make up gradually.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute about qada' for periods of unconsciousness. The primary rule: if fainting or insanity lasts for five prayers or less, one must make them up; if more than five, no qada' is required. The text also discusses the case of fainting during prayer: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that one can build upon the prayer when consciousness returns, while Muhammad (al-Shaybani) says one must start over, using the analogy of a follower following an imam. Regarding the cause of fainting: if caused by sin (like wine), Abu Hanifa says qada' is required even if long; Muhammad says it is excused if the substance is permissible. The Shafi'i position is that no qada' is required if one misses a complete prayer time while unconscious. Hanafi evidence includes the actions of ‘Ali and Ibn ‘Umar. The ruling also distinguishes between measuring by hours or by prayer times: the majority say if the period exceeds the time of five prayers (i.e., the sixth is also missed), then no qada' at all.

Key Terms
الإغماء (al-ighmā’): Fainting or unconsciousness; a state that may affect the obligation of prayer.
الجنون (al-junūn): Insanity; similar ruling to fainting in terms of qada' limit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All of them, regardless of duration
B) Only one prayer
C) Up to five prayers; if more, none
D) None, if it was due to illness

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits qada' for fainting/insanity to five prayers, based on Companion practice; beyond that, no qada', and the cause matters.

Building Prayer of a Sick Person upon Recovery
Ruling on building prayer after recovery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building prayer after recovery from illness and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar regarding gestures.

Core Idea
Building upon weak gestures is invalid; only actual bowing and prostrating allow continuation.

This lesson examines a specific case in the prayer of the sick: if a person begins prayer while too weak to bow and prostrate, using gestures instead, then recovers mid-prayer, can he continue from where he left off? The Hanafi school has a clear ruling, but a lesser-known intra-madhhab disagreement provides an opportunity to understand the principle of building upon valid acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between a sick person who prays sitting and actually bows and prostrates, versus one who only gestures with the head.
The ruling depends on the initial action.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
If the person performed actual bowing and prostration, he may build upon that prayer. If he only gestured, building is not allowed; he must restart.
The matn explicitly says 'and if he was gesturing, no'.
3
Understand the proof: building strong upon weak
The Hanafi position is based on the principle that one cannot build strong actions (actual bowing) upon weak ones (gestures). The gestures are a deficient substitute and cannot support the full effort.
This is a qawida (legal maxim).
4
Analyze Zufar's opposing qiyas and the Hanafi response
Zufar analogizes to the case of a gesturing follower behind an imam who bows and prostrates, which is valid. The Hanafi response rejects the analogy because the imam's strength does not transfer to the follower's deficit.
The mashayikh (majority) uphold the consensus and Zufar's view is not followed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة المريض ولو صلى قاعداً يركع ويسجد فصح بنى، ولو كان مؤميا لا ولو كان: أي المريض صلّى بعض صلاته. (ط) مؤمياً : ثم صح حتى قدر على الركوع. (ط) لا: أي لا يبنى بل يستأنف اتفاقاً للزوم بناء القوي على الضعيف، وقال زفر يبني بناء على اختلافهم في جواز الاقتداء بالمومي للراكع والساجد، فلا يجوز عند المشايخ ويجوز عند زفر. (فتح)
Chapter of the prayer of the sick. If he prayed sitting, then bowed and prostrated and recovered (from illness), he builds (on his prayer). And if he was gesturing, no (he does not build). And if he was: meaning the sick person prayed part of his prayer. (T) Gesturing: then he recovered and was able to bow. (T) No: meaning he does not build but starts anew by agreement because it would require building the strong upon the weak. Zufar said he builds based on their disagreement regarding the permissibility of a gesturing person being followed by one who bows and prostrates; according to the mashayikh it is not permissible, but Zufar allows it. (Fath)
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on the prayer of the sick. It addresses whether a sick person who begins prayer in a seated position and then recovers enough to perform actual bowing and prostration can build upon the already performed parts of the prayer. The matn states that if he was actually bowing and prostrating (i.e., performing the full motions), he builds; but if he was only gesturing with his head, he does not build. The commentary explains that the consensus (ittifaqan) is that he must start anew because building strong actions upon weak gestures is invalid. Zufar dissents, analogizing to the case where a gesturing follower may be led by an imam who bows and prostrates. However, the majority of mashayikh reject this analogy, establishing the mufta bihi as the consensus view.

Key Terms
مؤمياً (muʾmiyan): Gesturing with the head to indicate bowing and prostration when too weak to perform actual motions.
بناء (bināʾ): Continuing the prayer from the point where one left off, without repeating the earlier parts, after a recovery of ability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Build upon his prayer.
B) Start the prayer anew.
C) Continue but repeat the previous rakʿah.
D) It is invalid regardless.

Key Takeaway
A sick person who gestures with his head cannot build upon that prayer upon recovery; he must restart the prayer entirely.

Leaning and Praying in a Ship
Rulings on a sick person leaning in voluntary prayer and on praying in a ship without excuse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying sitting in a ship and explain the talil (reasoning) of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The constant dizziness from ship motion is an effective excuse, making sitting valid per Abu Hanifa.

This passage presents two rulings: first, a sick person may lean on something during voluntary prayer if fatigued; second, regarding prayer in a ship, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Hanifa holds that sitting without a separate excuse is valid because the ship's motion causes prevailing dizziness, which constitutes an excuse. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) maintain that standing is a rukn and cannot be omitted without a genuine excuse. The commentary clarifies the distinction between a tied and moving ship, and the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the passage
First, the ruling on leaning during nafl prayer for a sick person who becomes tired. The passage allows it and deems it disliked without excuse. Second, the ruling on praying sitting in a ship without a specific excuse.
The passage explicitly says 'valid' (صح) according to Abu Hanifa.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on ship prayer
Abu Hanifa rules that sitting without a separate excuse is valid because the prevailing dizziness from the ship's motion is considered a verified excuse. The Sahibayn disagree, arguing that standing is a rukn and cannot be omitted without a clear excuse.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Extract the proof for each position
Sahibayn's proof: standing is a rukn, so it cannot be left except for genuine excuse. Abu Hanifa's proof: the constant dizziness (ghalab al-dawar) is effectively a verified excuse, so the rule of rukn is relaxed.
Abu Hanifa's talil relies on the pervasive nature of sea-sickness.
4
Understand the talil for Abu Hanifa's view
The commentary explains that dizziness is the norm (ghalib) for people on a ship; thus it is treated as a confirmed excuse, making sitting permissible even without additional hardship.
This is the basis for the mufta bihi position.
5
Apply the distinction between tied and moving ship
If the ship is tied (marbutah) and stationary, consensus requires standing; sitting is invalid. If the ship is moving or violently rocking, it is treated as moving; if only slight motion, it may be like stationary.
The commentary mentions this differentiation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمتطوع أن يتكئ المريض بعض صلاته من المرض في أثناء صلاته بالنوافل على شيء إن أعيى ولو صلى في فلك قاعداً بلا عذر صح إن أعبي: أي تعب؛ لأنه عذر، فإن لم يجد شيئاً قعد، وكره الاتكاء بلا عذر في الصحيح. (ط،ع) إن بلا عذر : ولو مع القدرة على الخروج ويلزمه التوجه إلى القبلة عند افتتاح الصلاة وكلما دارت به السفينة؛ لأنها في حقه كالبيت ولا تجوز الصلاة فيها بالإيماء اتفاقاً. And for the one performing voluntary (prayer), the sick person may lean during part of his prayer due to illness, while praying nafl, on something if he becomes fatigued. And if he prayed in a ship sitting without excuse, it is valid. (Commentary: 'If he becomes fatigued' means tired, because it is an excuse; if he finds nothing (to lean on), he sits, and it is disliked to lean without excuse in the correct view. (T, A) 'Without excuse' (in ship): and even if he is able to go out, he must face the qibla at the start of the prayer and whenever the ship turns, because it is like a house for him; and it is not permitted to pray with gestures (i.e., sitting) in it by agreement. (T, A) 'Valid': according to Abu Hanifa, but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is not valid except with excuse, because standing is a pillar and should not be omitted without excuse. He (Abu Hanifa) argues that the prevailing dizziness becomes like a verified excuse. It is better for him to go out if he can. The disagreement is concerning a ship that is not tied; if it is tied, it is not permissible by consensus. It is said that according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is permissible in both the sailing and anchored states. If it is moored in the deep sea and it rocks, it is said there are two possibilities: the most correct is that if the wind moves it violently, it is like a moving ship; if it moves it slightly, it is like stationary. (Ayni, Miskin))
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings. First, for voluntary (nafl) prayers, a sick person may lean on something if he becomes tired; leaning without excuse is disliked. Second, regarding praying in a ship: Abu Hanifa rules that sitting (i.e., not standing) without an excuse is valid because the constant dizziness from the ship's motion constitutes an effective excuse. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree, insisting that standing is a pillar and cannot be omitted except for a genuine excuse. The commentary further distinguishes between a tied ship (where consensus prohibits sitting without excuse) and an unmoored ship. For a ship that rocks violently due to strong wind, it is treated like a moving one; if only slightly, it is like stationary, and the ruling may differ. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
مربوطة (marbūṭah): A ship that is tied to the shore or anchored (not freely moving).
إيماء (īmāʾ): Gesturing with the head or body to indicate bowing and prostration, used by the sick or those on a ship when unable to perform full motions.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, praying sitting on a moving ship is valid without a separate excuse because the prevailing dizziness is an effective excuse, per Abu Hanifa's mufta bihi view.

Making Up Prayers After Unconsciousness or Insanity
Ruling on qada' for prayers missed due to unconsciousness or insanity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada' for prayers missed due to unconsciousness or insanity, distinguish between natural and self-induced causes, and apply the five-prayer limit.

Core Idea
Missed prayers due to natural unconsciousness: qada' for up to five; beyond that, no qada'.

When a person loses consciousness or becomes insane, the obligation to pray is suspended. But once they regain reason, do they have to make up the missed prayers? The Hanafi school addresses this with a detailed ruling that balances the nature of the cause and the duration of the loss. This lesson unpacks the textual ruling and its proofs, including the companion-based evidence that establishes the five-prayer limit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making up (qada') missed prayers after unconsciousness or insanity. The matn states: if five prayers are missed, they are made up; if more, not. This is a composite ruling with conditions.
The ruling differs based on cause (natural vs. self-induced) and duration (up to five prayers vs. more).
2
Locate the dalil
The Hanafi proof is an athar (companion practice): ‘Ali made up four prayers after unconsciousness; Ibn ‘Umar did not make up after more than a day and night. This dalil is naqli (textual).
The commentary cites Fath and ‘Ayni as sources.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The athar shows that the companions treated the limit of five as a boundary. ‘Ali made up four (≤5), Ibn ‘Umar missed more than a day and night (which includes at least 6 prayers) and did not make up. This demonstrates that qada' is required up to five prayers, but not beyond.
The limit is based on the number of prayer times, not hours.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi‘i holds that if unconsciousness covers a complete prayer time, no qada' is required at all, regardless of number. There is also an intra-Hanafi difference: Muhammad considers prayer times, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's own earlier view?) consider hours for the limit.
Shafi'i's proof is the general principle that obligations are lifted for those without reason.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position relies on companion practice, which is a strong source (qawl sahabi). The Shafi'i position is overridden by this specific evidence. The mufta bihi is the standard Hanafi view: qada' for up to five prayers from natural causes; always for self-induced causes.
The commentary emphasises that the five-prayer limit is absolute, not dependent on hours.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أغمي عليه أو جن خمس صلوات قضى ولو أكثر لا. ومن أغمي عليه قيد بالإغماء؛ لأنه لو زال عقله بالخمر يلزمه القضاء وإن طال؛ لأنه حصل بما . يوجب التخفيف؛ ولهذا يقع طلاقه، وكذا إذا زال بالبنج أو الداء عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن سقوط القضاء عرف بالأثر إذا حصل بآفة سماوية، فلا يقاس عليه ما حصل بفعله، وعند محمد يسقط؛ لأنه مباح، فصار كالمرض، وأطلق في الإغماء فعم ما لو حصل بفزع من سبع أو آدمي؛ لأن الخوف بسبب ضعف قلبه وهو مرض، وقال الشافعي: لا يقضي إذا أغمي عليه أو جن في وقت صلاة كامل، ولنا ما روي أن علياً له أغمي عليه أربع صلوات فقضاهن وابن عمر لما أغمي عليه أكثر من يوم وليلة فلم يقض. (فتح، عيني) ولو أكثر لا: أي لو زاد الإغماء أو الجنون أكثر من الخمس لا يقضي مطلقاً سواء كان بالساعات أو بالأوقات وعند محمد: إن كثر بالأوقات بأن تفوته السادسة أيضاً لا يقضي فلو جن قبل الزوال ودام إلى ما بعد الزوال من اليوم الثاني، وأفاق قبل دخول وقت العصر لم يقض عندهما؛ لأنه من حيث الساعات أكثر من يوم وليلة، وعند محمد: يقضي ما لم يمتد إلى وقت العصر حتى يصير الصلوات ستاً. (عيني، مسكين) عندهما،
And if someone becomes unconscious or insane: (if he misses) five prayers, he makes them up; if more, no. (Commentary) And if someone becomes unconscious: it is restricted to unconsciousness; because if his reason goes due to wine, qada is obligatory even if long, because it occurs due to something that obligates leniency (i.e., sin). For this reason his divorce occurs. Similarly, if it goes due to an anesthetic (banj) or illness according to Abu Hanifa; because the dropping of qada is known by precedent only when it occurs due to a heavenly affliction (āfah samāwiyyah), so what occurs by his own action is not analogized to it. According to Muhammad, qada is dropped because it (the anesthetic) is permissible, so it becomes like illness. And unconsciousness is unrestricted, so it includes if it occurs due to fright from a wild beast or a person, because fear due to weakness of heart is illness. And al-Shafi‘i said: He does not make up if he becomes unconscious or insane during a complete prayer time. And our proof is what was related that ‘Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) once became unconscious missing four prayers, and he made them up; and Ibn ‘Umar when he became unconscious for more than a day and night, he did not make up. (Fath, ‘Ayni) And 'if more, no' means if the unconsciousness or insanity exceeds five, he does not make up absolutely, whether measured by hours or by prayer times. According to Muhammad, if it is numerous by prayer times such that he also misses the sixth, he does not make up. So if he becomes insane before noon and it continues until after noon of the next day, and he recovers before the time of ‘Asr enters, according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he does not make up because by hours it is more than a day and night. According to Muhammad, he makes up as long as it has not extended to the time of ‘Asr such that the prayers become six. (‘Ayni, Miskin) According to them (the two).
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage deals with the obligation of making up missed prayers due to unconsciousness or insanity. The matn states that if the condition lasts for five prayers or less, they are made up; if more than five, no qada' is required. The commentary expands on exceptions: if the loss of reason is caused by sin (like alcohol), qada is required even if prolonged, because the default leniency for natural causes does not apply. If caused by a permissible substance like anesthetic (bangi), Abu Hanifa says qada is still required (since it is self-induced), while Muhammad says it is waived because the substance is permissible. For natural causes (fright, illness), qada is waived after five prayers. The Hanafi proof is from the actions of Ali and Ibn Umar. There is also a dispute with Shafi'i, who says no qada if unconsciousness covers an entire prayer time. The Hanafi response is the athar of Ali making up four prayers. The commentary also details the calculation regarding time periods: the two (Sahibayn) consider hours, while Muhammad considers prayer times. The mufta bihi is that if the number of prayers missed is five or fewer, qada is required; if six or more, it is not.

Key Terms
إغماء (ighmāʾ): Unconsciousness caused by natural illness or fright, not self-induced.
آفة سماوية (āfah samāwiyyah): A calamity from heaven, i.e., a natural or divinely sent cause beyond human control.
قضاء (qadāʾ): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person becomes unconscious due to a natural illness and misses exactly five prayers, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) He must make up all five prayers.
B) He must make up none because the time was lost.
C) He must make up only three of them.
D) He must make up only if he missed a fard prayer.

Key Takeaway
For natural unconsciousness or insanity, the Hanafi school requires making up prayers only if five or fewer are missed; for self-induced loss, all missed prayers must be made up.

Obligation of Sajdat al-Tilawah and the Disputed Verses
Inter-madhhab dispute on obligation and list of verses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdat al-tilawah (wajib upon 14 verses), explain the Hanafi proofs, and evaluate the responses to Shafi'i and Maliki objections.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah is wajib on 14 verses; the preposition 'ala in the hadith proves obligation, and Quranic commands confirm it.

In this lesson, we examine the chapter on prostration of recitation from a Hanafi matn. The passage asserts the obligation (wujub) of sajdat al-tilawah upon reciting or hearing any of 14 specific Quranic verses. It then addresses two major inter-madhhab disputes: first with Imam al-Shafi'i, who considers it only a stressed sunnah, and second with Imam Malik, who excludes the mufassal chapters. The commentary provides the Hanafi proofs and rebuttals.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that sajdat al-tilawah is wajib (obligatory) upon reciting or hearing any of the fourteen specific verses. The obligation applies to both the reciter and the listener, even if the listener did not intend to hear.
2
Identify the fourteen verses
The text lists the following surahs and verses: the first prostration verse in Surah al-Hajj, and the verses in Surah Sad, al-A'raf, al-Ra'd, al-Nahl, al-Isra', Maryam, al-Furqan, al-Naml, al-Sajdah (Alif Lam Mim Tanzil), Fussilat (Ha Mim al-Sajdah), al-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and al-Alaq (Iqra'). Memorizing this list is essential for practice.
Surah al-Hajj has a dispute; the Hanafi position is that only the first verse is for tilawah, the second is for prayer.
3
Understand the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school adduces three categories of proof from the Quranic verses themselves: explicit commands (imposing obligation), actions of prophets (obligation to follow), and disdain of disbelievers (obligation to oppose). Additionally, the hadith 'السجدة على من سمعها وعلى من تلاها' uses the preposition 'ala which in legal language indicates obligation (wujub).
The word 'ala is a key indicator of wujub in Hanafi usul.
4
Analyse the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that sajdat al-tilawah is only sunnah mu'akkadah, citing that the Prophet sometimes recited these verses without prostrating. The Hanafi response interprets this as evidence that it is not immediate (wajib 'ala al-fawr), not that it is non-obligatory. Moreover, explicit commands and the hadith support obligation.
The Hanafi response distinguishes between immediate and delayed obligation.
5
Analyse the Maliki objection and Hanafi response
Imam Malik excludes the verses in the Mufassal (specifically al-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and al-Alaq) from prostration. The Hanafi school includes them, relying on the general evidence and the absence of a valid exclusion.
The practical consequence affects which verses require prostration for followers of each school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجدة التلاوة باب سجدة التلاوة هذا باب في أحكامها . يجب بأربع عشرة آية، منها: أولى الحج و'ص' على من تلا ولو إماماً وسمع بتلاوتها فيكون الباء للسببية أي من أربع عشرة ولو غير قاصد. أي السامع أما ثانيتها فصلواتية شر كان باب سجدة التلاوة : [ أي مصدر من تلا يتلو بمعنى قرأ. (ع)] المناسبة بينهما أن في سجدة التلاوة سقط بعض الأركان كما يسقط في صلاة المريض، وفي ذكر التلاوة إيماء إلى أنه لو كتبها أو تهجاها لم يجب، وركنه وضع الجبهة على الأرض أو الركوع أو ما يقوم مقامها من الإيماء للمريض أو التالي على الدابة وشروطها شروط الصلاة إلا التحريمة، ونية التعيين والتلاوة سبب بالإجماع، ولهذا أضيف إليها، والسماع . ط لعمل التلاوة في حق السامعين، وعند البعض هو السبب في حقهم؛ لقول الصحابة : السجدة على من تلاها وعلى من سمعها، والأول أصح. (فتح) يجب أي عندنا، خلافاً للشافعي؛ فإنها عنده سنة مؤكدة؛ لأنه عليها قرأها و لم يسجد لها، ولنا: أن آياتها كلها تدل على الوجوب؛ لأنها على ثلاثة أقسام قسم أمر صريح، وهو الوجوب، وقسم ذكر فيه فعل الأنبياء، والاقتداء بهم واجب، وقسم ذكر فيه استنكاف الكفار ومخالفتهم واجبة وتأويل ما رواه أنه لم يسجد للحال، وليس فيه دليل على عدم الوجوب؛ إذ هي لا تجب على الفور، وورد عنه عليها أنه قال: 'السجدة على من سمعها وعلى من تلاها'، وكلمة 'على' للوجوب رمز الحقائق: ۹۱/۱] (فتح) أولى الحج: وقال الشافعي: في سورة الحج سجدتان؛ لحديث عقبة بن عامر، قال: قلت: يا رسول الله، أفضلت سورة الحج بأن فيها سجدتين؟ قال: 'نعم، ومن لم يسجد هما لم يقرأ هما'، ولنا ما روي عن ابن عباس وابن عمر له أنهما قالا: سجدة التلاوة في الحج هي الأولى، والثانية سجدة الصلاة، وقرانها بالركوع يؤيد ما روي عنهما، وما رواه الشافعي لم يثبت، وذكر ضعفه في الغاية، ولئن ثبت فالمراد بأحدهما سجدة التلاوة، وبالأخرى سجدة الصلاة. (عيني) وص والأعراف والرعد، والنحل، والإسراء، ومريم والفرقان، والنمل، و'الــــم' تنزيل، و'حم' السجدة والنجم، وانشقت واقرأ . (ط)] وقال الشافعي: لا سجدة فيها، بل هي سجدة الشكر؛ لما روي عن ابن عباس أنه عليها سجد 'ص'، وقال: 'سجدها داود توبة ونحن نسجدها شكراً'، ولنا: ما روي عنه عن النبي له أنه سجد في 'ص'، وما رواه ضعفه البيهقي، والمراد به لأجل الشكر، وهو لا ينافي الوجوب، وقال مالك: لا سجود في المفصل أي في سورة النجم والانشقاق والعلق. [رمز الحقائق: ۹۱/۱]
Chapter of the prostration of recitation: this is a chapter concerning its rulings. It is obligatory for fourteen verses, among them: the first (verse) of Surah al-Hajj and Surah Sad, upon the one who recites, even if an imam, and upon the one who hears it recited. So the 'ba' in 'bi-arba' 'ashrata' is causative, i.e., because of fourteen. And even if the hearer did not intend (to hear). As for the second (prostration verse in Hajj), it is for prayer, (it is) evil? (Slightly corrupted). The chapter: (commentary) It is a verbal noun from tala-yatlu meaning to recite. (A) The connection between them (this chapter and the previous) is that in sajdat al-tilawa some of the pillars are dropped just as they are dropped in the prayer of the sick. And mentioning tilawa indicates that if one writes it or spells it out, it is not obligatory. Its pillar is placing the forehead on the ground, or bowing, or what stands in its place of gesture for the sick or the reciter on a mount. Its conditions are the conditions of prayer except for takbirat al-ihram and the intention of specification. Recitation is the cause by consensus, and for this it is attributed to it. And hearing is considered part of the action of recitation regarding the hearers. According to some, it is the cause for them due to the saying of the Companions: 'The prostration is upon the one who recites it and upon the one who hears it.' The first (view) is more correct. (Fath) 'Is obligatory' means according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, for according to him it is a stressed sunnah, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited them and did not prostrate. Our proof is that all its verses indicate obligation; they are of three types: a type containing an explicit command, which is obligation; a type mentioning the actions of prophets, and following them is obligatory; and a type mentioning the disdain of disbelievers, and opposing them is obligatory. The interpretation of what he (Shafi'i) narrated that he (the Prophet) did not prostrate at that moment does not prove non-obligation, because it is not obligatory immediately. And it is related from him (peace be upon him) that he said: 'The prostration is upon the one who hears it and upon the one who recites it,' and the word 'upon' indicates obligation. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq 1/91) (Fath) 'The first of al-Hajj': al-Shafi'i said: In Surah al-Hajj there are two prostrations, due to the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir who said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, has Surah al-Hajj been favored with two prostrations? He said: 'Yes, and whoever does not prostrate for them has not recited them.' Our proof is what is related from Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) that they said: The prostration of recitation in al-Hajj is the first, and the second is the prostration of prayer. And its conjunction with ruku' supports what is related from them. And what al-Shafi'i related is not established; its weakness is mentioned in al-Ghayah. And even if it were established, the meaning is that one of them is the prostration of recitation, and the other is the prostration of prayer. (Ayni) And (the verses are in) Sad, al-A'raf, al-Ra'd, al-Nahl, al-Isra', Maryam, al-Furqan, al-Naml, Alif Lam Mim Tanzil (al-Sajdah), Ha Mim al-Sajdah (Fussilat), al-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and Iqra' (al-'Alaq). (T) And al-Shafi'i said: There is no prostration in it (Surah Sad), rather it is a prostration of thanks, due to what is related from Ibn 'Abbas that he prostrated upon (reciting) Sad and said, 'David prostrated it as repentance, and we prostrate it as thanks.' Our proof is what is related from him (the Prophet) that he prostrated in Sad. What he (Shafi'i) related is weak according to al-Bayhaqi. And the meaning is for thanks, which does not negate obligation. And Malik said: There is no prostration in the Mufassal, i.e., in Surah al-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and al-'Alaq. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq 1/91)
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on sajdat al-tilawa and establishes its obligation. The matn states that it is obligatory upon fourteen specific verses, including the first prostration verse in Surah al-Hajj and Surah Sad, upon the reciter and the hearer, even if unintentional. The commentary first defines the term, then contrasts with Shafi'i who holds it as sunnah. The Hanafi proof is that the verses themselves indicate obligation through commands, following prophets, and avoiding disbelief. The hadith 'the sajdah is upon the one who hears and recites' uses the imperative preposition 'ala (upon) which denotes wujub. Then it addresses the dispute with Shafi'i regarding two prostrations in Surah al-Hajj: Shafi'i cites a hadith; Hanafi replies that the second prostration is the recommended one after ruku' in prayer, not recitation, citing Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. Regarding Surah Sad, Shafi'i calls it a prostration of thanks; Hanafi counters that the Prophet himself prostrated in Sad, and thanks does not preclude obligation. Malik excludes the three mufassal suras; Hanafi includes them. The Hanafi list of fourteen verses is given, including those three. The relied-upon position is that the prostration is wajib on all fourteen verses for both reciter and listener.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): A prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Qur'an, wajib according to Hanafi.
مفصل (mufaṣṣal): The final section of the Qur'an, from Surah Muhammad or al-Fath to the end; here specifically the last three surahs mentioned by Malik.

Who Must Perform Sajdat al-Tilawah
Ruling that both reciter and listener, even unintentionally, must perform sajdah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who must perform sajdat al-tilawah and identify the companion practice that supports the obligation for the listener even without intent.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah is wajib on the listener even without intent, based on companion practice.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies the obligation of sajdat al-tilawah for both reciter and hearer. The commentary emphasizes that intent is not required for the listener, drawing on the authoritative practice of the Companions. Understanding this ruling ensures you know when sajda becomes mandatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). The ruling is wajib (obligatory) for both the reciter and the hearer.
2
Identify the persons obligated
The reciter (tali) and the hearer (sami'), regardless of whether the hearer intended to hear or not.
Intent (qasd) is not a condition for the hearer.
3
Note the condition of intent
For the hearer, simply hearing the sajdah verse triggers the obligation; deliberate listening is not required.
The commentary explicitly says 'even if the hearer did not intend to hear'.
4
Locate the dalil
The proof is the practice of four Companions: 'Uthman, 'Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn 'Abbas, who held that sajda is wajib on both reciter and hearer without intention.
This is a qawl sahabi (companion statement), which is a valid source in Hanafi usul.
5
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Companions' practice is authoritative because they were the most knowledgeable. Their consensus or individual rulings carry weight when no contradictory evidence exists.
This establishes the Hanafi position firmly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على من تلا: 'على' يتعلق بقوله: 'يجب' أي يجب سجدة التلاوة في هذه المواضع على من تلاها. (ع) أي يجب على من سمع ولو السامع غير قاصد للسماع. ولو غير قاصد لما روي عن عثمان وعلي وابن وسمع مسعود وابن عباس له أنهم أوجبوا على التالي والسامع من غير قصد، وكفا بهم قدوة. [رمز الحقائق: ٩٢/١]
Upon the one who recites: 'upon' is connected to His saying 'it is obligatory', i.e., the prostration of recitation is obligatory in these places upon the one who recites it. (A) That is, it is obligatory upon the one who hears, even if the hearer did not intend to hear. And 'even if not intending' is due to what is related from 'Uthman, 'Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) that they made it obligatory upon the reciter and the hearer without intention, and they are sufficient as a model. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq 92/1)
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage clarifies who is obligated to perform sajdat al-tilawah. The matn states that it is obligatory upon the reciter and the one who hears the recitation, even if the hearer did not intend to listen. The commentary explains that the preposition 'ala indicates obligation, and the condition of intention is not required for the listener. The proof is the practice of the Companions: Uthman, Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Abbas all held that the prostration is wajib upon both the reciter and the listener regardless of intent. Their consensus (or at least their individual practice) is sufficient as a model for the Ummah. This establishes the Hanafi position that sajdah is obligatory upon hearing even without deliberately listening.

Key Terms
سامع (sāmiʿ): One who hears the recitation of a sajdah verse, whether intentionally or unintentionally.

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawah is wajib upon the reciter and the hearer, even if the hearer did not intend to listen.

The Follower's Sajdat al-Tilawa: Joining After the Imam
Ruling on follower's sajdat al-tilawa with intra-Hanafi difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a follower (muqtadi) performing sajdat al-tilawa when joining after the imam, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
A follower missing the imam's sajda does not make it up; following the imam is the key.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in congregational prayer: what happens when a follower joins after the imam has already recited and prostrated for a sajda verse. The Hanafi school has an internal difference between Abu Hanifa and his student Imam Muhammad. Understanding this ruling clarifies the principle that the follower's actions are tied to those of the imam, and that prayer-related prostration cannot be performed outside the prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
First, identify the ruling for a follower who joins the prayer after the imam has recited a sajda verse and performed the prostration. According to the mufta bihi view of Abu Hanifa, the follower does not prostrate at all, neither during the prayer nor after it.
This is based on the principle that the follower's obligation is by way of following (mutaba'a).
2
Identify the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani differs: he holds that the follower should prostrate after completing the prayer because the cause (hearing the verse) remains, and the follower can make up the sajda later.
The difference hinges on whether the sajda is 'prayer-related' (salatiyya) and therefore cannot be made up outside, or whether it can be compensated.
3
Follow Each Imam's Proof
Abu Hanifa's proof: the follower's sajda is tied to the imam's action; once the imam has performed it, the opportunity lapses. Imam Muhammad's proof: the recitation occurred, so the obligation remains; the prayer-related restriction does not apply because the follower did not perform it within the prayer.
The commentary analogizes to qunut in witr: if one joins in the third rak'ah after the imam has already done qunut, the follower does not make it up.
4
Analyze the Tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa, as stated in the text: 'wa al-mukhtar' and 'ala al-fatwa'. The reason is that the sajda is an integral part of that rak'ah, and following the imam is the overriding consideration.
This tarjih is consistent with the principle that the sajda is 'salatiyya' and thus cannot be performed outside the prayer.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
The practical result (thamarah al-khilaf): under Abu Hanifa's view, a follower who joins after the imam's sajda does nothing; under Imam Muhammad's view, he should prostrate after the prayer. A mufti must follow the mufta bihi.
This difference affects fatwa given to laypeople.

Source Text

باب سجدة التلاوة
أو مؤتماً لا بتلاوته، ولو سمعها المصلّي من غيره سجد بعد الصلاة، ولـــو أعادها، لا الصلاة، ولو سمع من إمام فائتم به قبل أن يسجد سجد معه وبعده لا، وإن لم يقتد سجدها، ولم تقض الصلاتية خارجها، . أي بالإمام ما سجد الإمام

أي المصلي لتحقق السبب وهو السماع

أي أو كان السامع أي لا يجب سجد فيها أعادها، لا الصلاة، ولو سمع من إمام فائتم به قبل أن يسجد سجد أي المصلي معه أي السجدة أي لا يعيد الصلاة

رجل آية سجدة أي الإمام للتلاوة أي المقتدي

وبعده لا، وإن لم يقتد سجدها، ولم تقض الصلاتية خارجها، . أي بالإمام ما سجد الإمام

أي الإمام تحقيقاً للمبالغة

الصلاة

أو مؤتماً: وإن لم يسمع حقيقة كما إذا قرأها الإمام سراً، أو لم يكن حاضراً وقت القراءة كما اقتدي به بعد التلاوة؛ لأنها تجب عليه تبعا للإمام. رمز الحقائق: ۹۲/۱](فتح) لا بتلاوته [ أي الموتم لا عليه ولا على إمامه لا في الصلاة ولا بعدها وقال محمد: يسجدونها إذا فرغوا. ط، مسكين)]، وإطلاقه يفيد عدم الوجوب على من كان خارجها بأن سمعها الخارج من المؤتم لكنه قول البعض، والأصح الوجوب؛ لأن الحجر ثبت في حقهم فلا يعدوهم والاختلاف في الوجوب على الخارج مقيد بعدم الدخول معهم، فإن دخل سقطت، وإذا علم الوجوب على السامع إذا كان خارج الصلاة، فكذا يجب عليه إذا كان في صلاة أخرى غير صلاة التالي، ومن تلاها في الركوع أو السجود أو التشهد لا يجب؛ للحجر عن القراءة فيه ولو سمعها ممن لا تجب عليه الصلاة لصغر أو جنون تجب؛ لتحقق السبب، وقيل: لا، ولا تحب بقراءة النائم أو المغمى عليه في رواية وكذا لو سمعها من طوطى على الصحيح. (فتح عيني)

السجدة

من غيره أي من ليس معه في الصلاة. (ط) فيها : أي في الصلاة تلك السجدة التي سمعها من غيره. (ع) أعادها لأنها ناقصة؛ لأن الشرع منع عن إدخال ما ليس من أفعال الصلاة فيها، فلا يتأدى به الكامل، وهي الواجبة بإسماع ممن ليس محجور ؛ فإن ما وجب كاملاً لا يتأدى ناقصاً، وقوله: "لا" الصلاة" أي لا يعيدها؛ لأن زيادة ما دون الركعة لا يفسدها، وما في "النوادر" من الفساد وقيل: هو قول محمد، لكن الأصح عدم الفساد اتفاقاً. لا الصلاة: لأن السجود من أفعالها فلا يفسدها. (ع) فائتم به إلخ أي اقتدى ذلك السامع قبل سجود الإمام،

(فتح)

وكذا لو لم يسمع، بل ولم يكن وقت التلاوة حاضراً سجد مع الإمام تحقيقاً للمتابعة ولا يسجد بعد ما سجدها الإمام، وهذا إذا أدركه في آخر تلك الركعة؛ لأنه صار مدرك ركاً للسجدة بإدراك تلك الركعة فيكون مؤدياً لها؛ ولأنه لا يمكنه أن يسجدها في الصلاة؛ لما فيه من مخالفة الإمام، ولا بعد فراغه؛ لأنها صلاتية، فلا تقضى خارجها،

And it is said in al-'Inaya that 'salatiyya' is a mistake that is used, and according to the jurists it is better than the rare correct one. So the prayer-related prostration is not made up outside prayer, so he sins and repentance becomes compulsory, because it has the excellence of prayer, and the actions of prayer and its actions are not performed outside it. And this is if he did not invalidate the prayer before the prostration, for if he invalidated it he makes it up as part of outside it, because when it became invalid, nothing remains except mere recitation, so it was not prayer-related. And even if after he prostrated it he does not repeat it.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage states the obligations of sajdat al-tilawa. The base text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) says that if a person in prayer hears a verse of prostration from someone not in his prayer, he must prostrate after the prayer, not during. If he prostrates during, it suffices and does not invalidate the prayer. If he hears from his imam, he follows him: if he joins before the imam prostrates, he prostrates with him; if after, he does not. This is because the prostration becomes obligatory due to hearing (for the listener) and due to following (for the muqtadi). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad says the muqtadi must prostrate with his imam even if he did not hear/join later; Abu Hanifa says he must follow. The relied position is that the muqtadi prostrates with his imam as long as he joins in that rak'ah. The commentary also discusses the ruling for one who recites in ruku', sujud, or tashahhud: no sajda is required because he is prohibited from recitation in those positions. Hearing from a child or insane person still obligates sajda because the cause (hearing) is present. The text then explains that the sajda that became obligatory during prayer cannot be made up outside; if one misses it, it is sin and requires tawba. If the prayer becomes invalid before the sajda, then it is merely a tilawa sajda and can be made up.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwa): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration (sajda) from the Quran.
مؤتم (mu'tam): Follower in congregational prayer (muqtadi).
صلاتية (ṣalātiyya): Related to prayer; specifically, a sajda that becomes obligatory during the prayer (by recital of a sajda verse) and is considered part of the prayer's acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person joins the congregation (muqtadi) after the imam has already recited and performed the sajdat al-tilawa, what should he do according to the mufta bihi position?
A) He should prostrate immediately upon joining, even if the imam is standing.
B) He should not prostrate, either during or after the prayer.
C) He should prostrate after the prayer completes.
D) He should repeat the verse and prostrate.

Key Takeaway
A follower who joins after the imam has performed sajdat al-tilawa does not prostrate, neither during nor after the prayer, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Performing Sajdat al-Tilawa Within Ruku': The Condition of Fawr
Ruling on fawriyya and performing sajda in ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which sajdat al-tilawa is performed by ruku' in prayer and identify when the condition of fawr is broken.

Core Idea
Your ruku' can fulfill the sajda if you bow immediately after recitation, without three intervening verses, and intend it.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi rule that sajdat al-tilawa can be fulfilled by the ruku' of prayer, but only under strict conditions. The key is fawriyya (immediacy): the recitation must be followed directly by bowing. Reciting three or more verses breaks this immediacy, requiring a separate prostration. Intention is also required for the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the text is ruling on: performing sajdat al-tilawa by ruku' in prayer. The act is valid (sahih) if conditions met.
The overall hukm of sajdat al-tilawa is wajib; the method of performance is being examined.
2
Locate the condition of fawr
Examine the text to find the condition that the ruku' must be immediate after recitation. The text states that if the reciter recites less than three verses or nothing after the sajda verse and then bows immediately, the sajda is performed.
This is based on the principle that fawr is required for the sajda to be merged into the ruku'.
3
Apply the three-verse threshold
The text mentions a disagreement on whether three verses break fawr. The relied-upon view is that three or more verses break immediacy. Apply this to determine when a separate sajda is needed.
The ikhtilaf is mentioned to show the scholarly discussion, but the practical ruling follows the view that three verses break fawr.
4
Add the intention condition
The text specifies that if the imam intends the sajda in ruku', but the follower does not, the follower must prostrate separately. Intention is necessary for the imam's ruku' to suffice.
This highlights that the act is not automatic; the niyyah is a distinct condition.
5
Conclude the ruling
Summarize: If a sajda verse is recited, and the reciter bows immediately without reciting three or more verses, and intends the sajda (if imam), the ruku' fulfills the obligation. Otherwise, a separate sajda is required.
This is the mufta bihi position for the Hanafi school.

ثم اعلم أن تصور فوت السجود لها في الصلاة بعد أن تلاها فيها يتوقف على ما إذا قرأ بعد آية السجدة ما يزيد على ثلاث آيات؛ لأنها لا توجب قطع الفورية فلو قرأ بعدها دون ثلاث آيات أو لم يقرأ شيئاً بعدها، وركع على فور القراءة فلا يتصور فوتها؛ لأنها تتأدى في ضمن سجود الصلاة ولو بدون النية، ولو نواها الإمام في الركوع عقيب التلاوة ولم ينوها المقتدي لا تنوب عنه، ويسجد إذا سلم الإمام، وهذا مبني على أن سجدة التلاوة إنما تتأدى في الركوع بالنية ويشترط كونه على الفور، وهل ينقطع الفور بثلاث؟ قيل: نعم وقيل: لا والحاصل أنه إذا تلا آية سجدة في صلاته ثم ركع للصلاة أو سجد للصلاة ولم يقرأ بعدها ثلاث آيات فما فوقها تأدى سجود التلاوة في ضمن ذلك الركوع بشرط النية، وفي السجود بلا نية اتفاقاً فلو لم يكن على فور القراءة فلا بد لها من السجود لها استقلالاً. (مستخلص، عيني) كفته واحدة: [ أي سجدة واحدة عن التلاوتين في الصلاة في الأصح. (ط)]؛ للتداخل، وجعلت الخارجية تبعاً للصلاتية؛ لقوتها حتى لو لم يسجد للصلاتية لم يأت بالخارجية أيضاً وأثم. (فتح، عيني)
کمن كررها أي في مجلس واحد كالبيت والمسجد والسفينة، فإنه يكفيه سجدة واحدة؛ لأن مبناها على التداخل ما أمكن، وإمكانه على اتحاد المجلس؛ لكونه جامعاً للمتفرقات، وشرط التداخل اتحاد الآية والمجلس، فلا يضر المشي خطوة أو خطوتين ولا أكل لقمة وشرب جرعة ولا انتقال من زاوية البيت أو المسجد إلى زاوية أخرى، بخلاف تسدية الثوب والانتقال من غصن إلى غصن والدياسة وكرب الأرض والسبح في النهر أو الحوض؛ لاختلاف المجلس حقيقة رمز الحقائق: ۹۲/۱ ، ۹۳] واعلم أن المجلس قد يختلف حقيقة وقد يختلف حكما، والمختلف حقيقة قد يتحد حكما كما إذا انتقل في المسجد وفي البيت من زاوية إلى أخرى؛ فإنه لا يتكرر الوجوب، وفي كل موضع الاقتداء يجعل كمكان واحد، والمختلف حكماً كما إذا اشتغل بفعل آخر كثير مثلا شرع بعد التلاوة في عقد النكاح أو البيع أو الشراء ثم تلاها أخرى يتكرر الوجوب، ولو كررها راكباً على الدابة وهي تسير يتكرر إلا إذا كان في الصلاة؛ لأن الصلاة جامعة للأماكن؛ إذ الحكم بصحة الصلاة دليل اتحاد المكان. (فتح عيني) لا في مجلسين [ أي لا تكفيه سجدة واحدة إن كررها، بل يجب لكل تلاوة سجدة. (ط)] لاختلاف المجلس، ثم التبدل سواء في حق السامع والتالي، فلو تبدل مجلس السامع دون التالي يتكرر الوجوب على السامع إجماعاً، ولو تبدل مجلس التالي دون السامع يتكرر على السامع عند البعض، والأصح أنه لا يتكرر وعليه الفتوى. [رمز الحقائق: ۹۳/۱] يصح
Then know that the conception of missing the sajda in the prayer after reciting it depends on whether he recited after the sajda verse more than three verses; because it (the sajda) does not require immediate performance (fawriyya). So if he recited after it less than three verses or did not recite anything after it, and bowed immediately upon the recitation, then it is not conceivable to miss it, because it is performed within the bowing of prayer even without intention. And if the imam intended it in the bowing immediately after the recitation and the follower did not intend it, it does not suffice for him, and he prostrates when the imam says salam. This is based on that sajdat al-tilawa is performed in bowing only with intention and it requires being immediate. Is the immediacy cut off by three? It is said yes and said no. The conclusion: if he recites a sajda verse in his prayer and then bows for prayer or prostrates and did not recite after it three verses or more, the sajdat al-tilawa is performed within that bowing on condition of intention, and in prostration without intention by agreement. So if it was not immediate upon recitation, he must perform it independently. (Fath) He prostrated another, meaning even if he recited outside prayer and prostrated, then entered the prayer and repeated it in the prayer, he prostrates another for it, because the independent (sajda) is prayer-related, and there is no way to join it to the first, lest it lead to precedence of the ruling over the cause, because the second is prayer-related and stronger, so it cannot be subordinate to the weaker. (Mustakhlas, 'Ayni) It suffices one: [meaning one prostration for both recitations in the prayer according to the correct (T)] due to tadaakhul, and the external (sajda) is made subordinate to the prayer-related due to its strength, to the extent that if he did not prostrate for the prayer-related, he also does not fulfill the external and sins. (Fath, 'Ayni) Like one who repeats it in one sitting such as the house, mosque, or ship, for one prostration suffices him, because its basis is on tadaakhul as much as possible, and its possibility is on unity of the sitting, as it is a gatherer of dispersed things. And the condition of tadaakhul is unity of the verse and the sitting. So walking one or two steps does not harm, nor eating a morsel and drinking a gulp, nor moving from one corner of the house or mosque to another, contrary to letting down the cloth, moving from branch to branch, threshing, hoeing the earth, swimming in the river or basin, due to difference of sitting in reality. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 1/92, 93) And know that the sitting may differ in reality and may differ legally, and what differs in reality may be united legally, as when one moves in the mosque and in the house from corner to another, for the obligation does not repeat. And in every place of following, it is made like one place. And what differs legally, as when he occupies himself with another major action, for example he starts after the recitation in a marriage contract or sale or purchase, then recites another, the obligation repeats. And if he repeats it while riding an animal that is walking, it repeats, except if he is in prayer, because prayer unites places, since the ruling of validity of prayer is evidence of unity of place. (Fath 'Ayni) Not in two sittings [meaning one prostration does not suffice him if he repeats it, rather for each recitation a prostration is obligatory. (T)] due to difference of sitting. Then the change is equal regarding the listener and the reciter. So if the sitting of the listener changes without the reciter, the obligation repeats upon the listener by consensus. And if the sitting of the reciter changes without the listener, it repeats upon the listener according to some, and the correct is that it does not repeat, and upon this is the fatwa. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 1/93) It is valid.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage discusses two connected topics: (1) the condition of fawr (immediacy) for sajdat al-tilawa to be performed within the bowing of prayer, and (2) the ruling on multiple recitations of the same sajda verse. Regarding fawr, if a person recites a sajda verse in prayer and then immediately bows (ruku') without reciting three or more verses in between, the sajda is performed by his ruku' if he intends it. If he recites more than three verses after the sajda verse, the fawr is broken, and he must perform a separate prostration for the tilawa later in the prayer. There is disagreement on whether three verses break fawr; the text mentions both views. Regarding multiple recitations: if one recites the same sajda verse multiple times in the same sitting (majlis), one sajda suffices for all, due to tadaakhul (merging). If the recitations occur in different sittings, each requires its own sajda. The commentary defines a 'majlis' in detail: within a house or mosque, moving from corner to corner does not change the majlis, but engaging in a completely different activity (like buying/selling) does. For a rider, if the animal moves, the majlis changes unless he is in prayer, because prayer unifies the place. The relied-upon position is that one sajda suffices for multiple recitations in one majlis, and if the reciter changes majlis but the listener doesn't, the listener does not have to repeat according to the preferred view.

Key Terms
فورية (fawriyya): The condition of performing the sajda immediately after recitation; if the reciter delays by reciting three or more verses, the immediacy is lost.
تداخل (tadākhul): Merging of multiple obligations into one performance; here, one sajda suffices for multiple recitations of the same verse in the same sitting.
مجلس (majlis): A single sitting or location where one remains; changing the majlis by moving to a different room or engaging in a separate activity breaks the unity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person recites a sajda verse in prayer, then recites two verses (not sajda), then bows, does his ruku' fulfill the sajda?
A) Yes, because less than three verses were recited.
B) No, because any verses break fawr.
C) Yes, because intention is not necessary.
D) No, because ruku' cannot substitute for sajda.

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawa can be performed by ruku' in prayer if you bow immediately after recitation, without reciting three or more verses, and with intention.

Multiple Recitations and the Principle of Tadaakhul in Sajdat al-Tilawa
Ruling on tadaakhul and definition of majlis for sajdat al-tilawa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of tadaakhul to determine when one sajda suffices for multiple recitations and define what constitutes a single majlis.

Core Idea
One prostration fulfills multiple recitations of the same verse in one sitting, thanks to tadaakhul.

This lesson explores the Hanafi rule that reciting the same sajda verse multiple times in one majlis (sitting) requires only one prostration due to tadaakhul (merging). We will examine the definition of majlis, what actions preserve or break it, and special cases like prayer and riding. The relied-upon position is that one sajda suffices for multiple recitations in one sitting, but a new sitting requires a new prostration.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The text begins by stating that one prostration suffices for multiple recitations of the same sajda verse in one sitting (majlis). This is the principle of tadaakhul.
The condition is unity of the verse and unity of the majlis.
2
Define the majlis
The text gives examples of a single majlis: a house, a mosque, a ship. Moving within the same building (e.g., from one corner to another) does not break the majlis.
Minor movements like walking a step or two, eating a morsel, or drinking a gulp are also permissible without breaking unity.
3
Identify what breaks the majlis
Actions that clearly break the majlis include: donning a cloth (tasdiya), moving from a branch to another (for trees), threshing, hoeing the earth, swimming in a river or basin. These change the majlis in reality.
The text distinguishes between real and legal change of majlis.
4
Apply the rider and prayer exceptions
If a person recites the same verse while riding a moving animal, each recitation requires a separate sajda because the majlis changes with movement. However, if he is in prayer, the prayer unifies the place, so one sajda suffices.
This shows that prayer has a special status in unifying the location.
5
Conclude with the listener's case
The text discusses a scenario where the listener's sitting changes but the reciter's does not, and vice versa. The relied-upon view is that if only the reciter's majlis changes, the listener's obligation does not repeat.
This is the mufta bihi position according to the text.

کمن كررها أي في مجلس واحد كالبيت والمسجد والسفينة، فإنه يكفيه سجدة واحدة؛ لأن مبناها على التداخل ما أمكن، وإمكانه على اتحاد المجلس؛ لكونه جامعاً للمتفرقات، وشرط التداخل اتحاد الآية والمجلس، فلا يضر المشي خطوة أو خطوتين ولا أكل لقمة وشرب جرعة ولا انتقال من زاوية البيت أو المسجد إلى زاوية أخرى، بخلاف تسدية الثوب والانتقال من غصن إلى غصن والدياسة وكرب الأرض والسبح في النهر أو الحوض؛ لاختلاف المجلس حقيقة رمز الحقائق: ۹۲/۱ ، ۹۳] واعلم أن المجلس قد يختلف حقيقة وقد يختلف حكما، والمختلف حقيقة قد يتحد حكما كما إذا انتقل في المسجد وفي البيت من زاوية إلى أخرى؛ فإنه لا يتكرر الوجوب، وفي كل موضع الاقتداء يجعل كمكان واحد، والمختلف حكماً كما إذا اشتغل بفعل آخر كثير مثلا شرع بعد التلاوة في عقد النكاح أو البيع أو الشراء ثم تلاها أخرى يتكرر الوجوب، ولو كررها راكباً على الدابة وهي تسير يتكرر إلا إذا كان في الصلاة؛ لأن الصلاة جامعة للأماكن؛ إذ الحكم بصحة الصلاة دليل اتحاد المكان. Then know that the conception of missing the sajda in the prayer after reciting it depends on whether he recited after the sajda verse more than three verses; because it (the sajda) does not require immediate performance (fawriyya). So if he recited after it less than three verses or did not recite anything after it, and bowed immediately upon the recitation, then it is not conceivable to miss it, because it is performed within the bowing of prayer even without intention. And if the imam intended it in the bowing immediately after the recitation and the follower did not intend it, it does not suffice for him, and he prostrates when the imam says salam. This is based on that sajdat al-tilawa is performed in bowing only with intention and it requires being immediate. Is the immediacy cut off by three? It is said yes and said no. The conclusion: if he recites a sajda verse in his prayer and then bows for prayer or prostrates and did not recite after it three verses or more, the sajdat al-tilawa is performed within that bowing on condition of intention, and in prostration without intention by agreement. So if it was not immediate upon recitation, he must perform it independently. (Fath) He prostrated another, meaning even if he recited outside prayer and prostrated, then entered the prayer and repeated it in the prayer, he prostrates another for it, because the independent (sajda) is prayer-related, and there is no way to join it to the first, lest it lead to precedence of the ruling over the cause, because the second is prayer-related and stronger, so it cannot be subordinate to the weaker. (Mustakhlas, 'Ayni) It suffices one: [meaning one prostration for both recitations in the prayer according to the correct (T)] due to tadaakhul, and the external (sajda) is made subordinate to the prayer-related due to its strength, to the extent that if he did not prostrate for the prayer-related, he also does not fulfill the external and sins. (Fath, 'Ayni) Like one who repeats it in one sitting such as the house, mosque, or ship, for one prostration suffices him, because its basis is on tadaakhul as much as possible, and its possibility is on unity of the sitting, as it is a gatherer of dispersed things. And the condition of tadaakhul is unity of the verse and the sitting. So walking one or two steps does not harm, nor eating a morsel and drinking a gulp, nor moving from one corner of the house or mosque to another, contrary to letting down the cloth, moving from branch to branch, threshing, hoeing the earth, swimming in the river or basin, due to difference of sitting in reality. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 1/92, 93) And know that the sitting may differ in reality and may differ legally, and what differs in reality may be united legally, as when one moves in the mosque and in the house from corner to another, for the obligation does not repeat. And in every place of following, it is made like one place. And what differs legally, as when he occupies himself with another major action, for example he starts after the recitation in a marriage contract or sale or purchase, then recites another, the obligation repeats. And if he repeats it while riding an animal that is walking, it repeats, except if he is in prayer, because prayer unites places, since the ruling of validity of prayer is evidence of unity of place. (Fath 'Ayni) Not in two sittings [meaning one prostration does not suffice him if he repeats it, rather for each recitation a prostration is obligatory. (T)] due to difference of sitting. Then the change is equal regarding the listener and the reciter. So if the sitting of the listener changes without the reciter, the obligation repeats upon the listener by consensus. And if the sitting of the reciter changes without the listener, it repeats upon the listener according to some, and the correct is that it does not repeat, and upon this is the fatwa. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 1/93) It is valid.

Commentary
This passage discusses two connected topics: (1) the condition of fawr (immediacy) for sajdat al-tilawa to be performed within the bowing of prayer, and (2) the ruling on multiple recitations of the same sajda verse. Regarding fawr, if a person recites a sajda verse in prayer and then immediately bows (ruku') without reciting three or more verses in between, the sajda is performed by his ruku' if he intends it. If he recites more than three verses after the sajda verse, the fawr is broken, and he must perform a separate prostration for the tilawa later in the prayer. There is disagreement on whether three verses break fawr; the text mentions both views. Regarding multiple recitations: if one recites the same sajda verse multiple times in the same sitting (majlis), one sajda suffices for all, due to tadaakhul (merging). If the recitations occur in different sittings, each requires its own sajda. The commentary defines a 'majlis' in detail: within a house or mosque, moving from corner to corner does not change the majlis, but engaging in a completely different activity (like buying/selling) does. For a rider, if the animal moves, the majlis changes unless he is in prayer, because prayer unifies the place. The relied-upon position is that one sajda suffices for multiple recitations in one majlis, and if the reciter changes majlis but the listener doesn't, the listener does not have to repeat according to the preferred view.

Key Terms
فورية (fawriyya): The condition of performing the sajda immediately after recitation; if the reciter delays by reciting three or more verses, the immediacy is lost.
تداخل (tadākhul): Merging of multiple obligations into one performance; here, one sajda suffices for multiple recitations of the same verse in the same sitting.
مجلس (majlis): A single sitting or location where one remains; changing the majlis by moving to a different room or engaging in a separate activity breaks the unity.

Key Takeaway

Sajdat al-Tilawah: One Sajdah Suffices for Repeated Recitations in One Gathering
Expansion on sufficiency of one sajdah for repeated sajdah recitations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on multiple sajdat al-tilawah in one gathering, apply the condition of fawr, and distinguish between same and different gatherings.

Core Idea
One sajdah suffices for multiple recitations in one gathering due to tadakhul (overlap).

This lesson unpacks a key ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: when you recite a sajdah verse multiple times in the same gathering, a single sajdah fulfills all. We will examine the conditions for this overlap, especially the role of fawr (immediacy) and what constitutes a single gathering.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
State the main ruling: one sajdah suffices for multiple recitations in one majlis, but not in different majalis. Note the exception when the first recitation is outside prayer and the second inside.
2
Examine the condition of fawr
Understand that fawr (immediacy) is required for the sajdah to be fulfilled by bowing or prostration in prayer. Fawr is broken by reciting three or more ayahs after the sajdah verse.
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether three ayahs break fawr; the relied-upon position is that it does not.
3
Analyze the principle of tadakhul
Recognize that tadakhul (overlap) allows one sajdah to fulfill multiple wajib acts of the same type when conditions are met. The condition for tadakhul is unity of the verse and unity of the gathering.
4
Define what constitutes one majlis
Learn that a majlis is defined by the place and continuity. Minor acts (walking a step, eating a morsel) do not break the gathering, but significant acts (changing garment, climbing a tree) do. In prayer, the entire prayer is considered one majlis.
5
Apply to the listener's case
If the listener's gathering changes but the reciter's does not, the obligation repeats for the listener. If only the reciter's gathering changes, the listener's obligation does not repeat according to the fatwa.

يصح
The Book of Prayer. Chapter on Sajdat al-Tilawah. If one recites outside prayer and prostrates for it, and then repeats it (the recitation) in prayer, he prostrates another sajdah. And if he did not prostrate the first time, one sajdah suffices him for the verse of sajdah. Like one who repeats it in one gathering, not in two gatherings. ... (detailed discussion of fawr, three ayahs, same/different gatherings).
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding sajdat al-tilawah. The author begins by giving the ruling: if one recites a sajdah verse outside prayer and prostrates, then recites it again in prayer, he must prostrate another sajdah in prayer. However, if he did not prostrate outside, then one sajdah in prayer suffices for both recitations. This is because the prayer sajdah is stronger. The passage then discusses the condition of fawr (immediacy): if one recites a sajdah verse in prayer and then immediately bows or prostrates for the prayer, that bowing or prostration fulfills the sajdah al-tilawah if he intends it, provided he did not recite three or more ayahs after the sajdah verse. If he did recite three or more, then the fawr is broken and he must prostrate separately. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about whether fawr is broken by three ayahs; the relied-upon position is that it is not, but caution requires separate prostration. The passage then explains the rule for multiple recitations in one gathering: one sajdah suffices, because the basis of sajdah is that they overlap when possible. The condition for overlap is unity of the verse and unity of the gathering. Actions like walking a step or two, eating a morsel, or drinking a sip do not break the gathering, but changing a garment, climbing a tree, treading grain, etc., are considered different gatherings. The passage concludes with rulings for a listener whose gathering changes, and emphasizes that the fatwa is on the position that the listener's obligation does not repeat if only the reciter's gathering changes.

Key Terms
الفورية (al-fawriyyah): Immediacy: the condition that bowing or prostration in prayer must follow the recitation of a sajdah verse without a significant gap (like reciting three or more ayahs) for it to fulfill the sajdah al-tilawah.
المجلس (al-majlis): The gathering or place where one recites or hears the sajdah verse; unity of majlis allows overlapping of multiple sajdahs. It can differ in reality (physical place) or in ruling (engagement in a different activity).
التداخل (al-tadakhul): Overlap; the principle that multiple wajib acts of the same type can be fulfilled by a single performance when conditions allow (e.g., one sajdah for multiple tilawahs in one majlis).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person recites a sajdah verse twice in the same mosque gathering, how many sajdahs are required?
A) Two separate sajdahs are required.
B) One sajdah suffices, but he must intend both.
C) One sajdah suffices without extra intention.
D) He must recite another verse to make up.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, one sajdah suffices for multiple recitations of a sajdah verse in the same gathering, due to the principle of tadakhul, provided the gathering and verse are the same.

Method and Conditions of Sajdat al-Tilawah
Ruling and method of sajdat al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of sajdat al-tilawah and identify its conditions of validity.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah is a simple prostration between two takbirs without the formalities of prayer.

This lesson explains the precise method (kayfiyyah) of sajdat al-tilawah as established by the Hanafi school. Understanding the required conditions and the absence of certain prayer elements is essential for performing this wajib act correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions
List the conditions that make sajdat al-tilawah valid: ritual purity (wudu), covering the private parts, facing the qiblah, and cleanliness of place, garment, and body.
These are the same conditions for prayer, except the opening takbir (tahrimah) and intention of the specific verse are not required.
2
Describe the takbirs and prostration
The prostration is performed between two recommended takbirs (takbir for going down and takbir for rising). One does not raise the hands, recite tashahhud, or say salam.
Both takbirs are sunnah (mandub), not wajib.
3
Note the evidence
The practice is based on the hadith of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet ﷺ did not perform additional actions in sajdat al-tilawah.
The absence of tashahhud and salam is because the prostration is a single act, unlike prayer which is a sequence of diverse acts.

(ط) لا عكسه وهو أن يقرأ آية السجدة ويترك ما سواها. (ط)] لأنه مبادرة إليها، ثم قيل: وجوب السجدة متعلق بالكلمة التي فيها ذكر السجود، وعن محمد: لا يجب إلا أن يقرأ معها أكثر آية السجدة، وقيل: كلها، وقال محمد وأحب إلي أن يقرأ قبلها آية أو آيتين دفعا للتوهم تفضيل آي السجدة على غيرها مع أن الكل من حيث في رتبة، واستحسنوا إخفاءها شفقة على السامعين، وقيل: إن وقع بقلبه أنهم يؤدونها ولا يشق ذلك بها؛ ليكون حثاً لهم على الطاعة، وإذا لم يعلم بحالهم ينبغي إخفائها. [تبيين الحقائق: ٥٠٥/١] مهمة: من قرأ آي السجدة كلها في مجلس واحد وسجد لكل منها كفاه الله ما أهمه سواء سجد لكل آية بعد تلاوتها بأن تلا الأولى وسجد، ثم الثانية وسجد ،وهكذا، أو تلا آيات السجدة كلها ثم بعد الفراغ من تلاوة الكل
سجد لها. (فتح) تتمة: سجدة الشكر لا عبرة بها عند أبي حنيفة وهي مكروهة تنزيها، وتركها أولى، وبه قال مالك، وعندهما: قربة يثاب عليها، وبه قال الشافعي وأحمد، وهيئتها كهيئة التلاوة، وقال في الأشباه : سجدة الشكر جائزة عند أبي حنيفة واجبة، والمعتمد أن الخلاف في سنيتها لا في الجواز والفتوى على قولهما، لكنها تكره بعد الصلاة؛ لأن الجهلة يعتقدونها سنة أو واجبة وكل مباح يؤدي إليه فهو مكروه. (فتح)
لا
The Book of Prayer. Chapter on Sajdat al-Tilawah. Its manner: that he prostrate with the conditions of prayer between two takbirs without raising hands, tashahhud, and salam. And it is disliked to recite a surah and leave the sajdah verse, not the opposite. Commentary: Conditions of prayer except for the opening takbir and intention of the specific verse. Hadith of Ibn Umar indicates no raising hands, tashahhud, or salam. Shafi'i differs. Then rules on reciting surah without sajdah verse, and sajdat al-shukr.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage describes the method (kayfiyyah) of sajdat al-tilawah. According to the Hanafi school, the prostration is performed with the same conditions as prayer (ritual purity, covering the private parts, facing the qiblah, and cleanliness), but without the opening takbir (tahrimah) and without the intention of the specific verse. The prostration is between two takbirs (both recommended), and one does not raise the hands, recite tashahhud, or say salam. The evidence is the practice of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i considers sajdat al-tilawah an independent act of worship requiring an opening takbir, tashahhud, and taslim because it is a distinct worship. The Hanafi response is that the command is for prostration alone, and adding extra elements is not justified. The passage then discusses the disliked nature of reciting a surah while deliberately omitting the sajdah verse because it resembles disdain for prostration. It is not disliked to recite only the sajdah verse, as that is a prompt to perform it. The passage also includes a note on sajdat al-shukr: according to Abu Hanifa, it is not a recognized practice and is considered lightly disliked (makruh tanzihan), but according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is a meritorious act. The fatwa is on their view, but it is disliked after prayer because people may consider it obligatory or sunnah, leading to potential innovation.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir that initiates the prayer and renders forbidden what was previously permissible. In sajdat al-tilawah, it is not required.
بين تكبيرتين (bayna takbiratayn): Between two takbirs: one to go into prostration and one to rise from it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for sajdat al-tilawah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Ritual purity (wudu)
B) Facing the qiblah
C) Reciting tashahhud
D) Covering the private parts

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires only the conditions of prayer minus the opening takbir, and the prostration is performed between two sunnah takbirs without tashahhud or salam.
