Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Disputes on the Method of Sajdat al-Tilawah and Sajdat al-Shukr
Inter-madhhab dispute and intra-madhhab ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Shafi'i objection to the Hanafi method of sajdat al-tilawah, state the Hanafi response, and describe the intra-Hanafi difference on sajdat al-shukr.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah is a single act, so it does not need the opening and closing of a multi-act prayer.

This lesson examines the key disagreements surrounding sajdat al-tilawah and the ruling on sajdat al-shukr. Understanding these disputes deepens your appreciation of the Hanafi methodology and its reliance on textual evidence and rational inference.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that sajdat al-tilawah is an independent worship (ibadah mustaqillah) and therefore requires its own opening (takbir), tashahhud, and closing (taslim).
He analogizes it to prayer, which requires entering (tahrimah) and exiting (taslim).
2
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the command is only for the prostration itself (al-m'amur bihi huwa al-sujud), and adding other elements is an innovation by opinion. The prostration is a single act, so it does not need the opening and closing that a sequence of different acts (prayer) requires.
The hadith of Ibn Umar supports this simplicity.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on sajdat al-shukr
Abu Hanifa considers sajdat al-shukr not recognized (la ibrah biha) and lightly disliked (makruh tanzihan). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it a meritorious act (qurbah) rewarded. The fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view, but it is disliked after prayer due to public confusion.
The ruling on sajdat al-shukr is thus permissible with conditions.
4
Determine the practical consequence
Hanafis perform sajdat al-tilawah simply, while Shafi'is include formalities. On sajdat al-shukr, Hanafis may perform it according to the Sahibayn's view but avoid it after prayer.
Knowing these differences helps avoid confusion in mixed congregations.

عبادة مستقلة (ibadah mustaqillah): An independent act of worship, as considered by al-Shafi'i for sajdat al-tilawah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Sajdat al-Tilawa: Method and the Shafi'i Dispute
Explains method of prostration of recitation and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of Sajdat al-Tilawa and explain why it differs from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-Tilawa is a single prostration between two takbirs, not a full prayer.

Sajdat al-Tilawa is a well-known practice, but its exact procedure is debated between madhahib. The Hanafi school, relying on the practice of the Prophet, keeps it simple, while the Shafi'i school treats it as an independent act of worship requiring entry and exit. In this lesson, we will examine the text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary to understand the Hanafi method and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi method: prostrate with conditions of prayer (except takbirat al-ihram and intention of the ayah) between two takbirs, without raising hands, tashahhud, or salam.
The text explicitly says 'between two takbirs without raising hands, tashahhud, and salam'.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i requires takbirat al-ihram, tashahhud, and salam because he considers sajdat al-tilawa an independent act of worship.
The text presents the Shafi'i view: 'He prostrates one prostration by standing and saying takbir raising his hands intending...'
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i reasoning: since it is an independent act of worship, it must have a formal entry (takbir) and exit (salam) like prayer.
This is based on qiyas on salah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the commanded act is only the prostration; adding extra elements is an unjustified increase. The hadith of Ibn Umar shows the Prophet did not do those acts.
The text says: 'Our evidence: That which is commanded is the prostration, so it is not increased with opinion.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis perform sajdat al-tilawa simply, while Shafi'is perform it with a full prayer format (takbir, tashahhud, salam).
This affects how Muslims in different madhhab observe the prostration.

(ط)] لأنه مبادرة إليها، ثم قيل: وجوب السجدة متعلق بالكلمة التي فيها ذكر السجود، وعن محمد: لا يجب إلا أن يقرأ معها أكثر آية السجدة، وقيل: كلها، وقال محمد وأحب إلي أن يقرأ قبلها آية أو آيتين دفعا للتوهم تفضيل آي السجدة على غيرها مع أن الكل من حيث في رتبة، واستحسنوا إخفاءها شفقة على السامعين، وقيل: إن وقع بقلبه أنهم يؤدونها ولا يشق ذلك بها؛ ليكون حثاً لهم على الطاعة، وإذا لم يعلم بحالهم ينبغي إخفائها. [تبيين الحقائق: ٥٠٥/١] مهمة: من قرأ آي السجدة كلها في مجلس واحد وسجد لكل منها كفاه الله ما أهمه سواء سجد لكل آية بعد تلاوتها بأن تلا الأولى وسجد، ثم الثانية وسجد ،وهكذا، أو تلا آيات السجدة كلها ثم بعد الفراغ من تلاوة الكل

(فتح) تتمة: سجدة الشكر لا عبرة بها عند أبي حنيفة وهي مكروهة تنزيها، وتركها أولى، وبه قال مالك، وعندهما: قربة يثاب عليها، وبه قال الشافعي وأحمد، وهيئتها كهيئة التلاوة، وقال في الأشباه : سجدة الشكر جائزة عند أبي حنيفة واجبة، والمعتمد أن الخلاف في سنيتها لا في الجواز والفتوى على قولهما، لكنها تكره بعد الصلاة؛ لأن الجهلة يعتقدونها سنة أو واجبة وكل مباح يؤدي إليه فهو مكروه. Book of Prayer. Chapter of the Prostration of Recitation. Its method: that he prostrates with the conditions of prayer between two takbirs without raising hands, tashahhud, and salam. It is disliked that he recites a surah and leaves the ayah of prostration, not the opposite. [Commentary: (i.e., the prostration, i.e., he leaves) With the conditions of prayer except for the opening takbir and intention of specifying the ayah. (T) i.e., it requires what is required for prayer of ablution, covering the private parts, facing the qibla, purity of place, garment, and body. His saying: 'between two takbirs without raising hands' etc. due to what is narrated in the hadith of Ibn Umar that when he was prostrating, he did not do in the prostration, meaning he did not raise his hands, nor tashahhud, nor salam; because that is for tahlil (to end prayer), and that requires prior opening takbir, which is absent here. The conclusion: whoever wants the prostration of recitation says takbir as recommendation without raising hands, tashahhud, and salam, and prostrates, then says takbir as recommendation, and raises his head like a prostration of prayer. He says the tasbih of prostration in it, and that is the most correct. If the prayer was supererogatory, he says what he wishes of what has been reported, and likewise outside prayer. Al-Shafi'i said: He prostrates one prostration by standing and saying takbir raising his hands intending, then says takbir for prostration without raising hands, then says takbir for rising and sits, recites tashahhud, then says salam twice; because it is an independent act of worship, so what is required for prayer of entering and exiting is considered for it. Our evidence: That which is commanded is the prostration, so it is not increased with opinion. The prostration is a single act, so it does not need an opening and closing as prayer needed them because it consists of varying acts. (Fath) Between two recommended takbirs, and he says the tasbih of prostration in it according to the most correct. (T) And salam meaning without tashahhud and other than salam. It is fulfilled by a prostration of prayer absolutely, and likewise by bowing if he intends it and does not cut off the immediacy of recitation. (T) He leaves it because it resembles disdain for it, and gives the impression of fleeing from the obligation of prostration and abandoning some of the Quran, and all that is disliked with a prohibition-like dislike (makruh tahrimi) (Fath) the ayah of prostration in prayer or other, because it resembles disdain for them. (T) Not the opposite, which is to recite the ayah of prostration and leave what is besides it. (T) because it is rushing to it. Then it is said: The obligation of prostration is attached to the word that contains the mention of prostration. From Muhammad: It is not obligatory unless he recites with it more of the ayah of prostration. And it is said: all of it. Muhammad said: I prefer that he recites before it an ayah or two to dispel the assumption of preferring the ayah of prostration over others, although all are in the same rank. They considered it good to conceal it out of compassion for the listeners. It is said: If it occurs in his heart that they will perform it and it is not difficult for them, to encourage them to obedience. When he does not know their state, he should conceal it. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/505] Important: Whoever recites all the ayahs of prostration in one gathering and prostrates for each, Allah suffices him in what concerns him, whether he prostrates for each ayah after reciting it by reciting the first and prostrating, then the second and prostrating, and so on, or recites all the ayahs then after finishing the recitation prostrates for them. (Fath) Appendix: The prostration of thanks is not considered according to Abu Hanifa and it is disliked with tanzih, and leaving it is better. Malik said the same. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): It is a good deed rewarded. Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad stated the same. Its form is like the form of recitation prostration. It was said in al-Ashbah: The prostration of thanks is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and obligatory. The relied-upon is that the difference is in its sunnah status, not in permissibility, and the fatwa is on their statement, but it is disliked after prayer because the ignorant consider it sunnah or obligatory, and every permissible thing that leads to that is disliked. (Fath) No.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with its commentaries, explains the method and rulings of Sajdat al-Tilawa (the prostration of recitation). It begins by stating the method: the worshipper prostrates with the conditions of prayer (ablution, covering awrah, facing qibla, purity) between two takbirs, without raising hands, without tashahhud, and without salam. It is makruh tahrimi to intentionally skip the verse of prostration when reciting a surah, but not vice versa (i.e., reciting only the prostration verse is commendable). The commentary clarifies that the conditions of prayer apply except for the opening takbir (tahrimah) and the intention to specify the verse. The hadith of Ibn Umar is cited to show that the Prophet (saw) did not raise hands, recite tashahhud, or say salam in sajdat al-tilawa. The passage then presents the Shafi'i view that sajdat al-tilawa is an independent worship requiring takbirat al-ihram, tashahhud, and salam. The Hanafi response is that the command is only to prostrate; adding extra elements is not permitted. The commentary also notes that the tasbih of prostration is recited, and that sajdat al-tilawa can be performed both inside and outside prayer. The passage then discusses issues like reciting multiple prostration verses in one sitting, and concludes with a note on Sajdat al-Shukr (prostration of thanks): according to Abu Hanifa it is not considered and is makruh tanzih, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it a rewarded act; the fatwa is on their view, but it is disliked after prayer due to common misunderstanding.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawa): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration in the Quran.
تكبيرة (takbira): The declaration 'Allahu Akbar' said at specific points in the prostration (beginning and end).
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in prayer; not required in sajdat al-tilawa according to Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how is Sajdat al-Tilawa performed?
A) With takbirat al-ihram, tashahhud, and salam.
B) Between two takbirs without tashahhud or salam.
C) With a single takbir and no prostration.
D) By bowing instead of prostrating.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of Sajdat al-Tilawa is a simple prostration between two takbirs, based on the Prophet's practice, and does not require the full prayer format.

The Hanafi Definition of a Traveler
Defines the traveler and minimum distance for prayer concessions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of a traveler eligible for concessions, identify the hadith proof and its istidlal, and explain the minimum distance ikhtilaf with Shafi'i.

Core Idea
A traveler must intend a three-day moderate journey beyond his residence to qualify for qasr and other concessions.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of a traveler (musafir) from the chapter on prayer. We will see how the minimum distance is derived from a hadith on wiping, and why the Hanafi school insists on three days despite differences with other imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is 'becoming a traveler' (musafir) which triggers rukhsas. The condition is a defined journey: passing beyond dwellings, with intention of a three-day moderate trek.
The ruling here is a shart (condition) for concessions, not a hukm taklifi directly.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith: 'The resident wipes one day and night, and the traveler three days and their nights.' The word 'traveler' (al-musafir) is general.
The passage cites the hadith from the chapter on wiping (mash) and applies it to travel.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The generality of 'al-musafir' requires that every traveler is entitled to three days of wiping. If travel could be less than three days, some travelers would not meet this, causing inconsistency in the Lawgiver's speech. Hence, the minimum travel is three days.
Hanafi usul: alif lam signals istighraq al-jins (genus inclusion).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Shafi'i: two days (16 farsakhs). Abu Yusuf (intra-Hanafi): two days and most of the third. The relied-upon Hanafi position is three days.
Each school has its own proofs from other hadith; the Hanafi tarjih relies on the generality here.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Mufta bihi is three days' moderate journey (sayr wasat). The moderate pace is that of camels/walking, avoiding very fast or very slow. Days counted from shortest days; full day not required (reaching noon suffices).
This tarjih is from Zahir al-Riwaayah.

باب صلاة المسافر المناسبة بينهما ظاهرة أي كل من التلاوة والسفر ،عارض، إلا أن التلاوة عارض هو عبادة في نفسها إلا بعارض، والسفر عارض مباح إلا بعارض يعني أن الأصل في التلاوة أن تكون عبادة إلا بعارض كالرياء، والأصل في السفر الإباحة إلا بعارض كالسفر لزيارة الرحم، وفي بعض النسخ "باب المسافر" وفي بعضها "باب صلاة المسافر، واختار الشارح مسكين النسخة الثانية، فالإضافة من إضافة الفعل إلى فاعله، والأصل في المفاعلة أن تكون بين اثنين، وقد تستعمل في واحد، وهنا من قبيل الأول؛ لأن المسافر لا يخرج من بيته غالباً إلا مع رفيقه، والسفر في اللغة الكشف، سمي به؛ لأنه يكشف عن أخلاق الرجال، وشرعاً: قطع مسافة تتغير به الأحكام من قصر الصلاة، وإباحة الفطر، وامتداد مدة المسح، وسقوط وجوب الجمعة، والعيدين، والأضحية، وحرمة الخروج على المرأة بغير محرم. (فتح) مريداً سيراً إلخ [ أي حال كونه مريداً؛ لأنه لو لم يرد ذلك فسافر الأقاليم يوماً بعد يوم لا قصر له، فالقصد وحده غير معتبر، والفعل وحده كذلك، وإنما العبرة للمجموع. Chapter of the Traveler's Prayer. i.e., regarding the explanation of its rulings. (f k s) Whoever passes beyond the dwellings of his town intending a medium journey of three days. (:) The chapter of the traveler's prayer: the suitability between them is apparent i.e., both recitation and travel are temporary, except that recitation is a temporary act of worship in itself except due to a temporary cause, and travel is a temporary permissible except due to a temporary cause, meaning that the origin in recitation is to be worship except due to a cause like riya', and the origin in travel is permissibility except due to a cause like travel to visit relatives. In some copies: 'Chapter of the Traveler' and in some: 'Chapter of the Traveler's Prayer'. The commentator Miskeen chose the second version, so the idafah is of the action to its doer. The origin in mutual action is between two, and it may be used for one. Here it is the former because the traveler does not leave his house usually except with a companion. Travel linguistically means uncovering, named because it uncovers the characters of men. Legally: Covering a distance by which rulings change: shortening prayer, permitting breaking fast, extending the period of wiping, dropping the obligation of Friday prayer, two Eids, sacrifice, and the prohibition of a woman going out without a mahram. (Fath, Miskeen) He passes beyond the dwellings from the side he left from, even if opposite from another side there is a building. (Ayni) His town: Not intended literally, but rather the place of residence, inclusive of city and village metaphorically, because the one who leaves a village for travel is a traveler. (Fath) Intending a journey etc. i.e., in the state of intending; because if he did not intend that and traveled provinces day by day, there is no shortening for him. So intention alone is not considered, nor action alone; rather the consideration is for the combination. (Mustakhlis) It is a circumstantial adverb for the pronoun of 'passes beyond', and 'journey' is the object of 'intending'. Then this journey is described by two things: First: that it is moderate, Second: that it is three days. So 'journey' is in the accusative as object, and 'moderate' and 'three days' are in the accusative as description. Restriction to three days: it is the minimum period of travel according to us, due to his saying (saw): 'The resident wipes one day and night, and the traveler three days and their nights.' The aspect of deduction: the word 'traveler' is used with the definite article alif and lam, so it includes the entire genus due to the absence of a specific referent, and it requires that every traveler is entitled to three days. That is possible only if the minimum period of travel is three days; because if it were less, some travelers would be excluded from availing this concession, and there would be inconsistency in the speech of the Lawgiver. Increase over it is rejected by consensus, so the need is to prove that three is the minimum period of travel. According to al-Shafi'i: It is estimated at two days, which is sixteen farsakhs, and in one opinion: one day and night. According to Malik: Four barid, each barid twelve miles. According to Abu Yusuf: Two days and most of the third. Each has evidences from traditions, and for us is what we narrated. (Ayni and others) (from wiping) very very. So the moderate journey is the journey of camels and walking. 'Moderate' is a precaution against the journey of post (speedy) and against slow walking. (Mustakhlis) Three days from the shortest days of the year, and the complete day is not required, rather up to noon. (T)
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage defines the traveler (musafir) who is eligible for concessions in prayer (qasr) and other rulings. The key definition is: a person who passes beyond the built-up area of his town intending a journey of three days at a moderate pace. The commentary explains that 'town' includes any place of residence, whether city or village. The journey must be intended; wandering without intention does not qualify. The three-day minimum is derived from the hadith about wiping (mash) over socks: the resident wipes one day and night, the traveler three days. The word 'traveler' with the definite article implies the genus, so every traveler is entitled to three days; therefore the minimum travel must be three days. The passage also notes differences: al-Shafi'i estimates at two days (16 farsakhs), Malik at four barid, and within the Hanafi school, Abu Yusuf says two days and most of the third. The relied-upon view is three days. The moderate pace is defined as camel or walking speed, avoiding very fast (post) or very slow speeds. Days are counted from the shortest days of the year, and the full day is not required; reaching noon suffices.

Key Terms
سير وسط (sayr wasat): A moderate pace of travel, typically the speed of camels or normal walking, avoiding very fast (like post) or very slow.
قصر الصلاة (qasr al-salah): Shortening the four-rak'ah prayers to two rak'ahs during travel.
مصر (misr): In this context, the place of residence, including towns and villages, not just a major city.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Three days
C) One day and night
D) Four barid

Key Takeaway
A traveler must intend a three-day moderate journey beyond his residence; this is the minimum for qasr and other travel concessions in the Hanafi school.

The Minimum Duration of Travel: Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Defining travel and its minimum duration with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi definition of travel as three days at moderate pace, explain the Hanafi proof from the hadith of wiping, and compare the positions of Shafi'i, Maliki, and Abu Yusuf on the minimum travel distance.

Core Idea
Travel is defined by a three-day moderate journey; the Hanafi proof uses the generality of 'al-musafir' in the hadith of wiping.

This lesson explains the Hanafi definition of travel (safar) that triggers legal concessions such as qasr of prayer. It begins with the criteria of leaving one's residence with intention, a moderate pace, and a minimum of three days. The central proof is the hadith on wiping, and we will see how the Hanafi school derives the three-day minimum from it, and how other schools disagree.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi conditions for travel
Identify that travel requires: (1) passing the houses of the place of residence, (2) intention to travel, (3) moderate pace, and (4) minimum of three days. Note that pace is measured by the moderate pace of camels/walking, not fast or slow.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
The proof is the hadith: 'يمسح المقيم يوما وليلة، والمسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليها'. The Hanafi argument: the word 'al-musafir' with alif lam indicates generality (istiqhraq al-jins), so every traveler must be able to avail three days, implying the minimum travel must be three days.
The increase over three is negated by consensus, so three is the minimum.
3
Map the opposing positions
Know the views: Imam al-Shafi'i: 2 days (16 farsakhs) or 1 day/night; Imam Malik: 4 barids (48 miles); Abu Yusuf: 2 days and most of the third. Each has its own proofs from narrations.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the hadith with alif lam is decisive; if the minimum were less, some travelers would not complete three days, causing inconsistency in the Lawgiver's speech. The opposing proofs are weaker or based on other considerations.
The Hanafi view is the mufta bihi.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: a traveler covering less than three days (e.g., 2 days) would complete (itmam) prayer according to Shafi'i/Malik, but shorten (qasr) according to Hanafi. This directly affects daily practice.

Source Text

باب صلاة المسافر أي في بيان أحكامها من جاوز بيوت مصره مريداً سيراً وسطاً ثلاثة أيام. المناسبة بينهما ظاهرة أي كل من التلاوة والسفر عارض، إلا أن التلاوة عارض هو عبادة في نفسها إلا بعارض، والسفر عارض مباح إلا بعارض يعني أن الأصل في التلاوة أن تكون عبادة إلا بعارض كالرياء، والأصل في السفر الإباحة إلا بعارض كالسفر لزيارة الرحم، وفي بعض النسخ "باب المسافر" وفي بعضها "باب صلاة المسافر"، واختار الشارح مسكين النسخة الثانية، فالإضافة من إضافة الفعل إلى فاعله، والأصل في المفاعلة أن تكون بين اثنين، وقد تستعمل في واحد، وهنا من قبيل الأول؛ لأن المسافر لا يخرج من بيته غالباً إلا مع رفيقه، والسفر في اللغة الكشف، سمي به؛ لأنه يكشف عن أخلاق الرجال، وشرعاً: قطع مسافة تتغير به الأحكام من قصر الصلاة، وإباحة الفطر، وامتداد مدة المسح، وسقوط وجوب الجمعة، والعيدين، والأضحية، وحرمة الخروج على المرأة بغير محرم. (فتح، مسكين) جاوز بيوت من الجانب الذي خرج منه وإن كان بحذائه من جانب آخر بناء. (ع) مصره: ليس المراد بالمصر حقيقة بل المراد محل إقامة أعم من البلد والقرية مجازاً، فإن الخارج من القرية للسفر مسافر. (فتح) مريداً سيراً إلخ أي حال كونه مريداً؛ لأنه لو لم يرد ذلك فسافر الأقاليم يوماً بعد يوم لا قصر له، فالقصد وحده غير معتبر، والفعل وحده كذلك، وإنما العبرة للمجموع. (مستخلص) حال من ضمير جاوز وسيراً مفعول قوله: "مريداً"، ثم إن هذا السير متصف بشيئين: الأول: أن يكون وسطا، والثاني: أن يكون ثلاثة أيام، فانتصاب سيراً على المفعولية، وانتصاب وسطا وثلاثة أيام على الوصفية، وقيد بثلاثة أيام وهي أدنى مدة السفر عندنا، لقوله عليه السلام: يمسح المقيم يوما وليلة، والمسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليها، وجه الاستدلال: أن المسافر ذكر محلّى بالألف واللام فاستغرق الجنس؛ لعدم المعهود، واقتضى تمكن كل مسافر ثلاثة أيام، ولا يمكن ذلك إلا أن تكون أقل مدة السفر ثلاثة أيام؛ إذ لو كان أقل من ذلك لخرج بعض المسافرين عن استيفاء هذه الرخصة، ويتطرق الخلف في كلام صاحب الشرع، والزيادة عليها منتفية إجماعاً فكان الاحتياج إلى إثبات أن الثلاثة أقل مدة السفر، وعند الشافعي: مقدر بيومين، وهو ستة عشر فرسخاً، وفي قول بيوم وليلة، وعند مالك بأربعة برد كل بريد اثنا عشر ميلا، وعند أبي يوسف يومين وأكثر الثالث، ولكل واحد دلائل من الآثار ولنا ما روينا. (عيني وغيره) فالسير الوسط سير الإبل ومشي وسطاً احتراز عن سير البريد، فإنه سريع . وعن سير العجلة، فإنه بطيء الأقدام. (مستخلص) ثلاثة أيام من أقصر أيام السنة، ولا يشترط سير اليوم بتمامه، بل إلى الزوال. (ط)
Chapter of the Traveler's Prayer. That is, explaining its rulings. Whoever passes the houses of his town intending a moderate journey of three days. The appropriateness between them is apparent: both recitation and travel are incidental, except that recitation is inherently worship unless an incidental factor arises, while travel is inherently permissible unless an incidental factor arises. That is, the basis of recitation is worship except for an incidental factor like showing off, and the basis of travel is permissibility except for an incidental factor like travel for visiting relatives. In some copies: 'Chapter of the Traveler' and in some: 'Chapter of the Traveler's Prayer', and the commentator Maskin chose the second version. The construct is of the infinitive to its subject, and the original in verbal nouns between two is between two, and it may be used for one, and here it is of the first type because the traveler usually does not leave his house except with a companion. Travel linguistically means uncovering; it is named so because it uncovers the character of men. Legally: covering a distance through which rulings change: shortening prayer, permission to break fast, extension of the period of wiping, dropping the obligation of Friday prayer, the two Eids, and sacrifice, and prohibition of a woman going out without a mahram. (Fath, Maskin) 'Passes the houses' from the side he left from, even if on the opposite side there is a building. (Ayni) 'His town' (misr): the intended meaning is not the town in reality, but rather the place of residence, general for city and village metaphorically; indeed, the one who goes out from a village for travel is a traveler. (Fath) 'Intending a journey etc.' i.e., while intending, because if he did not intend that and traveled the regions day after day, he does not shorten. Thus intention alone is not considered, nor action alone; rather, consideration is for the combination. (Mustakhlas) It is a hal from the subject of 'passes', and 'journey' is the object of 'intending'. Then this journey is described by two attributes: first, being moderate; second, being three days. 'Journey' is in the accusative as object, 'moderate' and 'three days' are accusative as adjectives. It is restricted to three days, which is the minimum travel period according to us, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'The resident wipes for a day and night, and the traveler for three days and their nights.' The aspect of deduction: the word 'the traveler' is mentioned with alif and lam, so it encompasses the entire genus due to absence of a specific referent, and it necessitates that every traveler is entitled to three days. This is not possible unless the minimum travel period is three days; because if it were less, some travelers would be excluded from availing this concession, and discrepancy would arise in the speech of the Lawgiver. The increase over it is negated by consensus, so the need is to establish that three is the minimum travel period. According to al-Shafi'i: it is estimated by two days, which is sixteen farsakhs, and in one opinion by a day and a night. According to Malik: four barids, each barid is twelve miles. According to Abu Yusuf: two days and most of the third. Each one has proofs from narrations, and we have what we narrated. (Ayni and others) The moderate pace is the pace of camels and walking, 'moderate' excludes the pace of the carrier (barid), for it is fast, and excludes the pace of the elderly (ajalah), for it is slow on foot. (Mustakhlas) Three days from the shortest days of the year, and the entire day's journey is not required, but only until noon. (T)
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the minimum duration of travel (safar) that triggers the concession of qasr. It begins by defining the chapter and travel itself. The matn states that a traveler is one who passes the houses of his town intending a moderate journey of three days. The commentary explains that 'town' (misr) here refers to any place of residence, not a specific city. The pace must be moderate, not too fast (like postal carriers) nor too slow (like the elderly). The Hanafi position is that the minimum travel is three days, and this is proved by a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ distinguishes between resident and traveler regarding the duration of wiping. The argument uses the principle that the word 'al-musafir' with alif lam indicates generality, so every traveler must be able to avail the three-day concession, meaning the minimum travel must be three days. Then the dispute is presented: al-Shafi'i says two days (16 farsakhs) or one day and night; Malik says four barids (48 miles); Abu Yusuf says two days and most of the third. Each school has its own proofs, but the Hanafi reliance on the hadith is presented as authoritative.

Key Terms
سير وسط (sayr wasaṭ): Moderate pace, neither fast (like postal carriers) nor slow (like the elderly). It is the pace of camels and walking.
مصر (miṣr): The place of residence (locality), whether a city or village, from which the traveler departs.
مسافة السفر (masāfat al-safar): The distance that changes rulings. Hanafi: three days' moderate walk. Other schools: varying distances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum duration of travel that permits qasr (shortening) of prayer?
A) One day and night
B) Two days
C) Three days at moderate pace
D) Four barids

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines travel for qasr as a three-day moderate journey, derived from the generality of the hadith on wiping, and this is the relied-upon position despite opposing views.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Ruling of Qasr and Its Termination
Ruling of shortening prayer and when it ends

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that qasr is wajib, explain when travel status ends (by entering town or intending 15-day residence), and evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute on residence duration.

Core Idea
Qasr is wajib for the traveler; travel ends by entering one's town or intending residence for 15 days.

This lesson covers the Hanafi rulings on qasr and its termination. The passage establishes the obligation of shortening the four-rak'ah fard, then discusses the conditions under which travel status ends. A key inter-madhhab difference arises on the minimum residence duration that breaks travel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is qasr (shortening) of the four-rak'ah fard prayer. According to Hanafi, it is wajib for the traveler — the fard becomes two rak'ahs.
The phrase 'قصر الفرض الرباعي' (shorten the four-rak'ah fard) indicates the subject.
2
Locate the dalil and analyse wajh al-dalalah
The proof is the hadith of Aisha: 'Prayer was prescribed as two rak'ahs, then travel prayer was confirmed, and residence prayer was increased.' This shows that the traveler's fard is two rak'ahs, making the extra two nafl.
The text states: 'تكون القعدة الأولى من الرباعية فرضا في حق المسافر' (the first sitting in a four-rak'ah prayer is fard for the traveler).
3
Determine the consequence of completing without sitting
If the traveler prays four rak'ahs and sits in the second (reciting tashahhud), the prayer is valid: the first two count as fard, the last two as nafl. If he does not sit in the second, the prayer is invalid.
The text says: 'فلو أتم وقعد في الثانية صح، وإلا لا' (if he completes and sits in the second, valid; otherwise no).
4
Identify the conditions that end travel status
Travel ends when the traveler enters his town (even without intention to stay) or intends residence for half a month (15 days) in a city or village. Intention of residence in a wilderness does not end travel unless three days of travel have already been covered.
The phrase 'حتى يدخل مصره أو ينوي إقامة نصف شهر' (until he enters his town or intends residence of half a month) sets the limit.
5
Evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute on residence duration
Hanafi holds 15 days, based on statements of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. Shafi'i and Maliki hold 4 days, based on a hadith of Uthman. The thamarah is that a traveler who intends 5 days completes according to Shafi'i but shortens according to Hanafi.
The Hanafi response emphasizes the strength of companion statements over the single authentic hadith.

Source Text

في برّ أو بحر أو جبل، قصر الفرض الرباعي، فلو أتم وقعد في الثانية صح، وإلا لا، أي الركعة قدر التشهد حتى يدخل مصره أو ينوي إقامة نصف شهر ببلدة أو قرية، هو خمسة عشر يوماً لا بمفازة أي يتم فيهما. في بر أو بحر إلخ يعني أن السفر في كل مكان معتبر به لا بغيره حتى لو كان لموضع طريقان: أحدهما في الماء، وهو يقطع بثلاثة أيام ولياليها إذا كانت الرياح ساكنة، والثاني في البرد، وهو يقطع بيومين، فإنه إذا ذهب بطريق الماء يقصر، وإن ذهب في البر يتم والمعتبر في البحر ما يليق بحاله، ولو سار في البر والبحر قطع في أقل من ولو سار في الجبل قطع في ثلاثة أيام لمكان الصعود والنزول فيقصر في طريق الجبل، والفتوى على أن ينظر إن تسير السفينة في ثلاثة أيام ولياليها عند استواء الريح حيث لم تكن عاصفة ولا هاذنة فيجعل ذلك هو المقدر في البحر، وينظر في الجبل كم يسير الماشي فيه في ثلاثة أيام ولياليها، فيجعل ذلك هو المقدر. (عيني، مسكين) أو جبل مع الاستراحات المعتادة حتى لو أسرع فوصل في يومين قصر، ولو لموضع طريقان: أحدهما مدة السفر والآخر أقل قصر في الأول لا في الثاني . (ط) قصر إلخ لأنه لا يجوز له الإتمام عندنا يعني ينقص من الفرض الرباعي الذي يصلي في الحضر بقدر ركعتين، ويكون فرضه ركعتين بقول عائشة رضي الله عنها: "فرضت الصلاة ركعتين ركعتين فأقرت صلاة السفر، وزيدت في صلاة الحضر، فتكون القعدة الأولى من الرباعية فرضا في حق المسافر، وقال الشافعي: فرضه الأربع، والقصر رخصة اعتباراً بالصوم ولنا أن الشفع الثاني لا يقضى ولا يأثم على تركه بالاتفاق، وهذا آية النفلية بخلاف الصوم فإنه يقضى وقيد الفرض بالرباعي؛ ليعلم أنه لا قصر في المغرب والفجر والوتر. (فتح، مستخلص، عيني) أتم: المسافر الرباعي و لم يقصر وصلى أربعاً . (ط، ع) صح: أي فرضه، والأخريان تطوع كما لو صلى الفجر أربعاً وأساء بتأخير السلام (ع) وإلا أي وإن لم يقعد في الثانية قدر التشهد. (ط) لا: أي لا بالنفل قبل إكمال الفرض. [رمز الحقائق: ٩٤/١] حتى يدخل إلخ الاشتغال غاية لقوله: "قصر" أي لا يزال يقصر في سفره إلى دخول مصره. (ع، ط) أي بعد استحكام السفر أو يعزم على الرجوع إليه قبل الاستحكام، وسير ثلاثة أيام، فإنه يتم بالدخول، أو بمجرد العزم قبله، وإن لم ينو الإقامة إلا إذا كان لاحقاً بأن اقتدى مسافر مسافر ثم نام فلما فرغ الإمام استيقظ ودخل مصره للوضوء، فإنه يقصر؛ لأنه وراء الإمام حكماً. (فتح عيني) أو ينوي: عطف على قوله يدخل مصره. (ع) ببلدة أو قرية أي بعد ما دخل ولو نوى الإقامة بأحدهما قبل الدخول لا يكون مقيماً، والتقييد بهما يؤذن بأنه لا تصح نية الإقامة في المفاوز لكن لا مطلقاً، بل مقيداً بما إذا سار ثلاثاً، وليس المراد بالمفازة خصوصها، بل في كل موضع غير صالح للإقامة، وأما إذا لم يسر ثلاثاً فيصح، وقال مالك والشافعي مدة الإقامة أربعة أيام؛ لحديث عثمان رضي الله عنه: "من أقام أربعاً صلى أربعاً"، ولنا ما ورد عن ابن عباس وابن عمر رضي الله عنهما أنهما قالا: "إذا قدمت بلدة وأنت مسافر وفي نفسك أن تقيم بها خمسة عشر يوما وليلة فأكمل صلاتك وإن كنت لا تدري متى تظعن"
On land, sea, or mountain, shorten the four-rak'ah fard. If he completes it and sits in the second, it is valid; otherwise no; i.e., if he sits the amount of tashahhud until he enters his town or intends residence of half a month in a city or village — it is fifteen days — not in a wilderness; that is, he completes in these (i.e., if intending in a wilderness, he completes? the phrase is ambiguous).' On land or sea etc.' means that travel is considered in every place, not by other things, so that if a place has two routes: one on water which is traversed in three days and nights if winds are calm, and the other on land which is traversed in two days, then if he goes by water he shortens, and if he goes by land he completes. And the consideration in the sea is what is suitable to its condition. And if he travels in a mountain, he covers in three days due to ascent and descent, so he shortens on the mountain route. The fatwa is to look: if the ship sails in three days and nights when the wind is steady, not stormy nor calm, then that is made the estimate at sea. And on the mountain, one looks at how much a walker covers in three days and nights, and that is made the estimate. (Ayni, Maskin) 'Or mountain' with customary rests, such that if he speeds and arrives in two days, he shortens. If a place has two routes: one of travel duration and the other less, he shortens on the first not the second. (T) 'Shorten' etc. because he is not allowed to complete according to us. That is, he reduces from the four-rak'ah fard that he prays in residence by two rak'ahs, and his fard becomes two rak'ahs based on the saying of Aisha: 'Prayer was prescribed as two rak'ahs, then travel prayer was confirmed, and residence prayer was increased, so the first sitting in a four-rak'ah prayer is fard for the traveler.' Al-Shafi'i said: his fard is four, and shortening is a concession by analogy to fasting. Our proof is that the second pair is not made up (qada) and one does not sin for omitting it by consensus, and this indicates it is supererogatory, unlike fasting because it is made up. He restricted it to the four-rak'ah fard to show that there is no shortening in Maghrib, Fajr, and Witr. (Fath, Mustakhlas, Ayni) 'Completes': the traveler of the four-rak'ah does not shorten and prays four. (T, A) 'Valid': i.e., his fard, and the other two are supererogatory, just as if he prayed Fajr as four and did wrong by delaying the greeting. (A) 'Otherwise': i.e., if he does not sit in the second the amount of tashahhud. (T) 'No': i.e., not valid as supererogatory before completing the fard. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 94/1] 'Until he enters' etc.: the phrase is a limit (ghaya) for his saying 'shorten', i.e., he continues shortening in his travel until he enters his town. (A, T) That is, after the travel is established, or he resolves to return before establishment, and three days of travel; then he completes upon entry, or by mere resolution before it, even if he does not intend residence, unless he is a latecomer (lahiq): if a traveler follows another traveler and then sleeps, then when the imam finishes he wakes up and enters his town for wudu, then he shortens because he is behind the imam in ruling. (Fath, Ayni) 'Or intends': conjuncted to his saying 'enters his town'. (A) 'In a city or village': i.e., after he has entered; and if he intends residence in one of them before entering, he does not become a resident. The restriction to these indicates that intention of residence is not valid in wildernesses, but not absolutely; rather it is restricted to when he has traveled three days. The intended meaning of 'wilderness' is not specifically that, but rather every place unsuitable for residence. But if he has not traveled three days, it is valid (i.e., his intention of residence in a wilderness makes him resident? The text is ambiguous). Malik and al-Shafi'i said the duration of residence is four days due to the hadith of Uthman: 'Whoever stays four days, let him pray four.' We have what is narrated from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar that they said: 'When you arrive at a town as a traveler and you intend to stay fifteen days and nights, then complete your prayer, even if you do not know when you will depart.'
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage covers two main topics: (1) the ruling of qasr (shortening) for the traveler and (2) the termination of travel status. It begins by stating that shortening applies to the four-rak'ah fard prayer, regardless of whether travel is by land, sea, or mountain. The commentator explains that the route taken matters: if both a long and short route exist, the traveler shortens only if the route taken itself qualifies as travel (3 days). The sea is measured by ship's journey with normal winds, and the mountain by the walker's pace with rests. The Hanafi position is that qasr is not merely a concession but an obligation (the four-rak'ah fard becomes two rak'ahs). This is supported by Aisha's hadith that prayer was originally two rak'ahs, and the increase was for residence. The second part discusses when travel ends: by entering one's town (even without intention to stay) or by intending residence of half a month (15 days) in a populated place (city or village). Intention of residence in a wilderness does not break travel status unless the traveler has already covered three days of travel. The passage ends with a dispute: Malik and al-Shafi'i hold that four days of residence break travel, citing Uthman's hadith, while the Hanafi school relies on the statement of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar for 15 days.

Key Terms
قصر (qaṣr): Shortening the four-rak'ah fard prayer to two rak'ahs during travel.
إقامة (iqāmah): Residing in a place, which ends the status of travel and requires completing prayers.
مفازة (mafāzah): Wilderness or uninhabited place where residence is not normally possible.
الشفع الثاني (ash-shafʿ ath-thānī): The second pair of rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer (the last two rak'ahs).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum duration of residence (iqamah) that ends travel status and requires completing prayers?
A) 4 days
B) 15 days
C) 3 days
D) 1 month

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qasr is wajib, and travel status ends by entering one's town or intending 15-day residence; the 4-day view of Shafi'i is a legitimate difference with practical consequences.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Shortening Prayer (Qasr) – Ruling, Conditions, and Proof
Core ruling on qasr with conditions and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qasr, identify the conditions that make it wajib, and explain the proof from the hadith of Aisha and the consensus on the second pair being supererogatory.

Core Idea
Shortening prayer is wajib; completing with sitting is valid but the extra two are nafl.

This lesson presents the foundational Hanafi ruling on the traveler's prayer (qasr). It establishes that shortening the four-rakat obligatory prayers to two is not merely a concession but an obligation, supported by the hadith of Aisha (RA) and the consensus that the second pair is not made up and its omission is not sinful. You will learn the precise conditions under which qasr applies, the ruling when a traveler completes the prayer, and how the Hanafi school defends its position against the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
State that the traveler must shorten the four-rakat obligatory prayers (zuhr, asr, isha) to two rak'ahs. This is wajib according to the Hanafi school, not a mere concession.
Contrast with the Shafi'i position that considers qasr a rukhsah (concession).
2
Determine the Conditions for Shortening
Identify that travel must be of a distance that takes three days and nights by the mode of travel (land, sea, or mountain). Shortening continues until the traveler enters his city or intends residence of 15 days in a town or village.
The measure of travel is based on time, not distance, and is specific to the means of transport.
3
Analyze the Ruling on Completing the Prayer
If the traveler prays four rak'ahs and sits for tashahhud in the second rak'ah, the prayer is valid; the first two are obligatory and the second two are supererogatory. If he does not sit, the prayer is invalid.
Sitting in the second rak'ah is wajib; its deliberate omission invalidates the prayer.
4
Examine the Proof
The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Aisha: 'Prayer was prescribed as two rak'ahs, two rak'ahs; the travel prayer was confirmed, and the residence prayer was increased.' This shows that the original fard for the traveler is two rak'ahs.
The increase for residence is an addition, not the baseline.
5
Refute the Opposing View
Al-Shafi'i holds that qasr is a concession by analogy to fasting. The Hanafi response: the second pair is not made up and omitting it is not sinful by consensus, proving it is supererogatory, unlike fasting.
This consensus is the decisive factor that distinguishes the case from fasting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
١٤٣
باب صلاة المسافر
في برّ أو بحر أو جبل، قصر الفرض الرباعي، فلو أتم وقعد في الثانية صح، وإلا لا، أي الركعة قدر التشهد حتى يدخل مصره أو ينوي إقامة نصف شهر ببلدة أو قرية،
هو خمسة عشر يوماً لا بمفازة أي يتم فيهما
ثلاثة
في بر أو بحر إلخ يعني أن السفر في كل مكان معتبر به لا بغيره حتى لو كان لموضع طريقان: أحدهما في الماء، وهو يقطع بثلاثة أيام ولياليها إذا كانت الرياح ساكنة، والثاني في البرد، وهو يقطع بيومين، فإنه إذا ذهب بطريق الماء يقصر، وإن ذهب في البر يتم والمعتبر في البحر ما يليق بحاله، ولو سار في البر والبحر قطع في أقل من ولو سار في الجبل قطع في ثلاثة أيام لمكان الصعود والنزول فيقصر في طريق الجبل، والفتوى على أن ينظر إن تسير السفينة في ثلاثة أيام ولياليها عند استواء الريح حيث لم تكن عاصفة ولا هاذنة فيجعل ذلك هو المقدر في البحر، وينظر في الجبل كم يسير الماشي فيه في ثلاثة أيام ولياليها، فيجعل ذلك هو المقدر. (عيني، مسكين) أو جبل مع الاستراحات المعتادة حتى لو أسرع فوصل في يومين قصر، ولو لموضع طريقان: أحدهما مدة السفر والآخر أقل قصر في الأول لا في الثاني . (ط) قصر إلخ لأنه لا يجوز له الإتمام عندنا يعني ينقص من الفرض الرباعي الذي يصلي في الحضر بقدر ركعتين، ويكون فرضه ركعتين بقول عائشة الها: "فرضت الصلاة ركعتين ركعتين فأقرت صلاة السفر، وزيدت في صلاة الحضر، فتكون القعدة الأولى من الرباعية فرضا في حق المسافر، وقال الشافعي: فرضه الأربع، والقصر رخصة اعتباراً بالصوم ولنا أن الشفع الثاني لا يقضى ولا يأثم على تركه بالاتفاق، وهذا آية النفلية بخلاف الصوم فإنه يقضى وقيد الفرض بالرباعي؛ ليعلم أنه لا قصر في المغرب والفجر والوتر. (فتح، مستخلص، عيني)
يصح
لاشتغاله
أتم: المسافر الرباعي و لم يقصر وصلى أربعاً . (ط، ع) صح: أي فرضه، والأخريان تطوع كما لو صلى الفجر أربعاً وأساء بتأخير السلام (ع) وإلا أي وإن لم يقعد في الثانية قدر التشهد. (ط) لا: أي لا بالنفل قبل إكمال الفرض. [رمز الحقائق: ٩٤/١] حتى يدخل إلخ الاشتغال غاية لقوله: "قصر" أي لا يزال يقصر في سفره إلى دخول مصره. (ع، ط)] أي بعد استحكام السفر أو يعزم على الرجوع إليه قبل الاستحكام، وسير ثلاثة أيام، فإنه يتم بالدخول، أو بمجرد العزم قبله، وإن لم ينو الإقامة إلا إذا كان لاحقاً بأن اقتدى مسافر مسافر ثم نام فلما فرغ الإمام استيقظ ودخل مصره للوضوء، فإنه يقصر؛ لأنه وراء الإمام حكماً. (فتح عيني) أو ينوي: عطف على قوله يدخل مصره. (ع) ببلدة أو قرية أي بعد ما دخل ولو نوى الإقامة بأحدهما قبل الدخول لا يكون مقيماً، والتقييد بهما يؤذن بأنه لا تصح نية الإقامة في المفاوز لكن لا مطلقاً، بل مقيداً بما إذا سار ثلاثاً، وليس المراد بالمفازة خصوصها، بل في كل موضع غير صالح للإقامة، وأما إذا لم يسر ثلاثاً فيصح، وقال مالك والشافعي مدة الإقامة أربعة أيام؛ لحديث عثمان الله: "من أقام أربعاً صلى أربعاً ، ولنا ما ورد عن ابن عباس اما وابن عمر لما أنهما قالا: "إذا قدمت بلدة وأنت مسافر وفي نفسك أن تقيم بها خمسة عشر يوما وليلة فأكمل صلاتك وإن كنت لا تدري متى تظعن
Book of Prayer. Section: Prayer of the Traveler. On land or sea or mountain, shorten the four-rakat obligatory prayer. If he completes and sits in the second, it is valid; otherwise not, meaning the rak'ah of the tashahhud. Until he enters his city or intends residence of half a month in a town or village, that is fifteen days. Not in a desert, meaning he completes in them? Three. On land, sea, etc.: meaning travel in every place is considered by it, not by other, so if a place has two routes: one on water, which takes three days and nights if winds are calm, and the other on land, which takes two days, then if he goes by water he shortens, if by land he completes. What is considered in the sea is what is appropriate to its state. If he travels on land and sea, he covers in less than? If he travels on a mountain, he covers in three days due to ascent and descent, so he shortens on the mountain route. The fatwa is that one considers if the ship travels in three days and nights when the wind is steady, not stormy nor calm, that is the measure at sea. On the mountain, one considers how fast a walker goes in three days and nights, that is the measure. (Ayni, Miskin) Or a mountain with customary rest stops, so even if he speeds and arrives in two days, he shortens. If a place has two routes: one of travel duration and the other shorter, he shortens in the first not the second. (T) Shortening etc.: because it is not permissible for him to complete according to us; meaning he reduces from the four-rakat obligatory that he prays in residence by two rak'ahs, and his obligatory becomes two rak'ahs, by the saying of Aisha: "Prayer was prescribed two rak'ahs, two rak'ahs; the travel prayer was confirmed, and the residence prayer was increased." Thus the first sitting of the four-rakat is obligatory for the traveler. Al-Shafi'i said: his obligatory is four, and shortening is a concession by analogy to fasting. For us: the second pair is not made up, and one does not sin by leaving it by consensus, indicating it is supererogatory, unlike fasting which is made up. He restricted the obligatory to the four-rakat to show that there is no shortening in maghrib, fajr, and witr. (Fath, Mustakhlas, Ayni) Sahih: for his occupation. Atamma: the traveler's four-rakat, he did not shorten and prayed four. (T, A) Sahih: meaning his obligatory [is valid], and the other two are supererogatory, like if he prayed fajr as four, and he erred by delaying the tasleem. (A) Otherwise: meaning if he did not sit in the second for the amount of tashahhud. (T) La: meaning not as supererogatory before completing the obligatory. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 94/1] Until he enters etc.: the limit for his saying "shorten", i.e., he continues to shorten in his travel until he enters his city. (A, T) i.e., after the travel is established, or he resolves to return before it is established and after traveling three days, then he completes by entering, or by mere resolution before entering, even if he did not intend residence. Except if he is a latecomer: if a traveler follows a traveler [as imam] then sleeps, and when the imam finishes he wakes and enters his city for wudu, then he shortens because he is behind the imam in ruling. (Fath, Ayni) Or intends: coordinate with his saying "enters his city." (A) In a town or village: meaning after he enters, even if he intended residence in one of them before entry, he is not a resident. The restriction to these two indicates that intention of residence is not valid in deserts, but not absolutely, rather restricted to when he has traveled three days. The desert is not specific, but any place unsuitable for residence. If he has not traveled three days, it is valid. Malik and al-Shafi'i said: the duration of residence is four days, by the hadith of Uthman: "Whoever stays four days, prays four." For us is what is narrated from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar that they said: "When you come to a town while you are a traveler and intend to stay there for fifteen days and nights, complete your prayer, even if you do not know when you will depart."
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, followed by its commentary. It opens the chapter on the traveler's prayer, establishing the core ruling: a traveler on land, sea, or mountain shortens the four-rakat obligatory prayer (zuhr, asr, isha) to two rak'ahs. The matn also states that if a traveler prays four rak'ahs (completes) and sits for tashahhud in the second rak'ah, the prayer is valid, but the extra two are supererogatory. If he does not sit in the second, the prayer is invalid. The traveler continues to shorten until he enters his hometown or intends to stay for half a month (fifteen days) in a town or village. The commentary explains that travel is measured by the specific mode: three days and nights by land, but if there are two routes, the one that takes three days makes shortening permissible, while a shorter route does not. For sea travel, the measure is what a ship covers in three days with normal winds; for mountains, three days considering ascent/descent. The commentary then provides the proof that shortening is obligatory, citing the hadith of Aisha (RA) that prayer was originally prescribed as two rak'ahs, and the travel prayer remained two while residence prayer was increased. It refutes al-Shafi'i, who considers shortening a concession, by arguing that if it were a concession, the missed prayer would need to be made up, but there is consensus that the second pair is not made up and omitting it is not sinful, proving it is supererogatory. The passage also clarifies that shortening applies only to four-rakat prayers, not to maghrib, fajr, or witr. The commentary on 'atamma' (completing) explains that if the traveler prays four with sitting in the second, the obligation is fulfilled and the extra two are nafl, but he is blameworthy for delaying the tasleem. If he does not sit, the prayer is invalid. Finally, it discusses the end of travel: entering one's city ends the concession immediately, even if one had not intended to stay. Intending residence for fifteen days in a town or village also ends it, but the intention must be made after entering the place. There is a dispute with Malik and al-Shafi'i, who require four days, but the Hanafi position relies on the athar from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar that fifteen days is the threshold.

Key Terms
قصر (qasr): Reduction of the four-rakat obligatory prayer to two rak'ahs for the traveler.
فرض رباعي (fard ruba'i): Obligatory prayers consisting of four rak'ahs: zuhr, asr, isha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a traveler who prays four rak'ahs for zuhr and does not sit in the second rak'ah?
A) The prayer is valid, and the extra two are supererogatory.
B) The prayer is invalid (batil).
C) The prayer is valid but he should repeat it.
D) The prayer is valid and he is rewarded for completing.

Key Takeaway
Shortening (qasr) is wajib for the traveler; completing with sitting is valid but the extra two are supererogatory; the proof is from the hadith of Aisha and the consensus on the second pair being nafl.

The Exception of Mecca and Mina: Unity of Place for Residence Intent
Details when travel status ends and exceptions for Mecca/Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi exception that a traveler does not become a resident in Mecca or Mina even with intent, and identify the five conditions for valid niat al-iqama with emphasis on unity of place and independence.

Core Idea
Mecca and Mina are not places of residence for the pilgrim; valid intent requires a unified, independent place.

The Hanafi text states that even if a pilgrim intends to stay 15 days in Mecca or Mina, they do not become a resident and continue to shorten. This lesson unpacks why—focusing on the condition of unity of place and the five prerequisites for a valid intention of residence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception
Note the ruling: 'لا بمكة ومنا'—the traveler does not complete prayer in Mecca or Mina even with intent. Understand that these are exceptional places for pilgrimage.
This applies to similar pairs of independent places.
2
Understand unity of place
The text explains that if one intends residence in two places jointly (e.g., Mecca and Mina), it is invalid unless the person stays overnight in one and goes to the other by day. The place of overnight stay becomes the residence.
The phrase 'موضعين مستقلين' indicates both places must be independent, not one subordinate to the other.
3
Derive the five conditions
From the commentary, extract the five conditions for valid niat al-iqama: cessation of travel, duration (15 days), suitability of place, unity of place, and independence of decision. Explain each briefly.
The condition of independence means the person is not a follower (e.g., a wife traveling with husband without independent intent).
4
Apply to similar cases
Generalize: any two places where one is subordinate to the other (e.g., a village near a city where Friday is held) do not break unity. The person completes prayer upon entering the main city.

Source Text

Book of Prayer. Section: Prayer of the Traveler. Not in Mecca and Mina, and he shortens if he intends less than that or does not intend and stays years, or if the army intends half a month, that is the residence. That in the land of war, and if they besiege a city or besiege its inhabitants, then he becomes a resident? The army of Muslims, so shorten it. The athar about measures is like hadith; opinion cannot reach it. And because absolute stay cannot be considered because travel cannot be devoid of it, so it leads to not being a traveler at all, so we measure it by the period of purity; because they are two obligatory periods. (Fath) Not in Mecca: meaning he does not complete if he intends residence. (T) Not in Mecca and Mina and similar from every two independent places, except if he intends to stay by night in one and go out by day to the other, then he completes in the one he stays by night. (T, A) By this he indicates that for the validity of intention of residence, unity of place is required. If he intends the duration of residence in Mecca and Mina jointly, he becomes a resident, except if he intends to mean he stays by night in one and goes out by day to the other place. Then if he enters first the place he resolved to stay in by day, he does not become a resident; if he enters first the place he resolved to stay in by night, he becomes a resident, then by going out to the other place he does not become a traveler, because the place of one's residence is where he spends the night. The restriction to Mecca and Mina is incidental; rather what matters is that both are original. So in every two places one of which is subordinate to the other, like a village near a city where Friday prayer is obligatory, then he completes by entering one of them. From his statement it is understood that the conditions of intention of residence are five: leaving travel, the duration, suitability of the place, unity of place, and independence of opinion. So the intention of the subordinate is not valid. (Miskin, Fath) And he shortens if he intends etc.: meaning if he intends residence less than half a month, he shortens. According to al-Shafi'i and Malik: if he intends residence for four, he becomes a resident. Entrance and exit becomes prayer? Ahmad: if he intends residence for a duration in which he prays more than twenty... otherwise no. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 95/1] And he stays years in a place resolving to leave tomorrow or not resolve anything. (T) i.e., on the absence of intention of residence, he shortens, because Ibn Umar stayed in Azerbaijan for six months and shortened, and a group of companions did likewise. And from Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas that they said: when you enter a town etc. as before. (Mustakhlas) Or intends army etc.: meaning if the army intends residence in dar al-harb, and if they besiege, they shorten absolutely. Abu Yusuf said in al-Imla': if the army overpowers the disbelievers and settles in their gardens, vineyards, and houses, and the Muslims have might and power, and they unanimously decide to stay fifteen days, they complete the prayer. According to Zufar, intention of residence is valid if they have power, but if the people of war have power, their intention is not valid. (Fath) In the land of war: meaning in dar al-harb, they also shorten if they intend residence, because they are between being victorious and settling or being defeated and fleeing, so there is no residence for them. (Mustakhlas) A city: meaning the army besieges a city in dar al-harb, they shorten, unlike one who enters it with aman, for he completes. (T, A) Days other than two? And according to... they complete, the companions. Or they besiege etc.: meaning they shorten if they besiege in dar al-islam outside the city, or they besiege them at sea absolutely, whether the power is theirs or ours. Zufar said it is valid in two cases, i.e., in the case of besieging outside the city on land.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the traveler's prayer, focusing on the conditions that end the ruler of shortening (qasr) and special exceptions. It begins by stating that in Mecca and Mina, even if one intends residence, he does not complete his prayer; he continues to shorten. This is because these places are not considered residence for the pilgrim due to the transient nature of the stay. The commentary clarifies that the intention of residence requires unity of place: if one intends to stay in two separate places like Mecca and Mina, it is not valid unless he spends the night in one and goes to the other by day, in which case his residence is where he sleeps. Five conditions for niat iqama are derived: cessation of travel, sufficient duration (half a month), suitability of the place (town or village), unity of place (single location), and independence of decision (not a subordinate). The text then rules that if a traveler intends less than half a month, he does not become a resident and continues to shorten. If he stays for years without any intention to stay, he remains a traveler and shortens, citing the example of Ibn Umar in Azerbaijan. For an army in dar al-harb, if they intend to stay half a month, they become residents and complete prayer, but if they are besieging a city, they remain travelers and shorten. Abu Yusuf and Zufar have nuanced views based on the power dynamic. The passage also covers besieging in dar al-islam: if the army besieges a city outside a major town (misr), they shorten; if they besiege at sea, they also shorten. The authority of these rulings is from the commentary sources: Fath, Mustakhlas, Ayni, Miskin, etc.

Key Terms
نية الإقامة (niyat al-iqama): Intent to reside in a place for a specific duration ending travel concessions.
اتحاد المكان (ittihad al-makan): Unity of place: the condition that the intended residence is a single location, not multiple independent places.
الاستقلال بالرأي (al-istiqlal bi al-ra'y): Independence of decision: the person is not a subordinate (e.g., wife, child, soldier without own choice).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A traveler intends to stay in two neighboring villages for 15 days, planning to sleep in Village A each night and work in Village B during the day. According to Hanafi school, what is his status?
A) He becomes a resident in Village A because he sleeps there.
B) He becomes a resident in Village B because he works there.
C) He remains a musafir because he has no single residence.
D) He becomes a resident in both villages.

Key Takeaway
Valid intention of residence requires five conditions: cessation of travel, 15 days, suitable place, unity of place, and independence; otherwise, the traveler shortens.

Duration and Intent: Half a Month or Indefinite Stay
Rulings on duration and intent for travel concessions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a traveler shortens prayer if he intends less than 15 days or has no fixed intention, even if he stays for years, and compare with Shafi'i and Hanbali positions.

Core Idea
It is intention, not duration alone, that ends travel; indefinite stay without intent keeps one a musafir.

The passage tackles a common scenario: a traveler who stays for years without intending to settle. The Hanafi school, relying on Ibn Umar's practice, rules that such a person remains a traveler and shortens. This lesson breaks down the critical role of intention and the fixed duration of half a month.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The text mentions: (a) a traveler who intends less than half a month, and (b) a traveler who stays for years without any intention to settle (e.g., resolving to leave tomorrow). For both, the ruling is shortening.
This contrasts with schools that consider a set number of days regardless of intent.
2
Understand the reason
The commentator explains that if mere stay without intent made one a resident, then travel could never be defined because all travel involves some stay. Thus, the rule is linked to the intention to reside permanently (15 days).
The example of Ibn Umar in Azerbaijan for 6 months shortening is cited as evidence.
3
Note the cross-madhhab comparison
Shafi'i and Maliki require 4 days of stay to become resident; Hanbali requires more than 20 prayers. The Hanafi position is more lenient for indefinite stays.
The text mentions these for contrast.

Source Text

ساكنها، فإنه يصير
مقياً،
عسكر المسلمين
فاقصرها"، والأثر في المقدرات كالخبر؛ إذ الرأي لا يهتدي إليه ؛ ولأنه لا يمكن اعتبار مطلق اللبث؛ لأن السفر لا يعري عنه، فيؤدي إلى أن لا يكون مسافراً أصلاً فقدرناها بمدة الطهر ؛ لأنهما مدتان موجبتان. (فتح) لا بمكة: أي لا يتم إذا نوى الإقامة. (ط) لا بمكة ومنا [ ونحوهما من كل موضعين مستقلين إلا إذا نوى أن يقيم بالليل في أحدهما ويخرج في النهار إلى الآخر فيتم في الذي يقيم فيه بالليل. (ط، ع)] أشار به إلى أنه يشترط لصحة نية الإقامة اتحاد المكان لو نوى مدة الإقامة بمكة ومنا على الاشتراك يصير مقيماً، إلا إذا نوى أن يعني يقيم بالليل في أحدهما ويخرج في النهار إلى الموضع الآخر، فإن دخل أولا الموضع الذي عزم على الإقامة فيه بالنهار لم يصر مقيما، وإن دخل أولاً الموضع الذي عزم على الإقامة فيه بالليل صار مقيماً، ثم بالخروج إلى الموضع الآخر لم يصر مسافراً؛ لأن موضع إقامة المرء حيث يبيت فيه، والتقييد بمكة ومنا اتفاقي، بل المعتبر كونهما أصلين، ففي كل موضعين أحدهما تبع للآخر بأن كانت القرية قريبة من المصر بحيث تحب الجمعة على فيتم بدخول أحدهما واستفيد من كلامه أن شرائط نية الإقامة خمسة: ترك السفر والمدة وصلاحية الموضع واتحاد المكان والاستقلال بالرأي، فلا تصح نية التابع. (مسكين، فتح) وقصر إن نوى إلخ يعني إن نوى الإقامة أقل من نصف الشهر قصر، وعند الشافعي ومالك: إن نوى الإقامة أربعة مقيماً، الدخول والخروج يصير صلاة أحمد: إن نوى إقامة مدة يصلي فيها أكثر من عشرين . وإلا فلا. [رمز الحقائق: ٩٥/١] وبقي سنين في موضع بأن عزم أن يخرج غداً أو لم يعزم على شيء. (ط)] أي على عدم نية الإقامة قصر ؛ لأن ابن عمر الله ما أقام بآذربائيجان ستة أشهر، وكان يقصر، وعن جماعة من مثل ذلك، وعن ابن عمر ما وابن عباس علما أنهما قالا إذا دخلت بلدة إلخ كما سبق. (مستخلص) أو نوى عسكر إلخ: أي إن نوى عسكر الإقامة في دار الحرب، وإن حاصروا قصروا مطلقاً، وقال أبو يوسف في الإملاء: إذا كان العسكر استولوا على الكفار ، ونزلوا بساتينهم وكرومهم وبيوتهم، وللمسلمين منعة وشوكة، فأجمعوا على الإقامة خمسة عشر يوماً أتموا الصلاة، وعند زفر تصح نية الإقامة إن كانت الشوكة لهم، وإن كانت لأهل الحرب لا تصح نيتهم. (فتح) بأرض الحرب أي في دار الحرب فإنهم يقصرون أيضاً إذا نووا الإقامة؛ أن لأنهم بين يهزموا فيقروا وبين أن ينهزموا فيفروا فلم يكن في حقهم دار إقامة. (مستخلص) مصراً: أي حاصر أهل العسكر مصراً في دار الحرب يقصرون بخلاف من دخلها بأمان فإنه يتم. (ط،ع)
أيام غير يومي
وعند
يتم،
الصحابة
أو حاصروا إلخ: أي قصروا إن حاصروا في دار الإسلام في غير المصر أو حاصروهم في البحر مطلقاً، سواء كانت الشوكة لهم أو لنا، وقال زفر يصح في فصلين أي في فصل ما لو كانت المحاصرة في غير المصر من البر،
Book of Prayer. Section: Prayer of the Traveler. Not in Mecca and Mina, and he shortens if he intends less than that or does not intend and stays years, or if the army intends half a month, that is the residence. That in the land of war, and if they besiege a city or besiege its inhabitants, then he becomes a resident? The army of Muslims, so shorten it. The athar about measures is like hadith; opinion cannot reach it. And because absolute stay cannot be considered because travel cannot be devoid of it, so it leads to not being a traveler at all, so we measure it by the period of purity; because they are two obligatory periods. (Fath) Not in Mecca: meaning he does not complete if he intends residence. (T) Not in Mecca and Mina and similar from every two independent places, except if he intends to stay by night in one and go out by day to the other, then he completes in the one he stays by night. (T, A) By this he indicates that for the validity of intention of residence, unity of place is required. If he intends the duration of residence in Mecca and Mina jointly, he becomes a resident, except if he intends to mean he stays by night in one and goes out by day to the other place. Then if he enters first the place he resolved to stay in by day, he does not become a resident; if he enters first the place he resolved to stay in by night, he becomes a resident, then by going out to the other place he does not become a traveler, because the place of one's residence is where he spends the night. The restriction to Mecca and Mina is incidental; rather what matters is that both are original. So in every two places one of which is subordinate to the other, like a village near a city where Friday prayer is obligatory, then he completes by entering one of them. From his statement it is understood that the conditions of intention of residence are five: leaving travel, the duration, suitability of the place, unity of place, and independence of opinion. So the intention of the subordinate is not valid. (Miskin, Fath) And he shortens if he intends etc.: meaning if he intends residence less than half a month, he shortens. According to al-Shafi'i and Malik: if he intends residence for four, he becomes a resident. Entrance and exit becomes prayer? Ahmad: if he intends residence for a duration in which he prays more than twenty... otherwise no. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 95/1] And he stays years in a place resolving to leave tomorrow or not resolve anything. (T) i.e., on the absence of intention of residence, he shortens, because Ibn Umar stayed in Azerbaijan for six months and shortened, and a group of companions did likewise. And from Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas that they said: when you enter a town etc. as before. (Mustakhlas) Or intends army etc.: meaning if the army intends residence in dar al-harb, and if they besiege, they shorten absolutely. Abu Yusuf said in al-Imla': if the army overpowers the disbelievers and settles in their gardens, vineyards, and houses, and the Muslims have might and power, and they unanimously decide to stay fifteen days, they complete the prayer. According to Zufar, intention of residence is valid if they have power, but if the people of war have power, their intention is not valid. (Fath) In the land of war: meaning in dar al-harb, they also shorten if they intend residence, because they are between being victorious and settling or being defeated and fleeing, so there is no residence for them. (Mustakhlas) A city: meaning the army besieges a city in dar al-harb, they shorten, unlike one who enters it with aman, for he completes. (T, A) Days other than two? And according to... they complete, the companions. Or they besiege etc.: meaning they shorten if they besiege in dar al-islam outside the city, or they besiege them at sea absolutely, whether the power is theirs or ours. Zufar said it is valid in two cases, i.e., in the case of besieging outside the city on land.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the traveler's prayer, focusing on the conditions that end the ruler of shortening (qasr) and special exceptions. It begins by stating that in Mecca and Mina, even if one intends residence, he does not complete his prayer; he continues to shorten. This is because these places are not considered residence for the pilgrim due to the transient nature of the stay. The commentary clarifies that the intention of residence requires unity of place: if one intends to stay in two separate places like Mecca and Mina, it is not valid unless he spends the night in one and goes to the other by day, in which case his residence is where he sleeps. Five conditions for niat iqama are derived: cessation of travel, sufficient duration (half a month), suitability of the place (town or village), unity of place (single location), and independence of decision (not a subordinate). The text then rules that if a traveler intends less than half a month, he does not become a resident and continues to shorten. If he stays for years without any intention to stay, he remains a traveler and shortens, citing the example of Ibn Umar in Azerbaijan. For an army in dar al-harb, if they intend to stay half a month, they become residents and complete prayer, but if they are besieging a city, they remain travelers and shorten. Abu Yusuf and Zufar have nuanced views based on the power dynamic. The passage also covers besieging in dar al-islam: if the army besieges a city outside a major town (misr), they shorten; if they besiege at sea, they also shorten. The authority of these rulings is from the commentary sources: Fath, Mustakhlas, Ayni, Miskin, etc.

Key Terms
نية الإقامة (niyat al-iqama): Intent to reside in a place for a specific duration ending travel concessions.
مدة (mudda): Duration; the period one intends to stay. Half a month (15 days) is the minimum for residence intent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A traveler stays in a city for 3 months without any fixed intention to leave or stay. He always plans to leave 'next week'. According to Hanafi fiqh, how should he pray?
A) He should complete because 3 months > 15 days.
B) He should shorten because he lacks the specific intent to settle.
C) He should complete from day 16 onward.
D) He should shorten for the first 15 days, then complete.

Key Takeaway
The traveler's prayer remains shortened unless he forms a clear intention to stay for half a month; indefinite stay without intent does not end travel.

The Army in Dar al-Harb: When Does Intent of Residence Take Effect?
Rulings on army's travel concessions in dar al-harb and besieging

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that a Muslim army in enemy territory remains musafir when besieging or when power is uncertain, and identify the differing views of Abu Yusuf and Zufar regarding the condition of power.

Core Idea
An army in dar al-harb is typically in a state of uncertainty; only when they have might, stability, and a 15-day intent do they become residents.

This lesson tackles the special rules for military personnel. When a Muslim army is on campaign in dar al-harb, the usual rules of travel are modified because of the uncertainty of war. The passage outlines when the army can become resident and when it must shorten, with nuanced views from Abu Yusuf and Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule for army in dar al-harb
The text states that if the army intends to stay half a month in dar al-harb, they still shorten because they are between victory and flight, so there is no stable residence.
This is the baseline: even with intent, they remain musafir.
2
Note the exception: overmighty and stable
Abu Yusuf's view: if the army has conquered and has power, reside in their gardens, etc., and they unanimously decide to stay 15 days, they become residents and complete.
Zufar conditions this on the power dynamic: if the Muslims have the upper hand, the intent is valid; if the enemy has power, it is not.
3
Understand the besieging scenario
If the army is besieging a city in dar al-harb, they shorten absolutely, even if they intend 15 days. This is because they are in a state of war and not in a secure residence.
This contrasts with an individual entering dar al-harb with aman (safe conduct), who must complete.
4
Extend to dar al-islam besieging
If the army besieges in dar al-islam outside a major town (misr) or at sea, they shorten regardless of power. Zufar adds a nuance for besieging on land outside the misr.

Source Text

A Muslim army that has conquered a city in dar al-harb and has full control unanimously intends to stay 15 days. According to the majority view in the text, should they complete or shorten?

C) Complete, because they conquered.
D) Shorten, because they are in a state of war regardless.
