Unity of Place for Valid Intention of Residence
Ruling statement with commentary expanding on conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for a valid niyyat al-iqama and apply the unity of place condition to distinguish when a traveler becomes a muqim.

Core Idea
Unity of place is essential: intending to stay in two separate places does not make you a resident.

In the Hanafi school, a traveler who intends to stay in a location for 15 days or more becomes a resident (muqim) and must perform prayers fully. However, the intention must be for a single place. This lesson dissects the condition of unity of place and the five prerequisites for a valid intention of residence, based on a passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
From the matn line 'Not in Mecca and Mina', the ruling is that intending to stay in two separate places like Mecca and Mina does not make one a muqim. The commentary clarifies that unity of place is a condition.
"Not in Mecca and Mina" refers to the traveler not completing prayers in either place if he intends to stay in both.
2
Understand the exception
The exception: if the traveler intends to stay overnight in one place and go to the other during the day, he becomes muqim in the place where he spends the night. This is because a person's residence is where he sleeps.
The principle is that 'the place of residence is where one spends the night' (موضع الإقامة حيث يبيت).
3
Extract the five conditions
From the commentary, we derive that a valid intention of residence requires: 1) leaving travel, 2) sufficient duration (15 days), 3) suitable place for residence, 4) unity of place, and 5) independence of opinion (the traveler decides for himself, not as a dependent).
These conditions are specific to the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the condition of unity of place
Unity of place means the intention must be for a single location. If the traveler intends to stay in two independent places, even if nearby like Mecca and Mina, the intention is invalid unless one is subordinate to the other or he sleeps in one.
The exception for Mecca and Mina is contractual; the actual criterion is independence of the two places.
5
Consider the independence condition
The intention of a dependent (e.g., a wife following her husband) is not valid. The traveler must have independent judgment and intention.
This ensures that the traveler truly intends to settle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا بمكة ومنا [ ونحوهما من كل موضعين مستقلين إلا إذا نوى أن يقيم بالليل في أحدهما ويخرج في النهار إلى الآخر فيتم في الذي يقيم فيه بالليل. (ط، ع)] أشار به إلى أنه يشترط لصحة نية الإقامة اتحاد المكان لو نوى مدة الإقامة بمكة ومنا على الاشتراك يصير مقيماً، إلا إذا نوى أن يعني يقيم بالليل في أحدهما ويخرج في النهار إلى الموضع الآخر، فإن دخل أولا الموضع الذي عزم على الإقامة فيه بالنهار لم يصر مقيما، وإن دخل أولاً الموضع الذي عزم على الإقامة فيه بالليل صار مقيماً، ثم بالخروج إلى الموضع الآخر لم يصر مسافراً؛ لأن موضع إقامة المرء حيث يبيت فيه، والتقييد بمكة ومنا اتفاقي، بل المعتبر كونهما أصلين، ففي كل موضعين أحدهما تبع للآخر بأن كانت القرية قريبة من المصر بحيث تحب الجمعة على فيتم بدخول أحدهما واستفيد من كلامه أن شرائط نية الإقامة خمسة: ترك السفر والمدة وصلاحية الموضع واتحاد المكان والاستقلال بالرأي، فلا تصح نية التابع. (مسكين، فتح)
Not in Mecca and Mina, and shorten if he intended less than it or did not intend and remained years, or if an army intended half a month... Commentary: 'Not in Mecca and Mina' means he does not complete if he intends residence. ... This indicates that it is necessary for the validity of the intention of residence the unity of place... From his speech we derive that the conditions of intention of residence are five: leaving travel, the period, suitability of place, unity of place, and independence of opinion.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage discusses the condition for a traveler to become a resident (muqim) by intending to stay for fifteen days or more. The matn states that if someone intends to stay in two separate places like Mecca and Mina, he does not become muqim. The commentary clarifies that unity of place is essential; however, if he intends to stay in one place at night and go to the other during the day, he becomes muqim in the place where he stays at night. The principle is that a person's residence is where he spends the night. The commentary also lists five conditions for a valid intention of residence: ceasing travel, the duration (15 days), the place being suitable for residence, unity of place, and independence of decision. The exception for Mecca and Mina is contractual; the actual criterion is that the two places are considered as two separate locations, but if one is subordinate to the other (like a village near a city where Friday prayer is held), then entering one suffices. The intention of a dependent (e.g., a follower) is not valid. This ruling is based on the authority of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqama): The traveler's resolve to stay in a place for a period that makes him a resident (muqim).
اتحاد المكان (ittihad al-makan): Unity of place; the intention must be for a single location.
الاستقلال بالرأي (al-istiqlal bi al-ra'y): Independence of opinion; the person must make the intention independently, not as a dependent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Intending to stay for 10 days.

Key Takeaway
Unity of place is a distinct Hanafi condition for becoming a muqim; without it, the traveler remains a musafir and must shorten prayers.

Duration of Intention for Muqim: Hanafi vs Other Schools
Defining the duration of intention for residency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the minimum duration of intention for becoming a muqim and compare it to the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali views.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school sets the residency threshold at 15 days; Shafi'i and Maliki at 4; Hanbali at 20.

The passage opens with the fundamental rule: a traveler who intends to stay less than half a month (15 days) shortens prayer. This simple statement immediately draws a sharp contrast with other schools, setting up a classic inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi proof relies on the practice of Ibn Umar and the analogy with the period of purity (tuhur).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Baseline Rule
Find the initial statement in the passage: if a traveler intends residence (niyyat al-iqama) for less than half a month (15 days), he shortens prayer. If he intends 15 or more, he completes.
This is the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the Opposing Positions
The text lists Shafi'i/Maliki (4 days) and Hanbali (20+ days). Identify the exact wording: 'عند الشافعي ومالك: إن نوى الإقامة أربعة' and 'أحمد: إن نوى إقامة مدة يصلي فيها أكثر من عشرين'.
The passage does not provide their proofs, only the numbers.
3
Examine the Hanafi Proof
The passage cites the practice of Ibn Umar (ra) who stayed in Azerbaijan for six months shortening prayer. This shows that mere length of stay without intention of 15 days does not make one a resident. Additionally, the analogy to tuhur (15 days of purity) is a Hanafi usul argument.
الطهر (purity) period is 15 days, so any obligation (like full prayer) requires at least that duration.
4
Analyze the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Consider a traveler intending 10 days: Hanafi says he still shortens; Shafi'i says he completes. This difference affects daily prayer obligation for the traveler.
The thamarah is clear: whether one prays 2 or 4 rak'at for each obligatory prayer.

(مستخلص) مصراً: أي حاصر أهل العسكر مصراً في دار الحرب يقصرون بخلاف من دخلها بأمان فإنه يتم. And shorten if he intended less than it or did not intend and remained years, or if an army intended half a month... Commentary: 'And shorten if he intended etc.' means if he intends residence less than half a month, he shortens; according to al-Shafi'i and Malik: if he intends residence for four days, he completes... And remained years in a place means he intends to leave tomorrow or did not intend anything. That is, with no intention of residence, he shortens because Ibn Umar stayed in Azerbaijan for six months and shortened... Or if an army intends residence in the land of war, and if they besiege, they shorten absolutely... And in the land of war they shorten even if they intend residence because they are between victory and flight... And if they besiege a city... And the people of tents, etc.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage covers several scenarios for shortening prayer. First, if a traveler intends to stay for less than 15 days, he shortens. This is disputed by Shafi'i and Malik who require 4 days, and Ahmad who requires 20+ days. Second, if he has no intention to stay, he shortens even if he stays years, proven by Ibn Umar's practice. Third, for a military camp in dar al-harb, if the army intends 15 days, they still shorten because they lack security; Abu Yusuf and Zufar have different conditions. Fourth, when besieging a city in dar al-harb, they shorten; but if in dar al-Islam, they shorten only if not in the city itself. There is also a discussion about people of rebellion (ahl al-baghy) and people of tents (ahl al-akhbiya) like Bedouins who can intend residency in the desert. The relied-upon view is that their intention is valid, making them residents.

Key Terms
قصر (qasr): Shortening the prayer from 4 to 2 rak'at for a traveler.
إقامة (iqama): Residency; legally, the state of intending to stay 15 days or more in a place.
مسافر (musafir): Traveler; one who travels the required distance and does not intend residency of 15 days.
مقيم (muqim): Resident; one who intends to stay 15 days or more in a place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 4 days
B) 10 days
C) 15 days
D) 20 days

Key Takeaway
A traveler remains a musafir and shortens prayer unless he intends to stay 15 days or more; length of stay alone is irrelevant.

Special Cases: Army, Rebels, and Nomads in Qasr
Expanding qasr to military and nomadic contexts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on qasr for military camps in dar al-harb, rebelling forces (ahl al-baghy), and tent-dwellers (ahl al-akhbiya).

Core Idea
In dar al-harb, even an army intending 15 days shortens due to insecurity; rebels in dar al-Islam are treated like travelers; nomads can become residents by intention in the desert.

The passage extends the qasr rules to three special categories: a military campaign in enemy territory, rebels against the legitimate caliph, and Bedouins living in tents. The underlying principle is the security of residence: where true residency is lacking due to war or mobility, the traveler's concession remains.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the Army in Dar al-Harb
The text says: if an army intends residency in dar al-harb, they shorten even if they intend 15 days. Why? Because they are 'between victory and flight'—they lack the security to be true residents. Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf and Zufar add conditions regarding who has the upper hand.
This is a unique Hanafi ruling based on istihsan.
2
Apply the Rule for Siege
When besieging a city (misdann) in dar al-harb, the army shortens. But if they besiege a city in dar al-Islam, they shorten only if they are outside the city (ghayr al-misr). If inside the city, they complete. Also, if on the sea, they shorten absolutely.
Note the exception: a person entering dar al-harb with aman (safe conduct) completes his prayer.
3
Examine the Ruling for Ahl al-Baghy
Ahl al-baghy (rebels) who are Muslims revolting against the Imam are treated as travelers. Even if they stay in a location for some time, they shorten just like a musafir.
This is based on their lack of secure residency.
4
Contrast with Ahl al-Akhbiya
Tent-dwellers (ahl al-akhbiya) like Bedouins can become residents if they intend to stay in a desert place, despite moving their tents. The relied-upon view (al-asahh) is that their intention of residency is valid, making them muqimin.
This is because they can settle in a fixed area for grazing.

Traveler Praying Behind Resident Imam
Ruling with Naqli proof on traveler completing prayer behind resident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a traveler prays behind a resident imam, explain the naqli proof, and contrast with the Maliki position.

Core Idea
Following a resident imam changes the traveler's obligation from two to four rak'at.

The passage discusses the scenario where a traveler joins a resident imam. It establishes that the traveler must complete the prayer, and provides the proof from the Prophet's practice. It also addresses the Maliki disagreement, which holds that if the traveler catches only the last two rak'at, he should not complete four.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a traveler (musafir) praying behind a resident (muqim) imam. The Hanafi ruling is that the traveler must complete the prayer to four rak'at (fard).
The text says 'أتم: أي المسافر صلاته مع الإمام مطلقاً'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is from the sunnah: The Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) said 'أتموا صلاتكم فإنا قوم سفر' when he prayed in Mecca as a traveler.
This is ahad hadith.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'أتموا' is an imperative indicating obligation. The Prophet explicitly commanded the followers to complete, showing that following a resident imam changes the traveler's obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Malik holds that if the traveler catches only the last two rak'at (al-shaf' al-akhir), he should not exceed his traveler's two rak'at.
Malik's view.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi. The Prophet's explicit command overrides the general rule of qasr.
The text mentions that after nullifying, he prays two rak'at because the obligation of four was due to following and is now gone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأتم: أي المسافر صلاته مع الإمام مطلقاً سواء أدركه في الشفع الأول أو الثاني؛ لأنه تغير فرضه إلى أربع لصحة الاقتداء، وإن أفسد الفرض يصلي ركعتين؛ لأن لزوم الأربع للمتابعة وقد زالت بخلاف ما لو اقتدى به بنية النفل ثم أفسد، حيث يلزمه الأربع بالشروع رمز الحقائق: ٩٥/١] وعند مالك: إذا أدركه في الشفع الأخير لا يجاوز شفعه. (عيني، مسكين وبعده لا [ولو اقتدي به بعد خروج الوقت. (ط)] لأن فرضه لا يتغير بعد الوقت لانقضاء السبب، كما لا يتغير بنية ،الإقامة، فيكون اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل في حق القعدة الأولى؛ إذ هي فريضة في حق المسافر وفي حق القراءة؛ لأن قراءته في الأخريين نفل رمز الحقائق: ٩٦/١] (فتح) وبعكسه: هو ما لو اقتدي مقيم بمسافر. (ط) صح فيهما: إذا اتفق الفرضان، لأنه يكون اقتداء متنفل مفترض في حق القعدة، فإن سلم المسافر يتم المقتدي ولا يقرأ فيما بقي؛ لأنه كاللاحق، وقيل: يقرأ كالمسبوق. [رمز الحقائق: ٩٦/١] ويستجب للإمام أن يقول: "أتموا صلاتكم فإنا قوم سفر"؛ لأنه عليها قال هذا حين صلى بمكة وهو مسافر. (فتح) فيهما: أي في الوقت وبعده وإذا سلم المسافر يتم المقيم بلا قراءة في الأصح ويستحب للإمام أن يقول لهم: أتموا صلاتكم فإنا قوم سفر. (ط) الوطن الأصلي هو مولد الإنسان أو البلدة التي تأهل فيها رمز الحقائق ٩٦/١٢] والأوطان ثلاثة: أصلي ووطن إقامة ووطن السكنى وهو ما يكون بنية الإقامة أقل من خمسة عشر يوماً، فالأول ينتقض بمثله؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والمهاجرين من أصحابه كانوا من أهل مكة ثم لما هاجروا واستقروا بالمدينة انتقض وطنهم بمكة حتى كانوا إذا أتوا مكة يصلون صلاة المسافرين ولا يبطل بالآخرين ولا بالسفر، والثاني يبطل بالأول وبالثاني وبالسفر، والثالث يبطل بالكل وبالسفر. ولم يعتبر المحققون وطن السكنى وهو الصحيح. [رمز الحقائق: ٩٦/١] (فتح)
And completes: meaning the traveler completes his prayer with the imam absolutely, whether he caught him in the first two rak'at or the last two; because his obligation changed to four due to correct following... And after it, no... And the opposite: a resident following a traveler is valid in both [time and after?]... And it is recommended for the imam to say: 'Complete your prayer, for we are travelers'... And the original homeland is the birthplace or the town where one settles... And homelands are three: original, residence, and dwelling... The first is abrogated by another like it...
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage first discusses the ruling when a traveler prays behind a resident imam. The traveler must complete the prayer (i.e., pray four rak'at) regardless of which part of the prayer he joins, because his obligation changes to four due to following. This is in contrast to Malik who says if he catches only the last two, he should not exceed his traveler's two. The Hanafi view is that following makes the traveler obligated to four. If the traveler nullifies his prayer, he prays two rak'at because the obligation of four was due to following and is now gone. If he enters with intention of nafl and then nullifies, he must pray four because he started. If he follows after the time, his obligation does not change. The second part discusses the reverse: a resident following a traveler. It is valid if both obligations are the same (i.e., both praying fard). The follower completes after the traveler salam, and it is recommended for the imam to tell them to complete. The third part defines the three types of homeland: original (birthplace or place of settlement), residence (intention of 15+ days), and dwelling (less than 15 days). The original homeland is abrogated by another original homeland (e.g., Makkan immigrants lost their Makkan homeland when they settled in Madinah). The residence homeland is abrogated by the original, another residence, or travel. The dwelling homeland is abrogated by all. The correct view is that dwelling homeland is not considered significant.

Key Terms
الشفع الأول (al-shaf' al-awwal): The first two rak'at of a four-rak'ah prayer.
الشفع الأخير (al-shaf' al-akhir): The last two rak'at of a four-rak'ah prayer.
اقتداء (iqtidā'): To follow an imam in congregational prayer.
مقتدي (muqtadī): The follower in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling when a traveler prays behind a resident imam?
A) He prays two rak'at.
B) He must complete four rak'at.
C) He may choose.
D) He repeats the prayer later.

Key Takeaway
A traveler praying behind a resident imam must perform the full four-rak'ah prayer, regardless of when he joins, due to the Prophet's command.

Resident Praying Behind a Traveler Imam
Ruling on resident following traveler imam with conditions and post-salam actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when a resident prays behind a traveler imam and describe the follower's actions after the imam's salam.

Core Idea
A resident following a traveler is valid; the resident completes the prayer without recitation in the remaining rak'at.

The text addresses the reverse scenario: a resident (muqim) praying behind a traveler (musafir) imam. It rules that the prayer is valid provided both are performing the same fard prayer. After the traveler imam says salam after two rak'at, the resident stands and completes the remaining rak'at without recitation. The imam is recommended to instruct the followers to complete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and condition
The scenario is a resident following a traveler imam. The condition for validity is that both are praying the same fard prayer (e.g., both Zuhr).
The text says 'إذا اتفق الفرضان' (if the two obligations agree).
2
Determine the ruling on validity
The prayer is valid (sahih). The resident becomes a follower, and the traveler leads as imam.
The text says 'صح فيهما' (it is valid in both cases).
3
Explain what happens after the imam's salam
When the traveler imam says salam after two rak'at, the resident completes the remaining rak'at alone. He does not recite Quran in those remaining rak'at.
There is a difference of opinion: some say he recites (like a masbuq), but the preferred view (al-asahh) is no recitation.
4
State the recommended practice for the imam
It is mustahabb for the traveler imam to say to the followers: 'Complete your prayer, for we are travelers.' This is from the Prophet's practice.
The text says 'ويستحب للإمام أن يقول: أتموا صلاتكم فإنا قوم سفر'.

Key Terms
مقيم (muqim): A resident; one who is not traveling.
مسافر (musafir): A traveler; one who intends to travel a distance of three days (approx. 48 miles) and does not intend to stay 15+ days.
لاحق (lahiq): A follower who joins the imam late but still within the same prayer, and then completes after the imam.
مسبوق (masbuq): One who misses part of the prayer and joins later, then completes after imam salam.

B) He prays two rak'at without recitation.
C) He does not need to complete; his prayer is done.
D) He repeats the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
A resident following a traveler imam for the same fard prayer is valid; the resident completes the remaining rak'at without recitation in the strongest opinion.

The Three Homelands (Watan) in Hanafi Fiqh
Definition and classification of watan with abrogation rules.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the three types of watan (homeland) in Hanafi fiqh and identify which watan is abrogated by which.

Core Idea
The original homeland is only abrogated by another original; the residence homeland is abrogated by the original, another residence, or travel.

The passage defines three types of watan: original (asli), residence (iqama), and dwelling (sukna). It explains how each is abrogated (yanqud) by others, which determines whether a person is considered a traveler or resident. The early scholars did not consider dwelling watan significant.

Guided Path
1
Define the original homeland (al-watan al-asli)
It is the birthplace or the place where one settles permanently. It is abrogated only by another original homeland.
Example: The Prophet and Muhajirun lost their Makkan nationality when they settled in Madinah.
2
Define the residence homeland (watan al-iqama)
It is a place where one intends to stay for 15 days or more. It is abrogated by the original homeland, another residence homeland, or travel.
3
Define the dwelling homeland (watan al-sukna)
It is a place where one intends to stay for less than 15 days. It is abrogated by all the above and by travel. Later authorities disregard it.
The text says 'لم يعتبر المحققون وطن السكنى'.
4
Apply the abrogation rules
Given a person's original homeland, if he moves to a new place with intention of permanent settlement, his original changes. If he intends 15+ days, he is not a traveler there. If he intends less, his traveler status remains.
The ruling on qasr prayer depends on watan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Rebels' Prayer and Travel Concessions
Explains ruling on rebels' prayer and distinction from tent dwellers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer for rebels and tent-dwellers, and apply the distinction between fixed and non-fixed residence.

Core Idea
Rebels' prayer is valid and complete in fixed dwellings; tent-dwellers can become residents by intention.

This lesson clarifies the prayer obligation for two unique groups: rebels (ahl al-baghy) who have revolted against the legitimate imam, and tent-dwellers (ahl al-akhbiya) such as nomadic Arabs and Turkmans. The key is whether they are considered residents (muqim) or travellers (musafir), which determines whether they must complete or may shorten their prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
Recognize ahl al-baghy (rebels) and ahl al-akhbiya (tent-dwellers) as distinct categories in Hanafi fiqh.
Both groups are Muslim; their rebellion or lifestyle does not invalidate their Islam.
2
Determine the ruling for rebels
Rebels in a fixed dwelling (e.g., a city) are residents and must complete their prayer. If they are not in a fixed dwelling (e.g., a mobile camp), they are travellers and may shorten.
The text says 'fi darina' (in our territory) meaning a fixed settlement.
3
Determine the ruling for tent-dwellers
Tent-dwellers can become residents by intending to reside in a place, even in the desert. Once they intend residence, they pray complete prayers.
This is the preferred (al-ashah) view according to the text.
4
Note the exception for seasonal movement
If tent-dwellers move from a summer settlement to a winter settlement with a travel distance (masafat al-safar), their residence intention ends and they become travellers who may shorten.
Moving between pastures for grazing does not break residence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أهل البغي في دارنا في غيره، بخلاف أهل الأخبية. أهل البغي وهم المسلمون الذين خرجوا عن طاعة الإمام [ رمز الحقائق ٩٥/١] غيره: أي غير المصر المتردد بين القرار والفرار. (ع) بخلاف أهل الأخبية [كعرب وتركمان نووا الإقامة في المفازة فإنهم يتمون. (ع، ط)] هي جمع خباء وهو بيت من صوف أي ذلك الحكم المتقدم ملتبس بمخالفة حكم أهل الأخبية حيث تصح منهم نية الإقامة، وإن كانوا في المفازة في الأصح وعليه الفتوى والأصح أنهم مقيمون؛ لأن الإقامة أصل فلا تبطل بالانتقال من مرعى إلى مرعى إلا إذا ارتحلوا عن موضع الصيف قاصدين لمكان الشتاء وبينهما مسيرة سفر حيث يقصرون إن نووا سفراً. (فتح)
The people of rebellion in our territory, not in other than it, contrary to the people of tents. The people of rebellion are the Muslims who have left obedience to the imam. 'Other than it': meaning other than the metropolis that wavers between stability and flight. Contrary to the people of tents [like Arabs and Turkmans if they intend residence in the desert, then they complete (the prayer)]: tents (akhbiya) is plural of khiba', which is a house of wool, meaning that previous ruling is mixed with a difference from the ruling of the people of tents, where their intention of residence is valid, even if they are in the desert in the most sound view and upon it is the fatwa, and the most sound is that they are residents because residence is a principle so it is not invalidated by moving from pasture to pasture except if they move from a summer place intending a winter place and between them is a travel distance, then they shorten if they intend travel.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining the prayer obligations of rebels (ahl al-baghy) and the distinction between rebels in fixed dwellings versus tent-dwelling nomads. The author explains that rebels who are in a fixed dwelling (a city or similar) are treated as residents and must complete their prayers, even if they are in a state of rebellion, unless they are in a place that is not a fixed settlement. The commentary clarifies that 'other than it' refers to a place that is not a proper city. In contrast, tent-dwellers (ahl al-akhbiya) like Bedouin Arabs and Turkmans, if they intend to reside in the desert for a period, their intention of residence is valid, and they become residents who must pray complete prayers. The preferred opinion is that they are considered residents because residence is the original state, and moving from one pasture to another does not break their residence unless they move from a summer settlement to a winter settlement with a travel distance between them, in which case they may shorten if they intend travel.

Key Terms
أهل البغي (ahl al-baghy): Muslims who revolt against the legitimate imam.
أهل الأخبية (ahl al-akhbiyah): People living in tents (khiba'), i.e., nomadic or semi-nomadic tribes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on ahl al-baghy (rebels) regarding prayer when they are in a fixed dwelling?
A) They shorten their prayer because of their rebellion.
B) They complete their prayer like residents.
C) Their prayer is invalid until they repent.
D) They pray two rak'ahs always.

Key Takeaway
Rebels in fixed dwellings and tent-dwellers who intend residence both complete their prayer; the key is the concept of residence based on intention and stability.
